when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師 , 她確實做了一些 , 但真正的情況是說 , 未來將會是遠遠多於這個 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	現在 , 一百年後 , 這傢伙來了 , alanturing , 1936年 , 又發明了一台電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是完全機械化的
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	圖靈的機器是完全理論性的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩位都是從數學的角度來的 , 但圖靈告訴了我們一件非常重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 說: 「 製造電腦並不重要 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不管是電腦的機械 , 像是babbage的原理或是電子 , 像是今天的電腦 , 或是未來的電腦 , 或是細胞 , 又或者 , 再一次機械化 , 一旦我們進入奈米科技
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器讓它變小 , 所有這些東西都是電腦
there is in a sense a computing essence .	一種計算的精髓 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這被稱為 「 教堂 」 論 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你就得到了這個連結 , 說babbage建造的東西真的是一台電腦
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠做到我們今天用電腦做的一切 , 只有很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓你們知道有多慢 , 它有1k的記憶體 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用打孔卡 , 裡面被餵食 , 它跑了大約一萬倍的速度 , 第一台zx81 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一個ram包 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想要的話 , 你可以在多餘的記憶上加入很多 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	那麼 , 今天這帶給我們什麼呢 ?
so there are plans .	所以 , 有一些計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在斯文頓 , 科學博物館的檔案庫 , 有數百個計劃和數千頁的筆記 , 是由查爾斯•巴貝奇所寫的 , 關於這個分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一組是我們稱之為 「 計劃28 」 的計畫 , 這也是我開始與doronswaade合作的慈善團體的名字 , 他是科學博物館計算機的策展人 , 也是開啟這個計劃的人 , 來建造一個差異引擎 , 我們的計劃是建造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在肯辛頓南部 , 我們將建造一個分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個項目有幾個部分 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	其中一個是掃描babbage的檔案庫
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	那是已經完成的 。 第二 , 是所有這些計畫的研究 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是電腦模擬那台機器 , 最後的部分是將它實體建造在科學博物館 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它被建造出來時 , 你終於能夠理解一個電腦是如何運作的 , 因為與其在你面前有一小塊晶片 , 你還得看著這個和諧的東西 , 說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶體在運作 , 我看到cpu在運作 , 我聽見它在運作 。 我可能聞到它在運作 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在那之間 , 我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	巴貝奇自己寫道 , 他說 , 一旦分析引擎存在 , 它一定會引導未來科學的發展 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有打造過 , 因為他總是很喜歡新的計畫 , 但當它真的被打造出來 , 當然 , 在1940年代 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我來給你們一點點它的樣子 , 用影片來呈現cpu機制的其中一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	所以 , 這只是三組齒輪 , 它會加上 。 這是加法的機制 , 所以你想像這台巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年的時間 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代發生之前 , 我們將擁有
thank you very much .	非常感謝大家 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這場影像填充的演說中 , 雅南•亞伯特蘭在他的網站上展示了他三個最近針對人類和我們棲息地的項目 , 在他的系列 「 上方的地球 」 中 , 來自全球各地的個人訪問 , 在他的網頁 「 其他六十億人 」 , 及他即將出版的電影《家》中 , 記錄了人類透過呼吸的影片 , 對環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人類、媒體、攝影、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	yannarhusbertrand用寬的形狀捕捉脆弱的地球 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響力 , 可以靠飛機來到這裡 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了九噸的二氧化碳 , 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡是要談談生態學 , 一年內我排放的二氧化碳和法國人一樣多 。
so what do i have to do ?	那我該怎麼做呢 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	我回家時 , 必須要殺一位法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須以另一種方式抵銷我的碳 , 就像我每次都一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的工作是展現我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我會給你們看一些例子 , 是我去年所拍攝的最後一張照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯達省的沙油 , 大量的污染
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題所在 ; 我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯達省 , 人們工作非作業 , 24小時 , 以7小時的速度 , 盡可能提煉石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的終點 。
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	石油沙不是個長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用比我們發現的石油多了三倍 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的
coral reef in new caledonia .	新加里多尼亞的珊瑚礁
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	百分之百的珊瑚可能在2050年因為全球暖化而被消滅 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	你知道珊瑚對溫度非常敏感 , 對海洋的生物多樣性也非常重要 。

it was impossible to do this picture 15 years ago .	15年前是不可能做到的 。
now there is a new way open between atlantic and pacific .	現在大西洋和太平洋之間有了新的開放方式 。
the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	從1960年起 , 北極的厚度減少了超過40% 。
there is a new face of kilimanjaro without ice .	在沒有冰的情況下 , 吉利馬扎羅是新的面孔 。
it lost 80 percent of its ice .	它失去了80%的冰 。
according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	根據科學家的說法 , 在一百年內 , 所有登山冰川都會消失 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰川對地球上的生命來說非常重要 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	就像艾爾•高爾說的 , 有二十億人住在來自喜馬拉雅冰川的水上 。

video: this earth is four and a half billion years old .	影片:地球已經有四十五億年的歷史了 。
these plants , several hundred million years old .	這些植物 , 幾億年來
and we humans have been walking upright for only 200 thousand years .	而我們人類只有二十萬年來直立行走 。
we've managed to adapt , and have conquered the whole planet .	我們想辦法去適應 , 而且已經征服了整個地球 。
for generations , we've been raising our children , not unlike millions of other species living beside us .	世代以來 , 我們一直在養育孩子 , 不像其他數百萬個物種住在我們身邊 。
for the past 30 years i've been closely watching the earth and its dwellers from high up in the sky .	在過去的三十年間 , 我很仔細地觀察地球和它來自天上高處的居民 。
our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生活與我們星球的福祉綁在一起 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們依賴水、森林、沙漠、海洋 。
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	捕魚、繁殖、耕作 , 仍然是世界上最重要的人類職業 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	而把我們結合在一起的 , 遠遠大於分裂我們的東西 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都有同樣的需求 , 對於地球的禮物 , 和我們自己上升的願望相同 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而 , 我們卻繼續築起圍牆 , 以讓我們分離 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	現今 , 我們最大的戰役就是要保護地球的天然資源 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	不到50年 , 我們已經徹底地改變了它 , 甚至比人類歷史更加徹底 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上有一半的森林已經消失了 。
water resources are running low .	水資源正在經營得很低 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	密集耕作正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源不是永續的 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在瀕臨我們自己 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只努力改善生活 。
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富差距越來越廣 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們還沒有了解到 , 我們的速度比地球能維持的速度還要快得多 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道現今的解決方案是可行的 。
we all have the power to change this trend for the better .	我們都有能力可以更好地改變這個趨勢 。
so what are we waiting for ?	所以 , 我們在等什麼 ?

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston的演講中 , 理查德•瑞斯尼克指出 , 基因定序即將把健康照護顛倒 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna , 生物科技 , 健康照護 , 科學 , 科技
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查德•雷斯尼克:歡迎來到基因革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我給你們看人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下方是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女人有兩個大的x染色體 , 男人有xx染色體 , 當然 , 還有那個小小的y複製品 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	抱歉男孩們 , 但這只是個小東西 , 讓你有所不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以 , 如果你放大這個基因組 , 那麼你所看到的 , 當然 , 就是這個雙螺旋結構--生命的編碼與這四個生化字母一起拼出來 , 或者我們稱之為鹼基 , 對了:a , c , g , t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少 ? 30億 。
is that a big number ?	這是一個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以大量地丟出去 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我要在這1280像素上安置一個鹼基 , 到800個解析度螢幕上 , 我們會需要300個螢幕來觀察基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以這真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	也許是因為它的大小 , 一群人 , 順帶一提 , y染色體決定他們會想要定序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	所以 , 事實上 , 15年後 , 大約40億美元後 , 基因組被定序並發表了 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	2003年 , 最後的版本被出版了 , 他們繼續研究它 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	全部都是在這樣的一個機器上完成的 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每一塊錢大約要花一塊美金 , 很慢的做法 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	所以 , 現在我們要做的是 , 我們拿一個基因組 , 大概50份複製品 , 我們把所有複製品剪成五十個鹼基 , 然後我們將它們排序 , 大量平行 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們將它帶入軟體中 , 重新組合起來 , 告訴你這個故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	所以 , 給大家看一下這是什麼樣子的 , 人類基因組計劃:3gbs , 對 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	其中一台機器在其中一台上運行 , 一個星期內就有200gbabab 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	而那200個今年夏天將會變為600個步調 , 沒有這個步調會慢下來 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以一個鹼基的價格 , 一個鹼基定序已經下降了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這就等同於你在1998年用氣體把你的車子塞滿 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開車到木星 , 後背兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc地點、所有醫學文獻的檔案庫、摩爾定律、測序的舊方法 , 這裡是所有新東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是個木質尺度 , 你通常不會看到像那樣上升的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 全世界對人類基因組的定序能力 , 今年大約有5萬到10萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	而且我們知道這基於正在被放置的機器 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	預計會在可預見的未來中增加一倍、三倍或四倍 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一個特別的實驗室 , 代表了所有能力的20% 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做北京基因組學研究所 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	順道一提 , 中國在新月球上絕對勝出了這個比賽 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學有何意義 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	所以一個女人年紀是37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她和第2階段的雌激素受體乳癌有關 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術、化療和放射線治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她帶著第三期卵巢癌回來 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次用手術和化療來治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她在42歲時 , 得了更多卵巢癌 , 更多化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她帶著急性髓性白血病回來 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸衰竭 , 八天後她就死了 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這名女子被治療的方式 , 只要10年 , 就會看起來像血液一樣 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	正是因為像我的同事rickwilson在華盛頓大學的基因研究所決定要檢視這位女生後模樣
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他做了測序 , 取出皮膚細胞 , 健康的皮膚 , 以及癌症的骨髓 , 他在幾週內完成了兩者的全部基因組 , 沒什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	接著 , 他在軟體中比較了這兩組基因 , 他在其它事情中發現 , 其中有兩千個鹼基耗損 , 在一個叫做tp53的基因中 , 有三十億個鹼基 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你在這基因中有這種神奇的突變 , 你一生中有90%的機率會罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	所以 , 不幸的是 , 這對這位女士沒有幫助 , 但它的確有嚴重、深刻的影響 , 如果你願意 , 影響她的家人 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有相同的突變 , 然後他們得到了這個基因檢測 , 然後他們了解了 , 那麼他們就可以去取得一般的螢幕 , 並且可以早期發現癌症 , 並且可能過著顯著更長壽的生命 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	現在讓我向各位介紹啤酒雙胞胎 , 在兩歲時被診斷出腦性麻痺 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的母親是個非常勇敢的女人 , 她不相信症狀不符合我們 , 透過一些英雄性努力和許多網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學界的人 , 事實上 , 他們還有別的東西 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們所擁有的就是預防反應性肌張力不全症 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了 「 左撇子 」 , 他們的症狀確實有所改善 , 但他們並沒有完全症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	結果 , 這張圖片中的先生是一位叫joebeery的人 , 他很幸運能成為一家叫做 「 生命科技 」 的公司 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	它們是兩間製造這些大量基因體定序工具的公司之一 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	所以他做的是讓他的孩子定序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現一系列突變基因在一個叫做spr的基因中 , 它負責製造血清素 , 和其他東西 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以 , 在左上方 , 他們給了這些孩子一種血清素前驅性藥物 , 現在他們很正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	沒有完整的基因序列 , 絕對不會發生這種事 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	幾年前 , 花費十萬美元 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天是一萬美金 。 明年是一千美金 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	價錢是100元後的一年 , 給或一年 。
that's how fast this is moving .	這就是這個動作的速度 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	以下是小尼克喜歡蝙蝠俠和松鼠槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果尼克出現在兒童醫院 , 帶著這種不良的肚子 , 像飢荒的受害者一樣 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	不是說他沒有吃東西 , 而是當他吃的時候 , 他的腸子基本上會打開 , 糞便外出到他的腸子裡 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	所以 , 一百個手術後 , 他看著他的母親 , 說: 「 媽 , 請為我祈禱 。 我好多痛苦 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫生剛好有臨床遺傳學的背景 , 他完全不知道發生了什麼事 , 但他說: 「 咱們來把這個孩子的基因序列定序吧 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	而他們發現的 , 是控制細胞死亡的基因突變 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以這個理論是他對食物產生了一些免疫反應 , 基本上這是自然的反應 , 這會造成一些程式化的細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但管控下去的基因卻壞了 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	這也說明了 , 當然 , 針對骨髓移植手術的治療 , 他也接受了這個治療 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	經過九個月的艱苦復原後 , 他現在用a1醬汁吃牛排了 。
the prospect of using the genome as a universal diagnostic is upon us today .	使用基因組作為普遍診斷的前景 , 今天就在我們面前 。
today , it's here .	今天 , 它就在這裡 。
and what it means for all of us is that everybody in this room could live an extra five , 10 , 20 years just because of this one thing .	這對我們所有人的意義是 , 在座的各位 , 可以多活五、十年、二十年 , 只因為這一件事 。
which is a fantastic story , unless you think about humanity's footprint on the planet and our ability to keep up food production .	這是個很棒的故事 , 除非你考慮到地球上人類的足跡以及我們維持糧食生產的能力 。
so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	所以 , 同樣的科技也被用來種植玉米、小麥、黃豆 , 和其他農作物 , 都是高度包容的乾旱、洪水、害蟲和殺蟲劑 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	現在 , 看看 , 只要我們繼續增加人口 , 我們就必須繼續種植和食用基因改造食物 , 這是我今天唯一要取的位置 。
unless there's anybody in the audience that would like to volunteer to stop eating ?	除非觀眾中有人願意自願停止吃東西 ?
none , not one .	沒有 , 沒有一個 。
this is a typewriter , a staple of every desktop for decades .	這是一台打字機 , 數十年來每台桌面的釘子 。
and in fact , the typewriter was essentially deleted by this thing .	事實上 , 打字機基本上是被這東西刪除的 。
and then more general versions of word processors came about .	然後更多文字處理器的普及版本就來了 。
but ultimately , it was a disruption on top of a disruption .	但最終 , 它在顛覆的上方出現了顛覆 。
it was bob metcalfe inventing the ethernet and the connection of all these computers that fundamentally changed everything .	鮑勃•米特卡菲斯發明了 「 乙烯 」 和 「 所有電腦 」 的連結 , 徹底改變了一切 。
and suddenly we had netscape , and we had yahoo and we had , indeed , the entire dotcom bubble .	突然間 , 我們有了netscape , 我們有yahoo , 我們有了整個網路泡沫 。
not to worry though , that was quickly rescued by the ipod , facebook and , indeed , angry birds .	不用擔心 , 很快就被ipod、facebook和憤怒的鳥救了 。
look , this is where we are today .	聽著 , 這是我們今天的處境 。
this is the genomic revolution today . this is where we are .	這是今天的基因革命 。 這是我們現在的處境 。
so what i'd like you to consider is: what does it mean when these dots don't represent the individual bases of your genome , but they connect to genomes all across the planet ?	所以 , 我想請各位考慮的是:當這些點無法代表你基因組的個別基對時 , 它意味著什麼 ? 但它們會連結到地球各地的基因組 ?
so i just recently had to buy life insurance .	所以我才剛買了生命保險 。
and i was required to answer: a . i have never had a genetic test , b . i've had one , here you go , and c . i've had one and i'm not telling .	我被要求回答:a.我從來沒有過基因檢測 , b.我已經有過基因檢測 , 開始了 , c.我已經有過一個 , 沒說過 。
thankfully , i was able to answer a , and i say that honestly in case my life insurance agent is listening .	謝天謝地 , 我能夠回答a , 我說實話 , 以防我的生命保險經紀人在傾聽 。
but what would have happened if i had said c ?	但如果我說過c , 會發生什麼事 ?
consumer applications for genomics , they will flourish .	消費者應用在基因組學上 , 他們會蓬勃發展 。
do you want to see whether you're genetically compatible with your girlfriend ? sure .	你想看看你是否和女朋友基因上相容 ? 當然 。

there's already a lab today that tests for allele 334 of the avpr1 gene , the socalled cheating gene .	今天已經有實驗室在測試avpr1基因中的alle3334 , 也就是所謂的作弊基因 。
so anybody who's here today with your significant other , just turn over to them and swab their mouth , send it to the lab and you'll know for sure .	所以 , 今天在場的任何人 , 都帶著你的重要性 , 只要轉向他們 , 換上他們的嘴 , 送到實驗室 , 你一定會知道 。
do you really want to elect a president whose genome suggests cardiomyopathy ?	你真的想要選出一位基因組建議心臟病的總統嗎 ?
now think of it , it's 2016 and the leading candidate releases not only her four years of back tax returns , but also her personal genome .	現在想想看 , 2016年 , 最頂尖的候選人不但釋放了她四年後的稅收 , 也釋放了她的個人基因組 。
and it looks really good .	而且看起來還不錯 。
and then she challenges all of her competitors to do the same .	接著 , 她挑戰她所有的競爭者都要做同樣的事 。
do you think that's not going to happen ?	你認為這不會發生嗎 ?
do you think it would have helped john mccain ?	你認為這會幫助約翰麥肯嗎 ?
how many people in the audience have the last name resnick like me ? raise your hand .	觀眾中有多少人有和我一樣的最後一個名字resnick ? 請舉手 。
typically , there's one or two .	通常有一兩種
so my father's father was one of 10 resnick brothers .	所以我父親的父親是10個雷斯尼克兄弟之一 。
they all hated each other .	都互相討厭
and they all moved to different parts of the planet .	並且都搬到地球的不同部位 。
so it's likely that i'm related to every resnick that i ever meet , but i don't know .	所以 , 很可能我跟我遇到的每一個resnick都有關 , 但我不知道 。
but imagine if my genome were deidentified , sitting in software , and a third cousin's genome was also sitting there , and there was software that could compare these two and make these associations .	但 , 想像一下 , 如果我的基因被辨識出來 , 坐在軟體裡 , 第三堂兄弟的基因也坐在那 , 有軟體可以比較這兩者 , 做出這些關聯 。
not hard to imagine . my company has software that does this right now .	不難想像 。 我的公司有軟體現在就這麼做了 。
and so imagine one more thing: that that software is able to ask both parties for mutual consents , " would you be willing to meet your third cousin ? "	所以 , 再想像一件事:那個軟體可以向兩方提出相互同意見 , 「 你願意見到你的第三表兄嗎 ? 」
and if we both say yes , voila ! welcome to chromosomally linkedin .	如果我們兩個都說好 , 瞧 , 歡迎來到染色體linkedin 。
now this is probably a good thing , right ?	這可能是件好事 , 對吧 ?
you have bigger clan gatherings and so on .	你有更大的族群聚會等等 。

okay , so experts think that one to three percent of you are not actually the father of your child .	好 , 所以專家認為在座有1%到3%的人其實不是你孩子的父親 。

and like any new technology , it's really in humanity's hands to wield it for the betterment of mankind , or not .	和任何新科技一樣 , 它真的是在人類的手中 , 為了人類的更好 , 或不是 。
and so i urge you all to wake up and to tune in and to influence the genomic revolution that's happening all around you .	所以 , 我鼓勵大家起床 , 開始調整並影響你周遭發生的基因革命 。
daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾•克拉夫特示範他的骨髓取樣了他的骨髓 , 一個新裝置 , 很快地收集了救命的骨髓 , 給捐贈者最少的疼痛 。 他強調 , 骨髓中發現的成體幹細胞可以用來治療許多臨終條件 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟病 。
biology , biotech , health , health care , medicine , science , technology	生物學、生物科技、健康、醫療、醫學、科學、科技、科技 。
daniel kraft invents a better way to harvest bone marrow	danielkraft發明了更好的方式來收集骨髓 。
so i am a pediatric cancer doctor and stemcell researcher at stanford university where my clinical focus has been bone marrow transplantation .	我是一名小兒科癌症醫生 , 也是史丹佛大學的幹細胞研究員 , 我的臨床焦點是骨髓移植手術 。
now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	去年jillboltetaylor的靈感來源 , 我沒有帶來人腦 , 但我的確帶來了一公升的骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	而骨髓實際上是我們用來拯救數萬名病患的生命 , 大部分患有先進的惡性腫瘤 , 如白血病、淋巴瘤 , 和其他一些疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	所以 , 幾年前 , 我在史丹佛做移植手術 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室 。 我們這裡有bob , 他是志願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們送他的骨髓到全國各地 , 以拯救白血病孩童的性命 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 實際上 , 我們要如何採集這種骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r.團隊 , 麻醉醫師 , 護士 , 還有另一位醫生從我身邊過來 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	鮑勃站在桌子上 , 我們拿著這個小針頭 , 你知道的 , 沒什麼大不了的 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們的做法是 , 我們把這個放在軟組織中 , 將它打到硬骨頭裡 , 進入tuchus這個技術名詞 , 每次用針筒把大約十層骨髓送出 ,
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	把它交給護士 , 讓她垂成一個錫片 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把手交回給我 。 我們一而再 , 再而三地做 。
about 200 times usually .	通常大約兩百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	最後 , 我的手臂是sore , 我手上有一通電話 , 更不用說bob , 他的後端看起來像這樣 , 像瑞士起司 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道嗎 , 這個程序在大約四十年間都沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	或許還有更好的方式可以做到 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以 , 我想到一個最少侵入性的方法 , 一個我們稱之為 「 骨髓採取器 」 的新裝置 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而骨髓採取器 , 這裡的運作方式
our standard seethrough patient .	我們標準的看法是病人 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨頭數十次 , 我們只需要進入一次 , 進入髖部前部 , 或臀部後部 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個靈活的導管 , 上面有特殊的電線迴圈 , 會留在骨髓的殘酷部分 , 跟著臀部的輪廓 , 隨著它移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它能讓你非常快速地呼吸 , 或快速地吸出骨髓 , 很快的通過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以透過同樣的入口多次穿梭 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快的 , 鮑勃就只能得到一個穿刺 , 局部麻醉 , 把這個收容器拿來當作門診 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了幾個原型 , 我在史丹佛得到了一個小額的補助 。
and played around with this a little bit .	再來玩一點點 。
and our team members developed this technology .	而我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們得到兩種大型動物 , 還有豬的研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 令我們驚訝的是 , 我們不僅僅把骨髓出去 , 我們還得到了骨髓採取器中十倍的幹細胞活動 , 相較於一般的裝置 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年剛核准的食品及藥物管理局
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是個活體病人 。 你可以看到它跟著有彈性的曲線繞著它轉 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	在同一個病人中 , 會有兩個穿過 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在局部麻醉下完成的 , 作為一個專門病患 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	再一次 , 我們得到的幹細胞 , 比標準的方法在同一個病人身上完成的多出三到六倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	所以 , 為什麼你要在乎 ? 骨髓是非常豐富的成體幹細胞來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	大家都知道胚胎幹細胞
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們很有潛力 , 但還沒進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成體幹細胞遍佈全身 , 包括我們骨髓內的血液檢查幹細胞 , 我們已經使用這種形式的幹細胞 , 超過四十年 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去十年間 , 骨髓幹細胞的爆炸用在治療病人的其他疾病例如心臟病、血管疾病、組織工程、甚至神經系統治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛出櫃了 , 我們正在商業化 , 今年 , 第二世代的骨髓採礦者 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望能得到更多幹細胞 , 轉化成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人簽名 , 成為潛在救命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	甚至可能可以讓你在更年輕、更健康時 , 銀行自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 用在未來你應該需要它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終 , 這裡是一張我們骨髓移植者的照片 , 每年在史丹佛聚集一堂 ,
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們在未來有更多這樣的倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者garrettlisi提出了一個有爭議的新宇宙模型 , 剛好可以回答所有大問題 。 如果沒有其他問題的話 , 它是最美麗的8d8d立體模型 , 是你所見過最美麗的8d立體粒子和力 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技、
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	garrettlisi在他所有東西的理論上
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 。 看看那些殺人方程式 。 甜心 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我會盡力去描述粒子物理的美 , 不用方程式來描述 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 我們可以從珊瑚身上學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗和不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每一塊珊瑚頭都是由數千個別的珊瑚蟲所組成 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些珊瑚蟲不斷地在繁殖和分裂成基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是一個超級聰明的珊瑚蟲 , 我們可以單獨一個體 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他在這個特定的地點 , 相較於他鄰居是否有機會 , 或是命運 , 又或者怎樣 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	現在 , 在我們向上指示我們要把溫度調高太高之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題完全是愚蠢的 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以是相當類似的意思 , 你看 , 我有衝浪的傷疤可以證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這個珊瑚蟲會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居是相當明顯的一模一樣的複製品 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也在其他的地點 , 但將他們視為獨立的個體 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚來說 , 分支成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	和我們不同的是 , 一個超級智慧的珊瑚蟲會獨特的準備去了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常準確地描述了我們的宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們現實是持續分支成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對我們人類來說 , 這是一件很奇怪的事 , 因為我們只能經歷一種可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子力學的怪異性 , 最早是由厄文•薛丁格和他的貓所描述的 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓更喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個設定中 , 薛丁格在一個有放射性樣本的盒子裡 , 由量子力學定律 , 分支到一種狀態 , 一種放射性和一種狀態 , 它不是 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在這個樣本放射線的樹枝中 , 它會觸發釋放毒液和薛丁格死亡的觸發器 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一個分支中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些實相是被每個個體分開的 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	無論如何 , 另一種都不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說似乎很奇怪 , 因為我們每一個人都只經歷一個個體的存在 , 而我們看不到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	這就好像我們每一個人 , 就像薛丁格 , 是一種珊瑚蟲 , 分裂成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們這就是世界在微小的尺度下運作的方式 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	可以用單一句子來總結:所有可能發生的事 , 都會做 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不表示一切都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其餘的物理則是要描述什麼可以發生 , 以及什麼不能發生 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們的是 , 一切都歸功於幾何學 , 以及基本粒子的相互作用 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只有在這些相互作用完全平衡的情況下 , 事情才有可能發生 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我來描述一下我們對這些粒子的認識 , 它們是什麼 , 以及這個平衡是如何運作的 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 一束質子和反質子會被加速到接近光速的速度 , 並且在一個碰撞中聚集在一起 , 產生了一股純粹的能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量馬上被轉換成亞原子粒子的噴霧 , 和偵測器和電腦用來弄清楚它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這個巨大的機器──日內瓦的cern核子對撞機──有一個圓周長17英里 , 當它在運作時 , 會比蒙特利市多出5倍的能量 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們不能明確預測在任何個體碰撞中粒子會產生什麼 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性都被實現了 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理的確告訴我們 , 粒子能產生什麼 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和能量就跟質子和反質子一樣多 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這個能量極限更巨大的粒子都不會產生 , 而且對我們來說仍然是看不見的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新的粒子加速器會如此興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它會把這個能量限制在前所未有的能量之外七倍所以我們很快就會看到一些新粒子
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談到我們可能看到的東西之前 , 讓我先描述一下我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有整個亞原子粒子的動物園
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人都很熟悉電子
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	現場的許多人都在做一個好的生活 , 把他們推過來 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有中性伴侶 , 叫做微中子 , 沒有電荷和很小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相對的 , 上層夸克有非常大的質量 , 相對的 , 相對的 , 相對的 , 相對的 , 相較之下 , 相較之下 , 相較之下 , 相對的夸克有著非常大的質量 , 相結合成三個組合
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	這些粒子都帶著相反電荷的反粒子 , 帶著相對電荷 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也有較不熟悉的第二代和第三代 , 和第一代有相同的載荷卻有較高的質量 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些粒子都與各種力粒子相互作用 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力的作用力通過所謂光子的粒子產生電荷的相互作用
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種非常微弱的力量 , 叫做 「 弱力 」 , 它只會和左撇子相互作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強力作用 , 會帶有不同的載荷 , 叫做顏色載荷 , 會出現三種不同的品種:紅、綠、藍 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪murraygellmann為這些名字--他們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 還有重力 , 透過質量和旋轉 , 與物質相互作用的力量 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 這裡有一種和每一種力有關的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力會根據每一種粒子所擁有的對應的載荷產生相互作用 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個還沒被看見的粒子 , 但我們很確定存在 , 就是希格斯粒子 , 它給予所有其他粒子的質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的就是看到這個希格斯粒子我們幾乎可以肯定它會
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的謎團 , 是我們可能還會看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	接下來我要給你們看一個美麗的可能性 , 正朝這場演說的結尾 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們用不同的旋轉和載荷來計算這些不同的粒子 , 總共有226種 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	那是很多粒子用來追蹤的 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	看起來奇怪的是 , 大自然會有這麼多基本粒子 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據它們的載荷把它們畫出來 , 有些美麗的圖案就會浮現出來 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的載荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有一個電荷 , 一個負電荷 , 夸克有三分之一的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	當2個上夸克和1個下夸克結合成質子時 , 它的電荷總和是1 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 有反式電荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷其實是另外兩種載荷的結合:超荷和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們散開超荷和弱荷 , 並在這個二度載荷空間中繪製粒子的載荷 , 電荷是這些粒子位於垂直方向的位置 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力的相互作用 , 根據它們的高檔和弱荷 , 產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這被稱為 「 聯合式電網模式 」 , 它在1967年被放在一起 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	大部分人都很熟悉電荷而不是兩者都是希格斯粒子
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯有很大的質量 , 打破了電擊模式的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	藉由給弱粒子一個很大的質量 , 使弱作用力變得很弱 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於大量的希格斯人坐著 , 沿著水平的方向 , 電磁力的光子仍然是無質量的 , 和電荷在這個載荷空間中沿著垂直的方向相互作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力在二維空間中被描述成粒子電荷的模式
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們能將強力納入 , 透過散播出它的兩個載荷方向 , 將強力粒子的載荷畫在夸克沿這些方向上 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四度載荷空間中被繪製出來 , 然後投射到像這樣的兩個維度 , 以便我們能看到它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子相互作用時 , 自然會在四個載荷方向上保持一個完美的平衡 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果一個粒子和一個反粒子相撞 , 它會在四個載荷方向中 , 產生出一股能量和總載荷的零 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	此時 , 任何東西都能被創造出來只要它有相同的能量並維持一個總載荷的0
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	例如 , 這種弱力粒子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的互動中 , 載荷必須總是平衡的 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個弱粒子可以腐化成一個電子和一個反中微子 , 這三個仍然可以加上零個總載荷 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些載荷的模式不僅僅是漂亮的 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們什麼樣的互動是被允許發生的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中轉動這個載荷空間 , 來更好地觀察強烈的交互作用 , 這有很好的對稱性 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強力相互作用中 , 一個強力粒子 , 例如這一個 , 會和一個有色夸克相互作用 , 例如這個綠色方塊 , 給一個有不同顏色的夸克載荷──這個紅色方塊 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	而強烈的相互作用每秒鐘都發生在我們身體的每一個原子上 , 將原子核放在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四種載荷對應三種力量並不是故事的結局 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以再包含兩種載荷對應到重力力 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們把這些納入 , 每個粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉載荷 , 旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以他們都分開了 , 在六度載荷空間中給予一個不錯的模式 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個圖案 , 看到它相當漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	目前 , 這個模式與我們目前對大自然的最佳知識是如何在這些基本粒子的微小尺度下建立的 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們對某些特定的認識 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	其中有些粒子是實驗的極限 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個圖案中 , 我們已經知道了這些微小尺度的粒子物理學 。 宇宙運作的方式和這些微小的尺度是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些新的、古老的想法 , 關於我們還不知道的事情 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想單單用數學來擴展這個模式 , 看看我們能不能把手放在整體的恩克拉達身上 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到所有組成我們宇宙的粒子和力 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想要用這張圖來預測新粒子 , 當實驗達到更高的能量時 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以 , 在粒子物理學中有一個很古老的想法 , 就是這種已知的載荷模式 , 不太對稱 , 可以從更完美的圖案中顯現出來 , 和希格斯粒子如何打破電極圖案 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了要做到這一點 , 我們需要引進有新的載荷方向的新力量 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們導入一個新的方向時 , 我們得以猜測粒子的載荷會隨著這個方向移動 , 然後我們可以把它和其他粒子一起旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們明智地猜測 , 我們就能在六度載荷維度中建立標準載荷的載荷 , 作為七度載荷維度中這個更完美的對稱性 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這個特別的選擇對應於1973年pati和salam推出的一個大統一理論 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看這個新統一的圖案時 , 我們可以看到一些缺口 , 粒子似乎缺少了 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是統一理論的運作方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家尋找更大、更對稱的圖案 , 將已建立的圖案納入為子集 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們可以預測從未見過的粒子的存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統一模型預測了這兩種新力粒子的存在 , 它應該會表現得很像弱力 , 只有比較弱的力 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七度空間中旋轉這組載荷 , 並考慮一個奇怪的事實:關於物質粒子的第二代和第三代物質在六度載荷空間中有完全相同的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並不是獨一無二的被它們的六個載荷所辨識 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們彼此坐在標準載荷空間的頂端 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 那麼我們可以把獨特的新載荷分配給每個粒子 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後我們可以在八度空間中旋轉 , 看看整個圖案是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡我們可以看到第二代和第三代物質與第一個世代的對稱性是 「 試驗性 」 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	八度中的這個特殊的載荷圖案 , 其實是數學中最美麗的幾何結構的一部分 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	它是最大的例外謊言團體 , e8的模式 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言團體是平滑的 , 彎曲的形狀有248維度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	圖案中的每個點都對應到這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀的對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論的彎曲時空 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	加上量子力學 , 這個形狀的幾何學可以描述宇宙如何在最小的尺度下運作的一切 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這個形狀存在於八度載荷空間的八度載荷空間之中 , 精確地漂亮 , 它總結了成千上萬個可能的相互作用 , 在這些基本粒子之間 , 每一個都只是這個複雜形狀的一面 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們旋轉它時 , 我們可以看到許多其他錯綜複雜的圖案在這一個圖案中 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	藉由一個特定的旋轉 , 我們可以向下看這個圖案 , 沿著一個對稱軸 , 同時看到所有的粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	這是一個非常美麗的物體 , 就像任何統一的物體一樣 , 我們可以看到一些洞 , 新粒子是這個圖案所需要的 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	新粒子應該有20個缺口 , 其中兩個已經被patisalam粒子給填滿了 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從它們的位置在這個圖案中 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該是像希格斯粒子一樣的疤田 , 但有色荷 , 和強力相互作用 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子完成這個圖案 , 給我們完整的e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有著非常深奧的數學根源 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這個偉大數學美的物體可以用最小尺度來描述粒子相互作用的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	而這個想法 , 大自然被數學所描述的完全不是新東西 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	在1623年 , 伽利略寫了這句話: 「 大自然的宏偉書 , 代表著持續開放給我們的目光 , 是用數學的語言寫的 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形 , 和其他幾何圖形 , 沒有這些 , 人類無法理解它的單字 ; 若沒有這些 , 一個人就會在黑暗的迷宮中漫遊 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這點是真的 , 我曾試著遵循伽利略的指導 , 以描述粒子物理的數學 , 只用了三角形、圓形 , 和其他幾何圖形 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我實際在研究這個東西時 , 數學可以像一個黑暗的迷宮 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但 , 要確保數學的核心是純粹的 , 美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	加入了量子力學 , 這個數學把我們的宇宙描述成一個正在成長的e8珊瑚 , 粒子在每個地點以各種可能的方式相互作用 , 根據一個美麗的圖案 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	當更多的圖案用像大型強子對撞機這樣的大型機器來觀察時 , 我們也許能看到大自然是否使用這個e8圖案或另一個圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這種發現的過程是很棒的探險 , 能參與其中 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc發現了符合e8圖案的粒子 , 那會是非常非常酷的 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc發現了新的粒子但它們不符合這個模式那會非常有趣但對這個e8理論不利
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人而言是不好的 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會有多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 很不好 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然的運作方式是很冒險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其它類似的 , 是長期的拍攝 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人會做很多辛苦的工作 , 知道大部分這些想法可能最後不會成天 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣子的:有很多的廢物 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論很像新創公司 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	就如同任何大型投資一樣 , 要放棄一系列研究是很困難的 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果有東西不管用 , 你就得要丟掉它 , 再試試別的 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在 , 在這種不確定性中 , 唯一能維持理智和達到快樂的方法 , 就是在生活中保持平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我已經盡我所能過著一個平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著在物理學、愛與衝浪中平衡自己的三個載荷方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這麼一來 , 就算我所研究的物理學什麼都沒有 , 我仍然知道我過得很好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著生活在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	在過去的十年間 , 我住在毛伊島上 , 一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在這是宇宙中最偉大的奧秘之一我父母是如何在那段時間中存活下來而不涉足任何與全職工作相似的東西
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我會告訴你那個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊島的家裡辦公室的一個景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到 , 這些美麗的觀點都很類似 , 但在稍微不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一種非常不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心房租讓我花我的時間做我愛的工作 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	過著遊牧民族的存在 , 有時是很困難的 , 但它讓我能住在美麗的地方 , 在我的生活中保持平衡 , 讓我能過得很開心 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我可以花很多時間和超級聰明的珊瑚相處 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明的人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	所以我很高興能在這裡受邀來ted演講 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概明白其中的2% , 但我還是很喜歡 。 所以我會聽起來很笨 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的萬事萬物理論:我很習慣珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克:沒錯 。 最少人感到興奮的原因是 , 如果你是對的 , 它會把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是不是說我們應該把宇宙想成是宇宙 , 它的心臟是最小的東西 , 不知何故 , 是e8物體的可能性 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小的尺度上 , 有沒有一個尺寸的尺寸 ?
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	格林:嗯 , 現在我給你們看的圖案 , 就是我們所知道的基本粒子物理學已經對應到一個非常美麗的形狀 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	那就是我說我們知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	這個形狀有著驚人的相似之處 , 也符合這個e8圖案的方式 , 可能是其餘的圖片 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我給你們看的這些點的圖案 , 其實代表了這個高維物體的對稱性 , 會在我們所體驗的太空時間間被扭曲、移動、跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就解釋了我們看到的所有這些基本粒子
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克:但弦理論學家 , 如我所知 , 用更小的弦振動來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面振動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該如何看待與e8相關的電子呢 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	格林:不 , 它會是這個e8形狀的對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當這個形狀在時空中移動時 , 它會扭轉 。 隨著它移動的方向 , 它會變成我們所看到的粒子 。 所以 , 它會是:e8形狀的大小 , 它會如何和電子相連 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	變大了嗎 ? 變小了嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	格林:嗯 , 據我們所知 , 電子是指粒子 , 所以它會下降到最小的可能範圍 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 這些東西在量子場理論中被解釋的方法是 , 所有的可能性都同時在擴張和發展中 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這也是為什麼我用類比來珊瑚的原因 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	如此一來 , e8進來的方式是 , 它會以時空的每個時點為一個附加的形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說 , 形狀的轉折方式在曲線表面上轉動時的方向是基本粒子本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	所以 , 透過量子場理論 , 他們將自己呈現為點 , 並且以此方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我是否能把這個更清楚 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:這真的無關緊要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它喚起了一種驚奇的感覺 , 我當然也想了解更多這種事 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但 , 非常謝謝你來 。 這絕對是令人著迷的 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇的黑猩猩研究員珍.古德.古德 , 談到塔卡爾和她的其他社區計畫 , 協助在非洲大鎮上 , 和受到威脅的動物一起生活 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類、科學、
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍•古德拉爾幫助人類和動物一起生活 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , 詹姆波 , 古德•阿班德 , 邦索爾 , 但是我們也可以--ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh 。
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	那是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺前所製造的叫聲 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一邊到另一邊 , 從一群巢穴到下一群 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今天晚上 , 我想從昨天zeray離開的地方來聽我的演講 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他在談論這個令人驚奇、三歲的奧地皮奇汀孩童賽蘭
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽過有關人類的歷史、家族樹 , 透過dna側寫 ,
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	那是一位古生物學家 , 已故的路易斯•勒克 , 他讓我踏上研究黑猩猩的路徑 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	早在那時候還蠻非凡的 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在這有點常見 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	各位可以看出這些化石的樣子 , 從肌肉依附的形狀 , 看出他們與之共存的各種手工藝品 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但它們的行為如何呢 ? 那是他想要知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為並不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張--而現在這是個相當普遍的理論 , 如果我們在最接近的生命親戚、大猩猩和人類的親戚身上發現行為模式或相同 , 那麼也許在七百萬年前那些行為就存在於猿類 , 人類的祖先 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們已經將這些特徵從古代、古老的過去帶過來 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你去看今天處理人類演化的教科書 , 你經常會發現人們在推測早期人類的行為 , 根據黑猩猩的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	牠們比其他生物都更像我們 , 在ted大會上我們也聽說過 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以對我來說 , 我還是要評論黑猩猩和我們很像的方式 , 在某些方面是如此 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每一隻黑猩猩都有他或她自己的個性
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給他們名字 。 他們可以活到60年以上 , 雖然我們認為大部份的人可能不會在野外活到60歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	沃茲爾先生 。 雌性在十一或十二歲時就生下了她的第一個寶寶 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	如此一來 , 她每五到六年就有一個嬰兒 , 一個長期的童年依賴兒童 , 當孩子在療養 , 晚上和母親一起睡覺 , 然後坐在她背上 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信 , 長久以來的童年對黑猩猩來說是很重要的 , 就像對我們一樣 , 和學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在演化過程中變得更複雜 , 以不同形式的動物來演化 , 因此我們發現 , 學習在個體的生命史中扮演著更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	而年輕的黑猩猩花了很多時間看牠們的前輩做的事 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道 , 他們有能力模仿他們所看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 正是這種不同的工具行為 , 目前已在非洲所有不同黑猩猩族群中被研究過的行為 , 是如何從一個世代傳到下一個世代 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習 , 這樣我們才能把這些工具行為描述成原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口語語言 。 我們已經談過了 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	牠們的確有非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 很多的姿勢都類似 , 甚至相同 , 與我們相同 , 在相同的背景下形成 。 迎接黑猩猩擁抱 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們還親吻、牽著手、拍著對方在後面 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	然後牠們會搖擺 , 也會扔石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩的社會中 , 我們發現很多很多同情心的例子 , 前導者是愛的 , 也是真正的利他行為 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 他們和我們一樣 , 本質上有黑暗面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們有能力做到極端殘酷 , 甚至是一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些非常具侵略性的行為 , 大部分的情況都是針對鄰近社會群體的個體 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	牠們非常具侵略性 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	我相信 , 黑猩猩們 , 比起其他生物 , 已經幫助我們了解 , 畢竟 , 人類和動物王國之間沒有明顯的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線 , 隨著我們觀察到的情況越來越模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我從1960年開始的研究至今仍在持續進行中 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些黑猩猩 , 生活在野外複雜的社交生活 , 比起其它任何事情 , 都更能幫助我們意識到我們是其中的一份子 , 而不是分離 , 那些與我們共享這個星球的神奇動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 要找到那隻黑猩猩 , 和世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 會失去牠們的棲息地是相當可悲的 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張從空中拍攝的照片 , 它展示了戈米普的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	就在我飛越整個區域時 , 大約16年前 , 我發現 , 在公園外面 , 這片森林 , 在1960年 , 幾乎沒有被打斷 , 沿著塔哥尼卡湖的東岸 , 在那裡 , 那個小小的30平方公里的戈米國家公園 , 一個問題來到我腦海 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何試著拯救這些有名的黑猩猩 , 當住在國家公園附近的居民在掙扎求生存時 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	比原本的土地還多的人能支援 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民數量增加 , 從蒲隆地到剛果湖邊的難民數量 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	而非常貧窮的人 , 他們買不起來自其他地方的食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 塔卡爾 」 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	以非常全面的方式 , 來改善住在公園附近村民的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	由12個村莊開始 , 現在在24個村莊
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間深入探究 , 但它包含了像樹木的護理之類的東西 , 最適合耕作的方法 , 目前是非常惡化、幾乎像沙漠的土地 , 在這些山上 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制、預防土壤侵蝕的方法 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	重新取得過度使用的農地的方法 , 讓兩年內他們再次能夠生產 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	努力協助村民從井中取得新鮮水源 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	或許建造一些教室
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 和一小群婦女合作 , 提供她們提供微型貸款的機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	如同世界各地的情況 , 我們有百分之九十五的貸款回貸款 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦予女性能力 , 和教育相關 , 為女孩們提供獎學金 , 讓她們能完成中學教育 , 很明顯地 , 在全世界各地都能了解 , 隨著女性的教育改善 , 家庭規模大幅下降 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供關於家庭規劃和關於愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	這個計畫的結果是 , 有些事情正在發生 , 發生在保育上 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育正在發生的是 , 居住在24個村莊的農民 , 與其以白人的身分來研究一群猴子 , 順帶一提 , 許多工作人員現在是坦尚尼亞人 , 但當我們開始計劃時 , 坦尚尼亞是一個坦尚尼亞人團隊進入村莊 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是坦尚尼亞的團隊 , 和村民談話 , 問他們感興趣的是什麼 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 ; 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間的推移 , 當他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始對保育的需求有更多的了解 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 隨著山坡的上層被除去了樹木 , 所以你有了這糟糕的土壤侵蝕和泥巴 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在發展我們所謂的更偉大的gmbe生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是國家公園以外的一個區域 , 延伸到這些非常惡化的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村落有更好的生活標準時 , 他們其實同意將10%到20%的土地放在高地上 , 所以 , 再一次 , 當樹木長回來時 , 黑猩猩們就會有葉廊 , 透過它可以在國家公園外的基因上和其他遺傳的族群互動 。
so tacare is a success .	所以 , tacare是成功的 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲的其它地方進行複製 , 針對面臨極端人口壓力的其他荒野地區 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 如同我們這幾天一直在ted討論的 , 是很重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	貧窮的問題非常嚴重 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你在土地上生活的許多人 , 並不那麼肥沃 , 特別是當你砍掉樹木 , 離開土壤 , 到風向侵蝕 , 隨著絕望的族群砍伐越來越多樹木 , 這樣他們就可以嘗試為自己和家人種植食物 , 有什麼事會發生 ? 有什麼事需要給予 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	其他的問題不只在非洲 , 還在發展中國家 , 到處都是 , 我們對地球做了什麼 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道 , 著名的科學家 , e.o.wilson說過 , 如果地球上的每一個人都達到了平均歐洲人或美國人的生活水準 , 我們需要三個新的星球 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們在說4個 。 但我們沒有它們 。 我們有1個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	到底發生了什麼事呢 ? 我的意思是 , 問題來了 , 在這裡 , 我們是 , 可以說是最聰明的生物 , 那些曾走過地球 , 擁有這個非凡的大腦 , 能夠利用這些科技 , 由這些ted大會所闡述的 , 然而我們卻是毀滅了我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	全世界的原住民 , 在他們做出重大決定之前 , 以前 , 常常會坐在一旁問自己: 「 這個決定會如何影響我們前後七代的人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	現今 , 重大的決策──我在這裡並不是特別談非洲 , 但已開發國家──重大決策包括數百萬美元 , 數百萬人 , 常常會根據 「 這會如何影響下一個股東的會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	而這些決定會影響到非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲各地旅行 , 談論黑猩猩和牠們消失的森林所面臨的問題時 , 我了解到 , 有越來越多的非洲問題可能是前次殖民時代的剝削之門 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始到非洲外面 , 在歐洲演講 , 在美國演講 , 到亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	而且你知道我在說的那種 , 我指的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水資源可能是這個世紀中最關鍵的議題之一也是每個地方的水都被農業、工業 , 和家庭的化學物污染 , 這些化學物仍然遍佈世界各地 , 似乎無法從過去的經驗中獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林正在被砍伐 ; 海嘯的影響越來越嚴重 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經談過土壤侵蝕 ,
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們和其他溫室氣體一起燃燒化石燃料是無情的 , 所以稱之為氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 在全世界 , 人們開始相信 , 我們的氣候出了問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	世界各地的氣候都混雜在一起了 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	而且是那些受影響較差的窮人
it's africa that already is affected .	已經影響到非洲了 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱情況更糟糕 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨量來臨時 , 通常會導致洪水湧入 , 再加上苦惱 , 還有貧窮、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	而居住在一個土地無法支撐的地區 , 太貧窮了 , 無法購買食物 , 無法搬離 , 因為整片土地都被分解了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以 , 沙漠化繁衍、令人毛骨悚然、令人毛骨悚然 , 如同最後一棵樹被砍伐一樣 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	而這種東西不只在非洲 , 在世界各地
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇見了許多年輕人 , 他們似乎失去了希望 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為在這種極端聰明的大腦中 , 會不會有某種不一致的區別 ? 那種被ted科技所展現出來的大腦 , 和人類的心臟 ? 用非科學的術語來說 , 用愛和同情的角度來談 , 是否有些不一致 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	而這些年輕人 , 當我跟他們談話時 , 基本上他們是憂鬱的 , 或冷淡的 , 或苦痛和生氣的 。 他們說的或多或少是一樣的: 「 我們有這種感覺 , 因為我們覺得你已經妥協了我們的未來 , 而我們卻無能為力 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥協了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子孫女 , 每一次我看著他們 , 我就會想我們如何在自從我還是他們的年紀就傷害到這個美麗的星球 , 我就感到這個絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這就導致了這個計畫 , 我們稱之為根與芽 , 它從坦尚尼亞這裡開始 , 現在已經擴散到全世界97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它具有象徵意義 。 根源製造一個堅定的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	芽看起來很微小 ; 為了要抵達太陽 , 它們可以穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆視為地球上所有的這些問題 , 環境和社交 。 這是希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	全世界有成千上萬的年輕人可以突破 , 可以為所有生物創造出更好的世界 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽的最重要的訊息:我們每一個人都會做出改變 , 每一天都一樣 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在座的每一位 , 我們都有選擇要做出什麼樣的不同 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	窮人沒有選擇 。 要靠我們去改變事情 , 才能讓窮人有選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽的團體全都選擇三個項目 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們年齡多大 , 以及哪個國家 , 不論他們在哪個城市或鄉村 , 都要看什麼樣的計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在有從幼兒園到大學的方案 , 有越來越多的成人開始他們自己的根部和槍擊團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	而每一個團體都選擇 , 在它們之間 , 三種不同的計畫 , 來讓這個世界更美好 , 認識到 , 所有這些不同的問題都是互相關聯的 , 並互相衝突的 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以 , 他們的一個計畫將是幫助他們自己的人類社群 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	接著 , 如果他們能 , 他們可能會募集資金來協助世界上其他地方的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	他們的其中一個計畫是幫助動物不僅僅是野生動物 , 還有家用動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	他們的計畫之一就是幫助我們共同的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	在這一切中 , 編織出的訊息是:學習生活在和平與和諧中 , 在我們自己、在我們的家庭、在我們的社區中、在國家之間、文化之間、宗教之間、在我們和自然世界之間 。
