and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 。 國家老化研究院實際上給了我們一個問卷 , 給這些百歲人瑞 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題 , 他們在文化上很常見 , 那些把問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上醒來
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對這位102歲的老婦人來說 , 她的ikigai只是她的曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩在十一歲時分離 , 分隔了半年 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 拿著一個曾曾孫女的感覺是怎樣的 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把頭放回去 , 說: 「 感覺就像跳上天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我以為那是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理雜誌的編輯希望我能找到美國的藍寶地 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子 , 我們看了明尼蘇達的金字塔 , 那裡有非常高的百歲人瑞 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們又轉向數據 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現美國有史以來最長的人口是七天的進口者 , 集中在加州的羅馬林達市附近 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	先驅者是保守的方法論者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們在星期五晚上從日落到日落來慶祝他們的安息日 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	一個 " 24小時避難所 " , 他們稱之為
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五個小習慣 , 來傳達給他們非凡的長壽 , 相對來說 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 一般女性的平均壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一個冒險的女人來說 , 他們的預期壽命是89歲 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	男性之間的差異更加明顯 , 他們預期比美國人多活大約11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	現在 , 這個研究追蹤了約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	嚴格研究 。 而且我認為它非常能說明這個藍色區塊計畫的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個異型社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	是白人、黑人、西班牙人、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共同點就是一組非常小的生活習慣 , 他們大半輩子都依循儀式式式的人生 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	直接從聖經上拿取他們的飲食 ,
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	gensis:第一章 , 上帝說過29 , 在那裡 , 上帝會談到樂高和種子 , 再來談談綠色植物 , 看似少了肉 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們認真看待這個避難所 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週有24小時 , 不論他們多忙 , 工作壓力有多大 , 孩子們需要被驅使 , 他們停止一切 , 專注在他們的上帝、他們的社交網路 , 然後 , 在宗教裡 , 大自然都是走路 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這種力量並不是說它是偶爾完成的 , 力量是每週一次都在進行一生 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	一點都不難 。 都不花錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	冒險家也傾向與其他的冒險家共存 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去看一位冒險家的派對 , 你不會看到有人在搖晃jimbeam , 或是滾動一個關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	取而代之的是他們在談論他們的下一個自然步行 , 交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們以很深刻且能測量的方式影響彼此 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化讓艾爾斯•沃爾斯•哈雷姆有所共識 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	埃爾斯•沃雷瑟姆九十七歲 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是千萬富翁 , 但當一個包商想要六千美金來打造隱私柵欄時 , 他說: 「 為了那種錢 , 我會自己做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以接下來的三天 , 他出去擠壓水泥 , 到處跑 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可以預測 , 也許 , 在第四天 , 他最後進到手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是像桌子上的那個人 , 而是開心手術的那個人 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	九十七歲時 , 他每個月仍然做二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•羅林斯 , 103歲 , 一個活躍的牛仔 , 開始游泳的早晨 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末 , 他喜歡貼在板子上 , 丟出羅斯特的尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在這裡的雙胞胎城市 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她從每天舉起重量開始 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎著腳踏車
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她穿上了牠的rootbeer的顏色 , 1994年的凱迪拉克塞維爾 , 在聖柏納迪諾高速公路上流下淚 , 在那裡 , 她仍然是七個不同的組織志工 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我曾參加過19次艱難的探險 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我大概是你會遇到的唯一一個人 , 他騎腳踏車穿過撒哈拉沙漠 , 沒有防曬霜 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴各位 , 沒有任何冒險比騎著margedeton的登山更具傷害性 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 一個陌生人是我還沒見面的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說:
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	那麼 , 在這三個文化中 , 共有的是什麼 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們都在做些什麼呢 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功的把它歸為9 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 自從這裡以來 , 我們已經完成了兩次藍寶地探險 , 這些共同點是真的 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我現在要說的是 , 這裡沒有一個是運動練習 , 至少我們認為運動是這樣 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	取而代之的是 , 他們設立了自己的人生 , 這樣他們才能不斷地被推入身體活動中 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的琉球婦女正在起身離開地面 , 她們坐在地板上 , 每天30到40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 上下樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每趟旅行到店裡 , 或去教堂 , 或去朋友家裡偶爾會走路 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何方便性 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有按鈕來推動做院子工作或房子工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想把蛋糕混在一起 , 他們就用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	燃燒的卡路里和跑步機一樣多 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做有意願的實體活動時 , 這是他們所享受的 。 他們傾向於走路 , 唯一被證實的辦法是擺脫認知衰退 , 他們都傾向於擁有一個花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何用正確的方式來設定他們的生活 , 這樣他們才有正確的觀點 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都需要時間去往下移 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 。 第七天的冒險家祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	琉球人有這種祖先的移情 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你很快或很有壓力時 , 會觸發一種叫做 「 發炎反應 」 的東西 , 和所有東西都有關 , 從阿茲海默症到心血管疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你每天慢下來15分鐘 , 就會把那個發炎狀態轉變成更反炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	牠們有詞彙 , 可以用來感知目的 , 像是琉球人 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你一生中最危險的兩年是你出生的那一年 , 是因為嬰兒死亡率 , 以及你退休的那一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們人生的目的感 , 並且活躍起來 , 這價值約七年的額外壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反的 , 這些人每天都喝一點點 , 不是很難賣給美國人口 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們傾向於以植物為主的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不代表他們不吃肉 , 而是大量豆類和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略不讓它們過度食用 , 有些小事會在適當的時間把它們推離桌子 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	這一切的基礎是它們如何連結在一起 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人放在第一 , 照顧他們的孩子和老年父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們全都屬於一個信仰型的社區 , 這個社區值四到十四年的預期壽命 , 如果你一個月做四次 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	這裡最大的是 , 他們也屬於正確的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是生來就要不就是主動把自己和對的人圍在一起 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從弗林漢研究中得知 , 如果你三個最好的朋友都過胖 , 就會有50%的機會讓你過重 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人在一起 , 這會隨時間產生很明顯的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反地 , 如果你朋友的 「 休閒 」 理念是身體活動、保齡球、打曲棍球、騎自行車或園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝了一點點 , 但也不多 , 他們吃得對 , 他們很投入 , 信任和可信 , 這會隨時間產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食是行不通的 。 世界歷史上沒有任何飲食對超過百分之二的人口都行得通 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計畫通常從一月開始 ; 通常是十月份完成 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	談到長壽 , 只能用藥丸或其他東西來修復 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你仔細想想 , 你的朋友是長期冒險 , 因此 , 或許是最顯著的事 , 你能在生命中加入更多年 , 並且生活在你這幾年 。 非常謝謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水會產生電力 ; 一扇窗戶會從開關的清晰轉變成不透明的開關 ; 一種讓音樂存在的果凍 。 所有這些東西都存在 , 加大莫特說:是時候該玩了 。 莫塔帶領我們一趟驚喜和酷炫的新材料之旅 , 並建議我們找出他們擅長的辦法 , 就是去實驗、調整、讓它有樂趣 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技、
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:玩弄智慧型材料
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有個在葡萄牙的朋友 , 他的祖父用腳踏車和洗衣機建造了一台車 , 讓他可以運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他買不起車子 , 也因為他知道如何建造一輛車 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾經有一段時間 , 我們了解事物如何運作 , 以及它們是如何被製造出來的 , 這樣我們就可以建造、修復它們 , 或者最少針對該買什麼的做法來做資訊的決策 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	許多這些做法都在二十世紀的後半葉消失了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造者社群和開放原始碼模型正把這種知識帶回我們的生活中 , 我相信我們需要把它們帶到下一個階段 , 到組成的元件 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的情況下 , 我們仍然知道像紙張和紡織品等傳統材料是由什麼構成的 , 以及它們是如何被製造出來的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些令人驚奇、美好的複合材料 , 能改變形狀 , 能導電的油漆 , 能改變顏色的顏料 , 能發光的織物 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電墨水讓我們可以畫電路而不是用傳統印刷電路或電線
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我舉的這個小例子中 , 我們用它來創造一個觸控感應器 , 藉由打開這個小燈 , 來對我的皮膚做出反應 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	導電油墨已經被藝術家使用了 , 但最近的開發顯示 , 我們很快就能在雷射印表機和筆上使用 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這張圖是用無顏色的光散射粒子所注入的晶狀物 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然一般的丙烯酸鹽只會散射光線 , 繞著邊緣的光線 , 這會照亮整個表面 , 當我打開周圍的燈時 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這材料的兩項已知應用包括室內設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	而熱變色素會在特定溫度下改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以 , 我要把這個放在一個熱板上 , 溫度比環境稍高一點 , 你可以看到會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以 , 這種材料的其中一項原則是 , 在嬰兒奶瓶裡 , 其它東西 , 在嬰兒奶瓶裡 , 它就表示 , 當內容物夠涼時 , 可以飲用 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是眾所皆知的智慧型材料中的一些 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年內 , 它們會成為我們每天使用的許多物品和技術 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有科幻小說裡的飛天車承諾過我們 , 但是我們有可以根據溫度改變顏色的牆壁 , 可以捲起來的鍵盤 , 窗戶會變得不透明 , 在開關的一閃而已 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	所以 , 我是社會科學家 , 所以 , 為什麼我今天在這裡談智慧型材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事物如何運作 , 以及它們如何被製造 , 也因為我相信我們應該要對構成我們世界的元件有更深的了解 , 而現在 , 我們對於這些高科技的複合物 , 我們的未來將不夠了解 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧型材料很難在小量中取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何資訊可以用在如何使用它們上 , 很少有人說它們是如何被製造出來的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 他們大多存在於這個貿易秘密和專利領域中 , 只有大學和企業才能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	三年前 , 克莉絲蒂男孩和我開始了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為開放材料 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是個網站 , 我們和其他想要加入我們的人 , 分享實驗 , 發表資訊 , 鼓勵其他人隨時都能貢獻 , 並且集合資源 , 例如像我們這樣的創作者 , 和其他造物者的研究論文和課程 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能成為一個大型、集體的資料庫 , 以智慧型材料為基礎提供多元性資訊 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但我們為什麼要在乎智慧型材料是如何運作的 , 以及它們是由什麼組成的 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造我們不了解的東西 , 而我們不了解和使用的東西 , 最後會塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們用的物品、我們穿的衣服、我們住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有著深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們生活在一個由智慧型材料構成的世界 , 我們應該要知道並了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新一直都是由tinker所推動的 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	許多次 , 業餘演員 , 不是專家 , 已經是發明家和改進者 , 從登山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學是複雜的 , 且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但事實並非總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學有兩個科學家了解這一點 , 當他們用更簡單的方法發表了一篇論文 , 來製造導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbunker , 他對化學一無所知 , 直到那時 , 他才讀到這篇論文 , 在他的自造者空間中 , 只用現成的物質和工具來進行實驗 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱 , 甚至製作了自己的背心混合器 , 根據的是另一位科學家的課輔 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	喬丹接著在網路上發表了他的成果 , 包括他試過的所有東西 , 沒有用 , 讓其他人可以研究並繁衍後代 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以 , 約旦的創新主要形式是把一個實驗在一個備用的大學實驗室裡進行 , 並在芝加哥的車庫中重現它 , 只使用便宜的材料和工具 , 他自己製作的 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這個作品 , 其他人可以拿起他離開的地方 , 想出更簡單的流程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個例子我想提一下她的計畫的目標是強調材料的表達特質同時專注於建造者的創造力和技能
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子裝置非常強大 , 能教導我們事物的運作 , 但設計的限制會影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	所以漢娜的做法是 , 另一方面 , 就是建立一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 , 讓我們免於預先設計的限制 , 來教導我們材料本身 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	在漢娜的許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的一個 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙上面有一些銅膠帶連接著一個mp3播放器和一個磁鐵
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	所以根據麻省理工學院的marcelocoelho的研究 , 漢娜創造了一系列的紙喇叭 , 從簡單的銅膠帶 , 到導電布和墨水 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和其他許多製造者一樣 , 漢娜發表了她的食譜 , 讓任何人可以複製、繁殖它們 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子產品是材料科學中最有前景的分支之一 , 讓我們能創造出更便宜又有彈性的電子產品 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜的手工藝作品 , 以及她分享她的發現的事實 , 打開了一連串新的可能性 , 兩者都具有審美性和創新性 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 製造者有趣的地方在於 , 我們用熱情和好奇心來創造 , 我們不怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常會從不規則的角度來解決問題 , 在過程中 , 最後會發現替代方案 , 或甚至更好的方式來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 越多人用材料做實驗 , 越多研究者願意分享他們的研究 , 製造者他們的知識 , 我們就越有機會創造出真正為我們服務的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	所以我覺得有點像泰德.尼爾森在1970年代早期 , 他寫道: 「 你現在一定要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	那時 , 電腦是這些大型主機 , 只有科學家在乎 , 甚至沒有人在家中有一台 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以 , 這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你現在一定要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 取得關於新興科技的先驅知識是最好的方式 , 來確保我們對未來有發言權 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入一個玻璃泡 , 鎖上門 , 按下加速器 , 仰賴眼睛來指導我們 , 即使我們只能看到前方和後方的車輛 。 但如果汽車能彼此分享他們的位置和速度 , 以及可預測的模型 , 來計算路上每個人最安全的路線 ? 珍妮佛•霍耶想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	jenniferhealey:如果汽車可以說話 , 意外可能是可以避免的 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	讓我們面對現實:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡去思考的事情之一 , 但事實上 , 宗教圖像和好運氣charm出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 其實我們知道這是真的 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是導致16至19歲人死亡的主因在美國導致死亡的主因而且百分之七十五的意外與毒品或酒精無關
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能肯定地說 , 但我記得我的第一個意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我是高速公路上的年輕駕駛員 , 前面的車子 , 我看到煞車燈亮了起來 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這傢伙慢下來了 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩煞車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙並沒有慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這個人在高速公路上停下來 , 死了 , 死了 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	當時只剩65到0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我踩煞車 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感受到了abs的踢進去 , 車子還在轉 , 它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 空氣袋部署 , 車子全都完工了 , 幸好 , 沒有人會受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全沒想到那輛車停了下來 , 我想我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我想 , 我們可以改變駕駛經驗 , 做法是讓我們的車子彼此交談 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只是想讓你們稍微想一下開車的經驗是怎樣的 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	進入你的車內 , 關上門 。 你在一個玻璃泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法真正直接感受到周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡 ,
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是將它導航到一部份的路上 , 在其他的金屬巨人之中 , 以超人的速度運行 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 而你只需要指導你是你的兩隻眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好吧 , 這就是你所有的眼睛不是為了這個任務而設計的 , 但是人們會要求你做這樣的事 , 像是 , 你想做一個轉換 , 他們最先要你做的事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路上拿下來 。 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	停止尋找你要去的方向 , 轉彎 , 檢查你的盲點 , 然後開車下車 , 不去看你要去的方向 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是安全的駕駛方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須要做選擇 , 我要看這裡 , 還是要看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做一份很棒的工作 , 選擇我們在路上要做的事 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們會懷念某些東西 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會感覺到不對或太晚的東西 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外中 , 司機說: 「 我沒看到它來了 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信這點 。 我相信這點 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看這麼多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現在科技的存在可以幫助我們改善這一點 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 有了汽車彼此交換資料 , 我們將不只能看到前面三輛車 , 後面三輛車 , 左邊也是 , 同時 , 鳥瞰視野 , 我們將能夠看見那些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能看到前面車輛的速度 , 看看他走得多快或多快 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那傢伙下降到零 , 我會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	透過計算和演算法和預測模型 , 我們將能夠看到未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能認為那是不可能的
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	實際上 , 沒有 。 有了汽車 , 並不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	汽車是三維的物體有固定的位置和速度
they travel down roads .	他們在路上旅行 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會在預先出版的路上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要合理地預測車子在不久的將來的位置 , 並不難 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使 , 當你在你的車上 , 還有摩托車騎士來了 ! 時速85英哩 , 車道配件--我知道你有過這種經驗--那個傢伙沒有 「 無處可去 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那傢伙在路上大概已經半小時了 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人見過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10、20、30哩前 , 有人看過那個人 , 一旦有一輛車看到那個人 , 把他放在地圖上 , 他就在地圖上的位置 , 速度 , 好的估計他會以每小時85英哩的速度持續下去 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為其他車會在他耳邊輕描淡寫一些東西 , 比如說: 「 順便說一下 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士 , 小心 ! 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以合理的預測汽車的行為 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 他們是牛頓的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	那對他們是很棒的 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何達到目的 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的東西開始 , 分享我們車子間的位置資料 , 只是分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我車裡有一台gps和一台攝影機 , 我有一個很精確的點子 , 知道我在哪裡 , 走得多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我就可以估計我身邊的車子在哪裡 , 有點像是 , 及它們要往哪裡去 。
and same with the other cars .	其他的車也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以很精確地知道自己在哪裡 , 並且有點模糊地知道其他車子在哪裡 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩部車共享這些數據 , 如果它們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你 , 會發生什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊做了電腦模擬當fuzy估計結合時會發生什麼事即使是輕型交通工具 , 當車子共用gps數據 , 我們也將這項研究從電腦模擬中移到機器人測試床上 , 現在在這些機器人上有實際的感應器:s音響攝影機、gps , 和二度雷射雷射 , 都在備用系統中很常見 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們還會附著一個短距離的短距離溝通收音機 , 機器人彼此交談 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人互相靠近時 , 它們會精確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 它們就能避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在在混搭中加入越來越多機器人 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題 , 當你拿到太多的聊天器時 , 很難處理所有的封包 , 所以你必須優先處理 , 而這就是預測模型幫助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車都在追蹤被預測的軌跡 , 你不會去注意那些包裝 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	優先考慮一個人 , 看似有點偏離目標 。
that guy could be a problem .	那個人可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	而且可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他出去了 , 你知道怎麼做 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而你知道你需要警示哪些駕駛才能出去 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想怎麼警告每一個人 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車子怎麼會竊竊私語: 「 你得出路 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 這取決於兩件事:一 , 汽車的能力 , 第二 , 駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人有一輛很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上 , 或者 , 你知道的 , 做點什麼 , 他們不可能會在緊急情況下做出最好的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以 , 我們開始了不同的研究線 , 做駕駛者州立模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 用一系列的三台攝影機 , 我們可以偵測到駕駛正在往前看 , 往下看 , 在電話上 , 或者喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外事故 , 我們可以預測誰 , 哪一輛車在最好的位置 , 可以走出去計算每個人最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術今天的存在 ,
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨的最大問題是我們自己願意分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我覺得這是一個令人不安的概念 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 跟其他車子談話 , 我們會在八卦的海面上下下下下下下下道 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信 , 它可以用一種方式來保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在 , 當我從外面看你的車 , 我其實並不清楚你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看你的車牌號碼 , 我其實不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	而我認為這將會是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	請各位稍微考慮一下 , 如果你不想要讓你後面那個分心的青少年知道你在煞車 , 你來到死胡同的站點 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	藉由有意願的分享我們的資料 , 我們可以為每個人做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車子八卦一下你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	會讓道路安全許多 ,
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize的創辦人peterdiamandis談到他是如何協助史蒂芬霍金實現太空的夢想藉由一起飛入上層大氣層 , 體驗到零g的無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、簡短的演講、空間、科技、宇宙、宇宙、
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	peterdiamandis在零gro的stephenhawkings上
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	認識我的人 , 知道我有多熱衷於打開太空邊境 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給予世界重力專家重力體驗無重力的體驗時 , 真是不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴你們那個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他透過基因組學的archonxprize
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所舉辦的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 讓第一支隊伍在十天內完成100個人類基因組的定序 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有所謂的 " 基因體 " -100個我們排序為其中的一部分
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特爾斯那事件的主席
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇到了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是要進入太空 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你去那裡 , 但我可以帶你進入無重力進入無重力 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說 , 在那個點上 , 「 絕對是 , 是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 要在地球上體驗zerog的唯一方法 , 其實是用拋物線飛行 , 無重力飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你搭飛機 , 飛越頂端 , 重達25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	再下來 , 你的體重是兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你一而再 , 再而三地
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到8、10分鐘的無重力 , 美國太空總署如何訓練他們的太空人這麼久 。
we set out to do this .	我們開始著手做這件事 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	並宣布我們要讓史蒂芬•霍金飛行 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一間政府機關 , 一家公司的飛機操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 不要這樣做 , 你就會殺了那個人 。
and he wanted to go .	而他想去
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力取得所有許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們舉辦了一場媒體大會 , 我們宣佈我們的目的是要做一場無重力拋物線拋物 , 給他25秒的zerog 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果一切順利的話 , 我們可能會做三個拋物面鏡 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	嗯 , 我們問他 , 為什麼他要上去做這件事 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	他所說的 , 對我來說 , 非常感動 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命正冒著越來越多的風險 , 被災難所消滅......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為 , 如果不進入太空 , 人類就沒有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	因此我想要鼓勵公眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們帶他到甘迺迪太空中心 , 在太空總署內部 , 進入zerog飛機的後面 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們約有20個人捐款我們募集了150 , 000美元捐款給那些與我們一起飛行的兒童慈善團體
a few tedsters here .	這裡的幾位tedsters
we set up a whole er .	我們設置了一整個er 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診室醫生和兩位護士登上飛機 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監測他的血液、心跳、血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	萬一緊急情況發生 , 天知道 , 你不想傷到這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭登陸設施起飛 , 太空梭在那裡起飛 , 降落地面 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	而我和我的夥伴byronlichtenberg , 小心地把他吊成zerog 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他在那裡 , 我們就讓他去體驗無重力真正的樣子 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在那首拋物線飛機結束後 , 你知道 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他在微笑 , 我們說去吧 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線飛行器 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們實際上是向艾薩克•牛頓爵士致敬 , 因為霍金教授在牛頓的劍橋有相同的椅子 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四個 , 第五個和第六個 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	和第七個和第八個 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	而這個男人看起來不像一個65歲的輪椅男子 。
he was so happy .	他好高興 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們生活在珍貴的珠寶上 , 在我們有生之年 , 我們正在離開這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請在這個史詩般的冒險中加入我們 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫師davidbolinsky提出了3分鐘令人震驚的動畫 , 顯示在一個細胞內繁忙的生命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫學、科學、科技、視覺化、視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky動畫一個細胞
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插畫家 , 我來自一個稍微不同的觀點 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	自從我長大以來 , 我一直在看真與美的表情 , 呈現在藝術、真與美中 , 在科學裡 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這兩者都是自己權利的美好事物 , 但他們都擁有非常美好的事物 , 可以將真與美視為理想 , 可以被科學和數學看待 , 就像是理想的結合雙胞胎 , 科學家會想要約會的雙胞胎 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些表達真相是令人敬畏的事物 , 意即 , 它們是你能崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是強而有力的理想 。 它們是不可思議的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 。 它們有時是有用的 , 通常是之後很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在可以把其中一些照片滾出來 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看著我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真與美是對不在科學界的人來說常常不透明的事物 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是用來描述美麗的事物 , 通常只有在你了解這個主題的語言和語法時才會使用 , 才能夠理解這個主題中的真與美 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看宇宙常數 , 那裡有人類的理想 , 你看到生命必須從描述宇宙的數字中演化出來 , 這些都是非常難以理解的事物 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我被訓練成醫學插畫家之後 , 我就試著做的事 , 是我父親教的動畫 , 他是一位雕塑家和我的視覺導師 , 我想找出一種方法 , 幫助人們了解生物科學中的真與美 , 藉由動畫、使用圖片、說故事 , 讓那些不見得是明顯的事物 , 能夠被教導 , 並且能被理解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生 , 常常會沉浸在一個環境中 , 在那裡 , 他們所學到的 , 是有真與美的主題 , 但他們被教導的方式是相互連結的 , 被拉到事實和美的境界 , 其實並不總是證據 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	幾乎就像是雞湯的舊食譜 , 把雞煮沸了 , 直到香味消失 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對我們的學生這麼做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們才有機會真正開放教育
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	幾年前 , 我接到哈佛大學的robertlue打來的電話 。 他問我 , 我和我的團隊是否有興趣 , 願意改變哈佛大學的醫學與科學教育的研究方式 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以 , 我們開始進行一個專案計畫 , 探討細胞能夠探索分子和細胞生物學中與生俱來的真與美 , 讓學生能更了解這些事實 , 把這些事實都掛在上面 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可以把細胞的心智圖像當作一個大型的 , 非常複雜的城市 , 被微機所佔據 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微機械真的是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 是世界各地的羨慕 , 它們是自我導向、強大、精確、精確、精確的裝置 , 它們是用胺基酸的弦所組成的 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	而這些微機械能強化細胞移動的方式 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們能供電一個細胞如何複製 。 它們能供給我們的心臟 。
they power our minds .	它們能驅動我們的心靈 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以我們想做的是 , 要想出如何把這個故事變成一種動畫 , 它會是哈佛的生物顧問的中心 , 它是一個哈佛大學的網站 , 用來研究它的分子和細胞生物學學生 , 除了所有文字訊息以外 , 除了視覺上把所有東西放在一起以外 , 讓這些學生對於細胞真正的真與美 , 能夠用這個觀點 , 讓他們的想像力能夠被運用 , 讓他們的想像力能夠被激發出來 , 讓他們的想像力能被運用 , 讓他們的腦海裡充滿熱情 , 讓他們的腦海裡能被發揮 , 讓他們的腦中充滿熱情 , 讓它們能被發揮 , 使得以發揮他們的腦海中新生命 , 以發揮 , 以發揮他們的想像力 , 以發揮 , 以發揮 , 讓它們的熱誠實現它們的力量 , 讓它們能夠發揮他們的腦中 , 使得以發揮他們的腦中充滿熱誠實現它們的力量 , 讓它們能夠發揮他們的腦海 , 使得以發揮他們的腦中充滿熱誠實現它們的力量 , 讓它們能夠發揮它們
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	我們開始研究這些分子是如何組合在一起的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們與一個主題合作 , 即 , 巨噬細胞在微血管中流動 , 它們在微血管壁表面接觸 , 它們從毛細管壁上的細胞中取得資訊 , 它們會被傳送到外面 , 外面有發炎症狀 , 無法看見和感知 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但它們得到了導致它們停止的資訊 , 導致它們內化它們需要製造出各式各樣的部件 , 讓它們能夠改變形狀 , 試著脫離這個微血管 , 找出到底發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須和哈佛的科學家及數據bank模型合作 , 原子上精確的分子 , 找出它們是如何移動的 , 找出它們做了什麼 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	想出如何實現這一點 , 讓它實現了當時的狀況 , 但不這麼說實話 , 細胞中的 「 緊密擁擠 」 會阻止視覺發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	所以 , 我要給你們看的是一個三分鐘的讀者消化版本 , 是我們製作的這部電影的第一面 。 這是一個持續進行的計劃 , 將會再往後四、五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	請各位看看這個 , 看到細胞製造這些小行走機的路徑 , 它們叫做運動員 , 將這些巨大的負荷 , 以相對尺寸來挑戰螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	請看電影 , 請看 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些能驅動細胞內部的機器真的很神奇 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器彼此間的互動 。
they pass information to each other .	他們會互相傳遞訊息給彼此 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們造成細胞內不同的事情發生 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造果蠅所需要的部位 , 從讀取基因的分子所取得的資訊中 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有任何生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每個人 , 若沒有這些小微機械 , 就有可能實現 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , 它的出席率真的很高 , 克里斯 , 真的很矛盾 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的fedex遞送小伙子 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙被稱為 「 腎上腺素 」 , 他把一個裝滿全新的製造蛋白質的袋子拉到細胞所需的任何地方 , 不論是用到細胞膜 , 不論是用到器官 , 不論是用來建造東西或修復東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人大約有十萬個這種東西在你一百兆個細胞內運作 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你有多懶惰 , 你其實什麼都不做 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 我希望你們回家時 , 能想想這一點 , 想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	並且思考一些我們在細胞機械學中學到的東西 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們弄清楚所有發生在我身上的事 , 相信我 , 我們幾乎知道一旦我們弄清楚到底發生了什麼事 , 我們就真的能夠對我們健康的所作所為有很大的掌控 , 帶著未來的世代 , 及我們將要活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用這個來發現更多的真相 , 和更多的美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但 , 這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 實在是非常驚人 , 它們能察覺到它們所需要的細胞 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	他們同心協力 , 讓細胞做該做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們一起努力 , 幫助我們的身體龐大的實體 , 使他們永遠看不到正常的功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受其他的節目 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪•布朗頓計畫要在她的旅行車裡住一年 , 見到這個國家 , 但當憂鬱症患者和她的自由工作結束時 , 她的露營旅程變成無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述了她經歷的經歷 , 成為美國工作無家可歸的無家者 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會變遷、社會、說故事、說故事、生活、個人成長、貧窮、貧窮、社會變革、社會變革、社會變革
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝琪•布蘭頓:我那一年是無家可歸的無家者 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是作家也是記者 , 我也是一個極度好奇的人 , 所以 , 身為記者的22年 , 我學到了如何做很多新事 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到了一件事 , 就是變成隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為了工作無家可歸者之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭掉了我父親同年二月去世後的報紙編輯的工作 , 決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死因讓我很辛苦 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	在我這麼做的時候 , 有很多我想要感受和處理的事情 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一輩子都在露營 。 我決定住在旅行車裡一年 , 這樣做會是一趟漫長的露營旅程 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我把我的貓、我的腐敗者、我的露營裝備都裝到1975年的雪佛蘭小貨車上 , 開到日落 , 完全沒有意識到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會等於是生活在一個永久的結構中 , 甚至是一台購物機 , 以人為本的價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	二:我沒有意識到別人的負面看法能多快影響我們的現實 , 如果我們讓它發生的話 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我沒有意識到無家可歸是一種態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在旅行車裡很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地洗澡 , 定期吃完飯
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但 , 接著 , 我父親死後的憤怒和沮喪出現了 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 。 我得要全職工作來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	溫和的春天已經變成了一個非常炎熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	在任何地方 , 都不可能停車 , 沒有很明顯我有一隻貓和一隻狗 , 真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓來了 , 穿越廂型車的開窗 ,
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗狗進入了日常照護 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我能時 , 我就用在辦公大樓的員工淋浴間 , 以及卡車站 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或是我在公共休息室清洗
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間在廂型車內的溫度很少下降到華氏80度以下 , 讓它難以入眠 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱裡腐爛 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	我胸部冰層的冰層在幾個小時內融化 , 而且還蠻悲慘的 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我買不起公寓 , 或是負擔不起一間公寓 , 讓我可以擁有rotweiler和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我待在廂型車裡 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱氣使我暈船走向公共廁所時 , 晚上我用桶和垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	冬天天氣剛開始的時候 , 溫度下降到凍結處 。 然後他們就待在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	而我面臨了一系列新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都停在不同的地點 , 以避免被警察察察察覺及發現 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功的 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感覺到 , 無法掌控我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道是何時、如何發生的 , 但是我從一個有才華的作家和記者 , 變成了無家可歸的婦女 , 住在旅行車裡 , 把我的呼吸帶走了 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有改變 , 我的智商沒有下降 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的天份、正直、價值觀 , 關於我的一切 , 都仍然是一樣的 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我有某種程度上改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我旋轉得越來越深 , 變成憂鬱症 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	終於有人提到我去了無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	然後我就去了 。 我三天沒洗澡了 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和排隊中的任何人一樣 , 都很臭、很沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒有喝醉或高醉 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當幾個無家可歸的男人意識到 , 包括一個前任大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸的人 。 你為什麼會來這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人沒有把我視為無家可歸 , 但我真的做到了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著 , 教授傾聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家可歸者沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給予我的憂鬱症讓我有自殺傾向的反應 。 我記得當時在想: 「 如果我殺了自己 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	一個朋友告訴我 , 在那之後不久 , 她聽說提姆•羅斯瑟特 , 他是一位全國知名記者 , 他在全國電視台上一直在談論我 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫過一篇關於我父親的論文 , 在他去世前的那一年 , 是在提姆的新書裡 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他正在做這場演說電路 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到提姆•羅斯瑟特 , 《迎接媒體》的前任主持人 , 是在談論我的寫作 , 當時我住在一輛在沃爾瑪停車場的貨車上 , 我開始大笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑 , 是因為它到達了我是作家 , 還是無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	於是我進了書店 , 找到了提姆的書
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 重新讀我的論文 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家 。
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後不久 , 我搬回田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友一起住在休旅車和沙發上 。
and i started writing again .	我又開始寫作 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	隔年夏天 , 我擔任記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我在贏得獎項 。 我住在我自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	而我不再隱形 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人全職工作 , 同時住在他們的車裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續汙名化和犯罪化生活在你的車輛或街道上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家可歸者 , 工作無家可歸者 , 主要是看不見 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇到一個人 , 讓他們投入 , 鼓勵他們 , 並給他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服任何事情 , 如果它有希望的話 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡當無家可歸的海報女生 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來鼓勵你們把錢給你遇到的下一個乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡是要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人不是他們住的地方、睡覺的地方 , 或他們在任何時候的人生狀況 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在一台廂型車裡 , 位在沃爾瑪的停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是 , 總是找到一個方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , 泰國的 「 保險套先生 」 , mechaiviravaidya , 帶我們走過國家的大膽計畫 , 來提升它的壽命標準 , 從1970年代開始 。 第一步:人口控制 。 意思是許多法蘭克、好笑且非常有效的談論保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、科學、
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	美西維拉瓦迪亞:保險套先生如何讓泰國成為更好的地方 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	現在 , 當我還是個40年前的年輕人時 , 這個國家非常非常貧窮 , 有許多人生活在貧窮之中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要做點什麼 , 但我們沒有從福利計畫開始 , 或減少貧窮計畫開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從家庭解釋計劃開始 , 遵循一個非常成功的母子健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	所以基本上 , 如果他們的孩子沒有生存 , 沒有人會接受家庭計劃 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:向孩子們 , 向母親們求助 , 然後跟著家庭計劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不僅僅是孩童死亡率 , 你還需要有家庭規劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回到為什麼我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的案例 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭有7個小孩成長率達3.3% 。
there was just no future .	根本沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 我們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	婦女們說: 「 我們同意 。 我們會用藥丸 , 但我們需要一個醫生來開處方藥 。 」 而我們有非常非常少的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有採取答案 ; 我們不採取答案 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去找護士和助產士 , 他們也是女性 , 做了一個很棒的工作 , 解釋如何使用藥丸 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那很棒 , 但它只佔了該國的20% 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們為其它80%的人做什麼 , 讓他們獨自一人說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去了你看到的普通人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	其實 , 在下面那個黃色的標誌我希望他們還沒有消失 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	我們當時的可口可樂大得多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選擇的對象是我們所選擇的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中很著名 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們很棒 , 他們自己實踐了家庭規劃 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以在全國各地供應藥丸和保險套 , 在全國各個村莊 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們就是這樣 。 我們去找那些被視為問題的成因的人 , 來成為解決方案 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論在哪裡 , 這裡有人 , 你都可以和女性一起看船 , 賣東西是漂浮市場 , 賣香蕉和螃蟹 , 還有避孕用品 , 不論你在哪裡找到人 , 在泰國都會找到避孕用品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	接著 , 我們決定 , 何不去宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教會很強烈 , 泰國人都是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 看 , 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我在那裡是藍色的 , 不是黃色的 , 拿著一碗聖水 , 讓僧侶把聖水灑在藥片和保險套上 , 以便讓家人神聖 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	而這張照片傳遍全國 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	所以有些村莊的僧侶自己也在做同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	女人說: 「 難怪我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	已經有福氣了 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的認知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們去找老師 。
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每個人都能參與 , 試著提供任何讓人類更美好的地方 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去找老師 。
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過25萬人被教導要用新的字母a、b、c來保險套、iud、v來做血液切除術 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	然後我們有了蛇和梯子遊戲 , 在那裡你丟骰子 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你在任何事務所的規劃上降落 , 你就往前走 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	像是: 「 媽媽們每天晚上吃藥 。
very good , mother . move ahead .	非常好 , 母親 , 來吧 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買了保險套 。 非常好 , 叔叔 , 往前走 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	叔叔喝醉了 , 不用保險套 。 回來 , 再開始 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	同樣的 , 教育、階級娛樂
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子們也在學校裡做 。
we had relay races with condoms , we had children's condomblowing championship .	我們和保險套有了相關的種族 , 我們有孩子的保險套冠軍 。
and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久之前 , 保險套被稱為女孩最好的朋友 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮人來說 , 鑽石不會讓保險套成為女孩的最佳朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年推出我們的第一個微型貸款方案 , 組織起來的那些婦女說: 「 我們只想向實踐家庭規劃的婦女貸款 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧你的懷孕
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你沒有懷孕 , 你可以從我們那裡拿出貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	而這是由他們來執行的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	經過35/36年後 , 仍然持續進行著 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 ; 它不是真正的銀行 , 但它是基金的小額貸款 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個大型組織來執行它 , 由村民自己來執行 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能幾乎看不到一個泰國人 , 總是有女人、女人、女人、女人 。
and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	接著 , 我們認為我們會協助美國 , 因為美國一直在協助所有人 , 不論他們是否想要協助他們 。
and this is on the fourth of july .	而這是在七月四日 。
we decided to provide vasectomy to all men , but in particular , american men to the front of the queue , right up to the ambassador's residence during his [unclear] .	我們決定為所有男人提供輸精管切除術 , 但尤其是美國男性 , 在他的[不清楚]期間 , 直到大使 。
and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	飯店給了我們這間房間非常適合的房間 。

of course , it must be american cola .	當然 , 這一定是美國的可樂 。

i said , " don't worry . come over and i'll do the whole lot of you . "	我說: 「 別擔心 , 請過來 , 我會全力以赴 。 」
in all this thing , from seven children to 1 . 5 children , population growth rate of 3 . 3 to 0 . 5 .	在這之中 , 從7個孩子到1.5個孩子 , 人口成長率是3.3到0.5 。
you could call it the cocacola approach if you like it was exactly the same thing .	你可以稱它為可口可樂方法 , 如果你喜歡它完全一樣的話 。
i'm not sure whether cocacola followed us , or we followed cocacola , but we're good friends .	我不確定可口可樂是否跟著我們 , 或是我們跟著可口可樂 , 但我們是好朋友 。
and so that's the case of everyone joining in .	這就是每個人加入的情況 。

then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	接著 , 愛滋病來了 , 來到泰國 , 我們得要停止做很多好事來對抗愛滋病 。

so i thought , " well , if you can't go to the government , go to the military . "	所以我想: 「 嗯 , 如果你不能去政府 , 去軍方 。 」
so i went to the military and asked to borrow 300 radio stations .	所以我去軍方 , 要求借300個電台 。
they have more than the government , and they've got more guns than the government .	他們擁有的比政府多 , 擁有的槍總比政府多 。

because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為窮人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能 , 取得信用 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	那些是要被商業界提供的 。
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著把他們變成赤腳企業家、小商人 。

the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	經由種植經費從公司進入村落 。
it's not a free gift .	這不是免費的禮物 。
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種植樹木 , 金錢進入了他們的小額貸款基金 , 我們稱之為村落發展銀行 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都加入 , 他們覺得自己擁有銀行 , 因為他們把錢帶進去 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	而在你能借到錢之前 , 你需要接受訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信 , 如果你想要幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧窮中的人 , 取得信用的人 , 一定是人權 。

and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	然後在取得貸款之前 , 你一定要受過訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	以下是我們所謂的 「 赤腳mba 」 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 這樣一來 , 當他們借錢時 , 他們就會成功地與企業合作 。

make these better , because we can afford them . "	把這些做得更好 , 因為我們負擔得起 。 」

so anyone sitting in and watching tv , get in touch with me .	所以 , 任何人坐在裡面看電視 , 跟我聯絡 。

and then now , finally in education , we want to change the school as being underutilized into a place where it's a lifelong learning center for everyone .	而現在 , 終於 , 在教育界 , 我們想要把學校改造成被禁止使用 , 成為一個終身學習中心給每個人的地方 。
we call this our schoolbased integrated rural development .	我們稱之為我們的學校為以農村為基礎的發展 。

redo the school , make it serve the community needs .	重新設計學校 , 讓它能為社區需求服務 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧型手機可能覺得像是朋友 , 但真正的朋友會給你微笑一陣子 。 在ted2013年 , 凱勒•里納多•羅莫 , 智慧型手機驅動的迷你機器人 , 能和你一起漫步 , 讓你一杯咖啡橫跨桌子 , 用可程控的表達方式對你做出反應 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinaudo:一個迷你機器人由你的手機掌控 ,
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	舉個手 , 有多少人家裡都有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	不少人 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好的 。 實際上這些手 , 如果你不包括roomba--有多少人在家裡有機器人 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這就是我們在romotive嘗試解決的問題 , 我和其他20位羅斯特國的書呆子 , 都很著迷於解決問題 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的很想打造一個機器人 , 任何人都可以用 , 不管你是八歲還是八十歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這真的是個困難的問題 , 因為你得要建造一個小型、可攜帶的機器人 , 它不僅真的負擔得起 , 它還得要是人們真的想要帶回家 , 圍繞著孩子 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人不能令人毛骨悚然或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該是友善且可愛的 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo是一個用你已經知道的裝置來使用的機器人 , 並將你的iphone視為他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	藉由iphone處理器的力量 , 我們就能創造出一台無線網路、電腦視覺化的機器人 , 只要150美元 , 這大約是這類機器人在過去的成本的1% 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo醒來時 , 他在生物模式中
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他其實是在用儀器上的錄影機跟著我的臉 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我倒下來 , 他會跟著我 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很警惕 , 所以他會把目光留在我身上 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我來到這裡 , 他就會轉身跟著我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我來到這裡 , 他很聰明 ,
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他就會像其他生物一樣害怕 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	所以 , 從很多方面來看 , romo就像一隻有自己心智的寵物 。
