you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	你可以想像一個八歲的小女孩 , 例如 , 誰有iphone , 她的媽媽買了個機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿她的iphone , 把它放在機器人上 , 發送一封電子郵件給祖母 , 住在該國另一端的祖母 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	奶奶可以登入那個機器人 , 和她的孫女玩捉迷藏遊戲 , 每晚十五分鐘 , 否則她一年只能看到她的孫女一到兩次 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	這些是romo今天能做的一些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我只想藉由談談未來我們正在努力的一件事來結束我的演講 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這其實是我們其中一個工程師 , dom , 在一個週末就建造出來的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在google的開放架構上 , 叫做blockly 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這讓你可以拖曳、丟下這些分號碼的積木 , 為你想要的這個機器人創造任何行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何寫程式 , 才能為romo創造出一種行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	而且你真的可以在瀏覽器中模擬那個行為 , 就是你在左邊看到romo在做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以把它下載到你的機器人上 , 在現實生活中執行 , 在現實生活中執行這個程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	然後如果你有你驕傲的事情 , 你可以和世界上所有擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以 , 所有這些無線網路的機器人實際上是互相學習的 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以如此專注於建造機器人 , 讓每個人都能訓練 , 是因為我們認為 , 在個人機器人中 , 最引人注目的使用案例是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	它們會從人變為人 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以 , 我們認為 , 如果你要在你家裡有個機器人 , 那機器人應該是你自己的想像力的呈現 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以我希望我能告訴你個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子的 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我完全不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們確實知道的是 , 它不是10年或100億美金 , 或大型的人型人形機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來就如今發生 , 它會依賴小型、敏捷的機器人 , 如romo之類的 , 以及像你自己這樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以我們迫不及待想讓你們全部的機器人 , 我們迫不及待想看看你們蓋什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和積極分子伊莎貝爾•阿言德討論女性、創意、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 還有這場演說中的熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂 , 全球議題 , 愛 , 養育 , 說故事 , 女人 , 世界文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•阿言德訴說著熱情的故事 。
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝 。 非常可怕 , 能來到最聰明的人當中 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我來這裡是要告訴你們一些熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有一個猶太人說我很喜歡 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	什麼比真相更真實 ? 答案是:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是說故事的人 , 我想傳達的比我們共同的人性更真實的東西 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都對我感興趣 , 有些在我最後寫下它們之前就一直縈繞在我心頭 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	某些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到我們身邊的奧秘 , 所以我寫下關於巧合、預防、情緒、夢、自然的力量、魔法的力量 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年裡 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但是我一直活在匿名中 , 直到2006年2月 , 當我帶著奧運在義大利冬季奧運時 ,
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成為一個名人 。 現在人們在macy's認得我 , 我的孫子認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	允許我講述我的名氣的四分鐘 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	奧運會典禮的組織者之一 , 開幕典禮 , 打電話給我 , 說我曾經被選為旗幟師之一 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答說 , 這肯定是錯誤身份的案例 , 因為你能從運動員那邊 , 我是最能得到的 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	其實 , 我甚至不確定我可以不用助行器就繞過體育館 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是笑話 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 只有女性會帶著奧運旗幟 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性 , 代表五大洲 , 還有三位奧運金牌贏家 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	一件制服 , 她說 , 請求我的測量結果 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我對自己有個遠景 , 在蓬鬆的氣旋裡 , 看起來像米其林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了二月中期 , 我發現我在杜林 , 在那裡 , 充滿熱情的群眾歡呼 , 當時有八十名奧運隊在街上 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了在遊戲中競爭的一切 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都應得勝利 , 但有運氣的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一小塊雪 , 一英吋的冰 , 風的力量 , 可以決定比賽或比賽的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 比訓練或運氣更重要的是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心才會得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	這一切都和熱情有關 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	杜林街上被紅色海報覆蓋著 , 宣佈奧運的口號 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情就活在這裡 。 不見得都是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅使我們、決定我們的命運的動力 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	那是我書中的角色所需要的:充滿熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要mavericks , 異議者 , 冒險家 , 外人和叛軍 , 他們會問問題 , 彎曲規則 , 冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人 ,
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	有共通感的好人 , 不會製造有趣的人物 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只會做好前夫 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育館的綠色房間中 , 我遇到了其他旗幟熊:三位運動員 , 女演員蘇珊•沙龍和蘇菲雅•羅蘭 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	還有 , 兩個充滿熱情的女性:旺加里•馬塔伊 , 來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎者 , 曾種過三千萬棵樹 。 藉由這麼做 , 她改變了土壤、天氣 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然也改變了許多村莊的經濟狀況 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	還有柬埔寨社會運動家 , 他熱切地對抗兒童妓女 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她十四歲時 , 她祖父把她賣給妓院 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男人強暴 , 她們相信和很小的處女做愛會把她們從愛滋病中治癒 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	至於兒童被迫每天接收五、十五個客戶 , 如果他們反叛 , 他們會被電擊折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在我收到的綠色房間裡 ,
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我平常穿的那種衣服 , 但它離米其林人的衣服很遠 , 我預期的不好 , 真的 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但 , 除了蘇菲雅羅蘭 , 大部分的旗幟也是如此 , 普遍的美麗和熱情的象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅已經超過70歲了 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感 , 很瘦 , 身高很高 , 有著深色的針筒 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	現在 , 要怎麼做才能有深色皮膚 , 沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當在一個電視訪問中問到: 「 她怎麼能看得這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 。 我的背總是直的 , 我不製造老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 這裡有一些免費的建議 , 來自地球上最漂亮的女性之一 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	沒有草 , 沒有咳嗽 , 沒有休息 , 沒有對自己說話 , 沒有遙不可及 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她沒有說的完全是這樣 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在午夜的某個時點 , 我們被召喚到體育館的翅膀 , 大聲說話者宣佈奧運旗 , 順帶一提 , 音樂是從這裡開始 , 艾達遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅蘭就在我面前 , 她比我高一英尺 , 不計尖的頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走著 , 像一隻長頸鹿在非洲大草原上 , 肩上拿著旗幟 。 我在我的背上 , 拿著旗幟在伸展手臂上 , 這樣我的頭就在該死的旗子下面 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有的攝影機都是在蘇菲雅 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	那對我來說是很幸運的 , 因為 , 在大部分的媒體照片中 , 我也會出現 , 雖然通常在蘇菲雅的雙腿之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個大部分男人都樂意去的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的四分鐘是奧運體育館裡的人 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我先生很冒犯 , 說到這點 , 雖然我向他解釋 , 我們私人的做法通常只花不到四分鐘 , 所以他不應該親自承受 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有這四個壯麗的分鐘數的差別 , 因為我不想忘記它們 , 因為當年紀破壞了我的腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想永遠帶著奧運熱情的關鍵字 。
so here's a tale of passion .	以下是熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	今年是1998年 , 那個地方是剛果圖西難民營的監獄營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順道一提 , 世界上80%的難民和流離失所的人都是女性和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以把這個地方叫做剛果一個死亡營 , 因為那些沒有被殺的人 , 會死於疾病或餓死 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕的女子 , 蘿絲.馬德羅 , 也是她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕和寡婦
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵們強迫她看著她的丈夫被虐待和殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼地 , 她能讓七個孩子活下去 , 幾個月後 , 她生下了產前的雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子剪斷臍帶 , 用自己頭髮將它和它連結在一起 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她用營地的指揮官命名為雙胞胎 , 以獲得他們的協助 , 用黑茶餵飽他們 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持他們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵闖進她的牢房來強暴她最大的女兒時 , 她會抓住她 , 拒絕放下 , 即使當他們拿著槍抵著她的頭 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 家庭存活了16個月 , 之後 , 靠著非凡的運氣 , 以及一位年輕美國人的熱情心 , 薩夏•查諾夫 , 他想辦法把她安置在美國救援飛機上 , 羅斯•馬丁和她的九個孩子最後到亞利桑那州鳳凰城 , 在那裡他們現在居住、成長茁壯 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	斯瓦希里語中 , mapendo代表著偉大的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書中的主角是堅強且熱情的女性 , 如羅絲•馬迪諾 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不把它們做成 , 不需要這樣 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處可見 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都在和女性一起工作 。
i know them well .	我很清楚他們 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在遠古時代 , 在世界末日 , 在父權天主教和保守的家庭中 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪 , 到五歲時 , 我是個憤怒的女權主義者 , 雖然這個詞還沒達到智利 , 所以沒人知道我到底出了什麼問題 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 要為我的自由付出很高的代價 , 為了質疑父權制度 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能付出代價 , 因為每次我拿到的炸彈 , 我都能遞兩張 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我的女兒寶拉在二十多歲時 , 她對我說女權主義是約會約會 , 我應該繼續下去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有一場難忘的戰鬥 , 女權主義是約會 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於有特權的女性 , 像我女兒 , 也是今天在座的各位 , 但不是為了世界上其他大部分的姐妹 , 她們仍然被迫成為早產的婚姻、妓女 , 被強迫到她們有不想要的孩子 , 或無法養活的孩子 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法控制自己的身體或生活 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 也沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、毆打 , 有時被處死 , 有時還被處死 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	對於現今大部分西方年輕的女性來說 , 被稱為女權主義者是種侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權主義從來沒有性感過 , 但讓我向各位保證 , 它從來沒有阻止我調情 , 而我已經因為缺乏男性而受苦 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女權主義沒有死 , 絕非如此 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經演化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個名詞 , 改變它 , 改變它 , 為女神的sake 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱之為 「 phrodite 」 、 「 金星 」 、 「 bimbo 」 , 或 「 不論你想要什麼 」 ; 這個名字無所謂 , 只要我們了解它的內容 , 我們就支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這裡還有另一個充滿熱情的故事 , 這是很可悲的一個 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	那個地方是孟加拉的一個小型婦女診所 。
the year is 2005 .	2005年 ,
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙齒衛生學家 , 她在三週假期時去診所當義工 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備了乾淨的牙齒 , 但當她到達時 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是一間滿是蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	在外面 , 有一行女性等了好幾個小時才被治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一個病人在疼痛之中 , 因為她有好幾個腐爛的臼齒 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮意識到 , 唯一的解決方案就是拔掉壞牙 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有執照 , 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她冒了很多險 , 她嚇壞了 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有合適的樂器 , 但幸運的是 , 她已經帶來了一些諾娃卡因 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有著勇敢且充滿熱情的心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她拍了一段禱告 , 帶著手術前進 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 病人親吻她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天衛生專家拉出更多的牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	第二天早上 , 當她再來到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一名病人正在和她老公一起等待她 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	女人的臉看起來像個西瓜 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	它是如此的腫脹 , 你甚至看不到眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫 , 憤怒 , 威脅要殺死美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮對她所做的事感到害怕 , 但接著翻譯解釋 , 病人的狀況和手術無關 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她的丈夫打她 , 因為她不在家 , 不時為他準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	今天有數百萬的女性像這樣生活著 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是窮人中最窮的人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然女性會做世界上三分之二的勞動卻擁有不到世界資產的百分之一
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水比男性的薪水還少 , 只要他們有薪水 , 他們就會保持脆弱 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 且他們會不斷受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	給予女性教育、工作、控制自己的收入、繼承和產權的能力 , 讓社會受惠 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦予能力 , 她的孩子和家人就會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭繁榮 , 村落的繁榮 , 最終整個國家也是如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	旺加里•馬塔伊到肯亞的一個村莊
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和婦女們談話 , 解釋說 , 土地是貧瘠的 , 因為他們已經砍伐、賣掉了樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女們種植新的樹木 , 澆到他們身上 , 滴下來 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在五、六年內 , 他們有一片森林 , 土壤豐富 , 村落就拯救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮和最落後的社會 , 總是那些把女性放下來的人 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	然而這個顯而易見的事實卻被政府和慈善事業所忽略 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	給予女性計畫的每一塊錢 , 給男性計畫二十塊美金 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性是51%的人類 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	賦權他們改變一切 , 勝過科技、設計和娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向你們保證 , 女性們攜手合作 , 連結、知情、受教育 , 能為這星球帶來和平和繁榮 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在今天的任何一場戰爭中 , 大部分的傷亡都是平民百姓 , 主要是婦女和兒童 。 他們是相對的傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人跑遍世界 , 看看我們遇到的亂象 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大多數人都在問的基本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	是否合理地參與現有的世界秩序 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個被保存下來的世界 , 生活品質也被豐富每個人 , 不僅僅是為了特權 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	一月份我看到了費南多.波特羅在加州大學柏克萊圖書館的畫展 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	美國沒有博物館或畫廊 , 除了紐約的畫廊以外 , 都敢於把畫作展示出來 , 因為主題是阿布格萊布監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	它們是巨大的折磨和濫用權力的畫作 , 以極大的波特羅風格 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我沒有辦法把那些影像從我的腦海中或我的心中
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的是有罪惡感的力量 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 以及濫用權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們這個物種中 , 雄性領袖定義現實 , 並強迫其餘的群體接受現實 , 並遵循規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則隨時都在改變 , 但它們總是有好處 , 在這個例子中 , 下面是三角函數的效應 , 在經濟上行不通 , 完美地工作 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	虐待騙局從梯子的上到下面 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	婦女和兒童 , 尤其是窮人 , 處於底層 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即便是最多男人也有人可以虐待一個女人或一個小孩
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我是以少數人透過性別、收入、種族、階級的手段 , 來支撐這些權力 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 時間是成熟 , 要在我們的文明中做出根本的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但 , 對於真正的改變 , 我們需要女性化的能源 , 在世界的管理上 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要一個關鍵的女性在權力的位置 , 我們需要培育男性內含的女性能量 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我指的是有年輕心智的男人 , 當然 ,
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老人是沒有希望的 ; 我們必須等待他們死去 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很想有蘇菲雅羅蘭的長腿和傳說性胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 若要做選擇 , 我寧可有來自華加里•馬塔伊的勇士心臟 , 索瑪莉、瑪麗、珍妮 , 和羅絲•瑪迪諾 。
i want to make this world good .	我想讓這個世界變得很好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是要把它做得很好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不呢 ? 這是有可能的 。 看看這個房間裡的周圍 , 所有的知識、能源、才華和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	讓我們脫離炫耀 , 捲起袖子 , 熱情地工作 , 創造一個近乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦一個城市大小的城市裡 , 有三千萬份餐是服務的 。 但所有的食物都來自哪裡 ? 建築師卡羅琳鋼鐵討論餵養一座城市的日常奇蹟 , 並展現出古老食物路線如何塑造了現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡羅琳•史黛爾:食物如何形塑我們的城市
how do you feed a city ?	如何養活一個城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代最偉大的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但卻很少被問到 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們理所當然地認為如果我們去一家商店或餐廳 , 或在大概一小時內進入這間劇院的倉庫 , 那裡將會有食物等著我們 , 神奇地從某處來 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但 , 當你認為 , 每一天 , 倫敦大小的城市 , 都要有足夠的食物來生產、運送、買、吃、吃、丟 , 每天都要發生同樣的事 , 對於地球上的每個城市而言 , 都很了不起的是 , 城市會被餵養 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在這樣的地方 , 彷彿牠們是世界上最自然的東西 , 忘了那是因為我們是動物 , 需要吃東西 , 其實我們和我們古老的祖先一樣依賴自然界 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	當更多人搬到城市裡時 , 更多的自然世界正被轉變為非凡的景觀 , 就像我身後的那一塊大豆田 , 是巴西馬托格羅索的大豆田 , 為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是非凡的景觀 , 但很少人能看到它們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	越來越多的這些景觀也不只是餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著更多人搬到城市裡 , 更多人吃肉 , 所以 , 全球三分之一的年度穀物會被餵食給動物 , 而不是給人類動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	由於它需要三倍的穀物事實上是10倍的穀物來餵飽人類如果它是先經過動物 , 那就不是非常有效率的方式來餵飽我們
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個持續不斷的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到2050年 , 估計我們居住城市的數量將會是城市的兩倍 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	據估計 , 肉類和乳類的消耗量將會是兩倍 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以 , 肉類和都市化手工興起 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	那會造成很大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	到2050年 , 要餵飽六十億隻餓食肉動物 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 如果我們繼續這樣下去 , 我們就不太可能解決問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有一千九百萬公頃的雨林被丟棄 , 以創造新的可耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然我們同時也失去了等量既有的可耕性 , 以鹽化和侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也很渴望石化燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	大約需要10卡路里來產生我們西方所消耗的每一卡路里食物 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管我們有大量生產的食物 , 但我們卻不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國目前生產的食物有一半是丟棄的 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	為了結束這一切 , 在這個漫長過程的盡頭 , 我們甚至沒有適當的管理來餵飽這個星球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	我們有十億人過胖 , 卻有十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	一點都不合理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為現在全球百分之八十的糧食交易是由五個跨國企業所控制 , 這是很嚴峻的照片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	隨著我們搬進城市 , 世界也擁抱西方的飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	而如果我們看向未來 , 這是一種無法永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	所以 , 我們是怎麼走到這一步的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 要回答這個問題稍微簡單一點 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 是這個過程在古老的近東地區 , 也就是所謂的 「 肥沃日新月沃 」 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是近代的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	它也很肥沃 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約在一萬年前 , 這裡有兩項非凡的發明 , 農業和城市化 , 大約在同一個地方 , 同時發生 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是意外 , 因為農業和城市是互相限制的 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們古老祖先第一次發現的穀物 , 產生了足夠大且穩定的食物來源 , 足以支撐永久定居處 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些定居處的狀況 , 我們就會看到它們是緊縮的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被有生產力的農田圍繞著 , 被大型神廟複雜的土地支配著 , 像這個在烏爾的大型神殿 , 事實上 , 是靈性化的中央食物分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為是神殿安排收割 , 聚集在穀物裡 , 提供給諸神 , 然後提供神所不吃的穀物給人民 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你願意 , 這些城市的精神和實體生活都是由穀物和收成所支配的 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古城都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是全部都那麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	著名的是 , 羅馬在西元前一個世紀 , 大約有一百萬名公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市是如何自給自足的 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案就是我所謂的 「 古代食物哩程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬能接觸到大海 , 這使得它從很遠的地方進口食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是在古代世界中唯一可能做到這一點的方法 , 因為要運送食物很困難 , 要運送食物在路上 , 路面很粗糙 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物很快就被吃掉了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以羅馬有效地發動了戰爭 , 戰爭發生在如汽車和埃及這些地方 , 只為了讓它的爪子放在穀物的保護區上 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 帝國的擴張真的是一場長期的軍事化的購物中心 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提一下:羅馬其實曾經是從倫敦進口牡蠣 , 在一個階段 。 我認為那很特別 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬透過它的食慾塑造了它的後塵 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 另一件事也發生在工業化前的世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看十七世紀的倫敦地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 從泰晤士河的底部 , 沿著這張地圖的下方 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場就到市區的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	道路從它們引領到便宜 , 那是主要的市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	看看其中一條街道的名字 , 麵包街 , 可以分辨300年前的狀況 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	魚也是一樣的 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也是由河流進來的 。 同樣的道理 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , billingsgate , 著名的是倫敦的魚市場 , 直到1980年代中期 , 在這兒操作 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	想想看 , 這真的很不尋常 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他所有人都帶著像磚塊一樣的手機遊走 , 有點像是在港口上聞到魚的味道 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是關於城市裡食物的另一件事:一旦它的根源被建立起來 , 它們很少會移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類是非常不同的 , 因為 , 當然 , 動物可以走進這個城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦的大部分肉都來自西北 , 來自蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它就要來了 , 抵達西北部的城市 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦非常著名的肉市場 , 位在那邊 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	從東安格里亞來到東北部 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得這有點像天氣女人這樣做 。 總之 , 鳥兒們進來用腳保護著小畫布的腳 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	然後當他們碰到便宜的東端時 , 那是他們被賣掉的地方 , 這也是為什麼它被稱為 「 家禽 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看一下任何一個城市的地圖 , 在工業時代之前 , 你可以追溯到食物的來源 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何被食物所塑造 , 兩者都透過閱讀街道的名字 , 這給了你許多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在一個前世 , 是你星期五去買魚的地方 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但同時你也要想像它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共場所是唯一一個被食物買賣的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年史密斯菲爾德的圖像 , 可以看出 , 生活在這樣的城市 , 很難過 , 不知你的食物是從哪裡來的 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你吃了星期日午餐 , 你的窗外有機會 , 大約三天前就在你的窗戶外面開心或出血 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	顯然這是個有機城市 , 是有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	然後十年後一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年大西方國家的影像
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 一些最早的火車乘客是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	所以突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 ,
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被視力和心靈屠殺 , 在鄉下的某個地方 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們通過欄杆進入城市 。
and this changes everything .	而這會改變一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 它讓城市能夠生長 , 在任何地方 , 任何大小和形狀都能實現 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	以前 , 城市會受到地理限制 ; 以前 , 城市得要透過非常困難的實體手段來取得它們的食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間它們被有效地從地理上解放了 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	如你所見 , 從倫敦的這些地圖 , 在火車來臨的90年後 , 從一個小小的光團 , 很容易被動物們帶進來 , 以此類推 , 到一個大型的液體 , 很難和任何人搭配 , 不論是動物 , 或人 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然這只是個開端 。 火車來了車之後 , 真的是這個過程的結尾 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	它是整個城市最後的解放 , 從任何與自然的明顯關係中得到的 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	而這就是那種沒有味道的城市 , 沒有亂七八糟 , 肯定沒有人 , 因為沒有人會夢想走在這樣的地景中 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們的做法是 , 他們在車上拿到食物 , 開車到外面的某個箱子 , 回來了一週的購物 , 想著 , 地球上要怎麼用它 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	這才是真正的時刻 , 我們的關係 , 和食物和城市的關係 , 完全改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡我們有過去的食物是中心 , 城市的社會核心在邊緣地帶 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	曾經是社交活動 , 購買和賣食物
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前會煮飯 ; 現在我們只會加水 , 或是做蛋糕或其他東西 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物看是不是可以吃
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只讀包裝上標籤的背面 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	而我們不珍視食物 , 不信任它
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是去評價它 , 而是把它丟掉 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食品系統的一個很諷刺的一點是 , 他們已經做出了他們承諾要更加困難的事 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	透過讓它能夠在任何地方和任何地方建立城市 , 它們已經讓我們遠離我們最重要的關係 , 那就是我們和大自然的關係 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	此外 , 它們讓我們依賴的是只有它們能傳遞的系統 , 如我們所見 , 是不可持續的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那我們該怎麼做呢 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前 , 湯瑪斯更多在問自己 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他書 " 烏托邦 " 的前身
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	它是一系列半獨立的城市 , 如果那聽起來很遙遠 , 一天的步行 , 每個人基本上都在耕種 , 在他們的後園裡種植蔬菜 , 吃了共產餐 , 諸如此類 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想 , 你可以主張 , 食物是烏托邦的基本原則 , 即使它從來沒有這樣框架過 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這是另一個非常有名的 「 烏托邦 」 遠景 , 艾貝茲霍華德 , 《花園城市》 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一系列半獨立的城市 , 小型的大都市 , 隨處可見 , 加入鐵路 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	再說一次 , 食物可以被說是他願景的訂定原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建造出來了 , 但與默斯克韋茲的遠景無關 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這個問題就是烏托邦的想法 , 他們是烏托邦人 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是托馬斯.摩爾刻意使用的一個字 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	那是個笑話 , 因為希臘有雙重衍生 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它要不就是一個好的位置 , 要不就是一個位置 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為這是一個理想的 。 這是個想像不到的東西 。 我們不能擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念 , 用來思考人類居住的深層問題 , 讓它不太有用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 就是希托邦 , 來自古希臘 , 「 西托 」 供應食物 , 和 「 湯波 」 供應給位置 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在西索比亞了 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個被食物形塑的世界 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們可以用食物來當作一種強大的工具 , 一種概念化的工具 , 設計工具 , 以不同的方式塑造世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以 , 如果我們要這麼做 , 西索比亞可能會變成什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	嗯 , 我想這看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我得用這張投影片 。 這只是狗的臉上的表情 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	但無論如何 , 這是食物在生活的中心 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌、被享受 , 人們花時間為它著想 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這是我們社會中食物應該要的所在地 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但你不能有這樣的場景 , 除非你有這樣的人 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順便說一下 , 這些也可以是男人 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	而是人們對食物的看法 , 前方的看法 , 誰能計劃 , 誰能盯著一堆原生蔬菜 , 並且能真正認出它們 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 , 我們是網絡的一部分
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為若沒有這類人 , 我們就不能有這樣的場合 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	我故意選這個 , 因為它是買蔬菜的男人 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但是網絡 , 讓食物在當地生長的市場
it's common . it's fresh .	很常見 , 很新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	是城市社會生活的一部分 。
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為 , 若沒有這些 , 你就不能有這種地方 , 當地的食物也能成長 , 成為地景的一部分 , 且不只是零和的商品 , 還能在不見的地獄中出現 。
cows with a view .	用景象觀看牛 。
steaming piles of humus .	蒸蒸汽堆的嗡嗡聲 。
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上就是把整件事集合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多參觀的一個社區計畫 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是一間溫室 , 那裡的孩子們對食物和種植自己的食物都說了一遍 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有一株叫凱文的植物 , 或者它是屬於一個叫凱文的孩子 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	但無論如何 , 這類企圖將我們與大自然重新連結的項目是極為重要的 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 對我來說 , 西索比亞真的是一種觀看的方式 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上 , 意識到 , 西索比亞已經存在於各處的小口袋裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	訣竅是要加入他們 , 用食物當作看待的方式 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們將會停止將城市看成是大都市 , 大都市 , 沒有生產力的blob , 就像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會把它們看得更像這樣 , 視為是有生產力、有機體架構的一部分 , 它們是無可避免的一部分 , 共生性連結在一起 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	但當然 , 這也不是很棒的畫面 , 因為我們不需要再這樣生產食物了 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要更多的思考永續經營 , 這也是為什麼我認為這張圖片可以總結出我們需要做的那種思維 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	將食物形塑我們生活的方式重新概念化 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道的最好的圖像 , 是從650年前
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	是安布羅吉歐•羅倫澤蒂的 「 好政府的寓言 」 。
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	關於城市和鄉村之間的關係
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這個訊息非常清楚 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧這個國家 , 國家會照顧這個城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我現在要我們問 , 如果他今天畫出這張影像 , 阿姆布羅吉歐•羅倫澤蒂畫的是什麼 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天好的政府會變成什麼樣子 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個迫切的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	它是我們必須要問的 , 我們得要開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們吃的東西
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要意識到 , 世界也是我們所吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採用這個想法 , 我們可以用食物來當作強大的工具 , 來塑造更好的世界 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	幾週後 , 來自慈悲發起的憲章 , karenarmstrong看著宗教在21世紀所扮演的角色:它的教條會分裂我們嗎 ? 還是它會讓我們團結一致嗎 ? 她會重新審視促使世界的信仰 , 來重新發現黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝、ted大獎、全球議題、政治、宗教、tedglobal-2009年、暴力、
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:讓我們重新審視黃金法則吧 !
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我一直覺得很沮喪 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我很敏銳地意識到 , 在所有主要世界的信仰中 , 同情心的中心 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個都已經演化出他們自己的 " 黃金法則 " 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時它會帶著正面的版本 「 永遠只會把其他人對待 , 就像你想要對待自己一樣 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面的版本 「 別對其他人做你不希望他們對你做的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的心臟 , 發現它帶給你痛苦的是什麼 , 然後在任何情況下拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 在任何情況下 , 在任何其他人身上都能感受到痛苦 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	而人們強調了同情心的重要性不只是因為它聽起來很好 , 而是因為它有用 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施了 " 道德規則 " 如同孔子所說的 " 一整天與每天 " , 不僅僅是 " 做善事 " 的問題 , 然後回到貪婪與自我主義的生命中 , 每天都要實現 , 你將自己從世界的中心中偷走 , 把另一個放在那裡 , 超越你自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它會把你帶到被稱為 「 神 」 、 「 神 」 、 「 神 」 、 「 神 」 、 「 神 」 、 「 神 」 、 「 泰 」
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越了我們自大的存在 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來都不知道 , 這對宗教生活來說是很重要的 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有幾個很棒的例外 , 當宗教人士聚集在一起時 , 宗教領袖會聚集在一起 , 他們爭論的是關於不安的教義 , 或說出一個充滿憎恨的理事會 , 或是反對同性戀或其他類似的說法 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們並不真的想要有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到 , 當我對宗教人士說話時 , 一種相互意見的表情 , 穿過他們的臉孔 , 因為人們通常會想對他們說話 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	那當然會打敗運動的物體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	我為什麼對ted這麼感激 ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們溫和地帶領我從我的書線研究帶領我進入21世紀 , 讓我能和更廣的觀眾對話 , 比我想像中的還要廣 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我對此感到急迫 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們無法在全球實施黃金法則 , 以便我們對待所有人 , 不論他們在哪裡 , 不論他們在哪裡 , 就好像他們和我們自己一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們將會有一個可行的世界 , 可以將這個世代交給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 我們這個時代的一個偉大任務 , 就是建立一個全球性的社會 , 如我所說的 , 在那裡 , 人們可以在和平中共同生活 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該做出重大貢獻的宗教 , 反而被視為問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然不只是宗教人士相信黃金法則
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的源頭 , 這種富有同理心的想像力 , 把自己放在另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以 , 我們有選擇 , 對我來說 ,
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以繼續帶出或強調我們信仰的教條和寬容的面向 , 或者我們也可以回到拉比希爾 。 大的耶穌當代 , 當他要求他把整個猶太教義都歸納在一條腿上時 , 他說: 「 這對你來說很討厭 , 不要對你的鄰居做事 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	那是托拉 , 其他的都只是評論而已 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	而教堂的拉比人和早期的父親 , 他們說任何對教義的詮釋 , 培養出憎恨和不利的教義是不合法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	而我們需要復興這種精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	而這不只會發生 , 因為愛情的精神讓我們失望 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須讓這一切成真 , 我們可以用ted所引進的現代溝通來實現 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對我們所有伴侶的反應感到極度的振奮 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一群人 , 要用這個圖表來治癒近期的分裂 , 在新加坡社會 , 議會中的一些成員都想要在政治上實施 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將來會有一場藝術展覽 , 領先藝術家將要帶領人們 , 年輕人 , 並向他們展示 , 同情心也屬於所有藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 穆斯林社區正在舉辦活動和討論 , 正在討論伊斯蘭和所有信仰中的慈悲中心 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能停在那兒 。 它不能隨著發射而停止 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教學 , 這是我們出錯的地方 , 單純集中在相信荒誕的教義上 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教誨一定會導致行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	我打算在我死去的那天工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	而我想要繼續和我們的夥伴一起做兩件事 , 教育和刺激同情心的思考 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育是因為我們已經脫離了同情心
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常常認為這只是對某人感到抱歉 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但你當然不會懂得同情心 , 只要你只是想一想 ,
you also have to do it .	你也得去做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望他們能參與媒體 , 因為媒體非常關鍵 , 要協助破除一些刻板印象 , 我們對其他人的看法 , 把我們從彼此之間分開 。
the same applies to educators .	教育家也一樣 。
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望年輕人能感受到一種充滿同情心的生活方式的動力和挑戰 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時也看到 , 它需要敏銳的智慧 , 而不只是一種美好的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想請求學者 , 來探索他們自己以及他人傳統中的同情心主題 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	最重要的是 , 若要鼓勵對不友善的發言權的敏感度 , 這麼一來 , 由於人們有這種特質 , 不論他們的信念 , 或缺乏他們的信念 , 他們都覺得有能力去挑戰不友善的言論 , 來自於他們的宗教領袖、他們的政治領袖 , 來自工業部隊的領袖 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來沒有想過要把圖表放上網 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我還困在舊世界裡 , 一大堆小販坐在一間房間裡 , 說出另一句話 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted向我介紹了一種全新的思維和呈現想法的方式 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為這就是ted的精彩之處 。

and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他把這和友情比較 , 當兩個人站在一起 , 就像是肩並肩 , 雙眼固定在共同目標上 。

everything he sees from this point on is slightly affected by the linguine , but keeps on moving because this guy's got a job to do .	他從這時候開始看到的一切都稍微受到語言的影響 , 但繼續前進 , 因為這傢伙有工作要做 。
removes some scaffolding . one of the reasons rome remains the extraordinary place it is that because of scaffolding and the determination to maintain the fabric , it is a city that continues to grow and adapt to the needs of the particular time in which it finds itself , or we find it .	除去一些支架 。 羅馬之所以保持非凡之處在於 , 是因為支架和決心要維護布料 , 它是個持續成長和適應特定時空的城市 , 在特定的時間內它自己會找到它 , 或我們會找到它 。
right through the piazza della rotonda , in front of the pantheon again wreaking havoc and finally getting to work .	穿過皮亞札•德拉•羅頓達 , 在萬神殿前又再次吹噓 , 最後終於能上班了 。
marcello , as it turns out , is the driver of the number 64 bus , and if you've been on the number 64 bus , you know that it's driven with the same kind of exuberance as marcello demonstrated on his scooter .	馬塞羅 , 結果是 , 64號公車的司機 , 如果你坐過64號公車 , 你就知道 , 這和馬塞洛在他的摩托車上展示的一樣讓人興奮 。
and finally carletto . you see his apartment in the upper lefthand corner .	最後是卡爾萊托 。 你看到他在左上角的公寓
he's looking at his table ; he's planning to propose this evening to his girlfriend of 40 years , and he wants it to be perfect .	他在看他的桌子 ; 他打算在今晚向他的女朋友提出這個晚上40年的提案 , 他希望它完美 。
he's got candles out , he's got flowers in the middle and he's trying to figure out where to put the plates and the glasses .	他把蠟燭拿出來 , 中間有花朵 , 試圖找出該把板子和眼鏡放在哪裡 。
but he's not happy ; something's wrong .	但他不快樂 ; 有些事情不對勁 。
the phone rings anyway , he's called to the palazzo .	電話響了 , 他被叫去palazzzo 。
he saunters he saunters at a good clip , but as compared to all the traveling we've just seen , he's sauntering .	他用一個好的短片來抵達 , 但和我們剛剛看到的所有旅行相比 , 他在發出聲音 。
everybody knows carletto , because he's in entertainment , actually ; he's in television .	大家都知道carletto , 因為他在娛樂界 , 實際上 , 他在電視裡 。
he's actually in television repair , which is why people know him .	他其實是在電視修復 , 這就是為什麼大家認識他 。
so they all have his number .	所以他們都有他的號碼 。
he arrives at the palazzo , arrives at the big front door .	他到達了帕拉佐族 , 抵達大前門 。
enters the courtyard and talks to the custodian , who tells him that there's been a disaster in the palazzo ; nobody's tvs are working and there's a big soccer game coming up , and the crowd is getting a little restless and a little nervous .	進入庭院 , 和客戶交談 , 他告訴他 , 帕拉索發生了一場災難 ; 沒有人的電視機在工作 , 有一場大型足球比賽要上來 , 人群都變得有點不安 , 有點緊張 。
he goes down to the basement and starts to check the wiring , and then gradually works his way up to the top of the building , apartment by apartment , checking every television , checking every connection , hoping to find out what this problem is .	他下到地下室 , 開始檢查線路 , 接著 , 漸漸地 , 他走到建築的頂端 , 公寓靠著 , 檢查每一台電視機 , 檢查每一台連結 , 希望能找出問題的所在 。
he works his way up , finally , the grand staircase and then a smaller staircase until he reaches the attic .	最後 , 他開始往上爬 , 到大樓的樓梯 , 再到達閣樓 , 再到達閣樓 。
he opens the window of the attic , of course , and there's a tablecloth wrapped around the building's television antenna .	他打開閣樓的窗戶 , 當然還有一張桌布包裹著大樓的電視天線 。
he removes it , the problems are solved , everybody in the palazzo is happy .	他移除它 , 問題就解決了 , palazzo裡的每一個人都很開心 。
and of course , he also solves his own problem .	當然 , 他也解決了他自己的問題 。
all he has to do now , with a perfect table , is wait for her to arrive .	他現在要做的就是 , 用一個完美的桌子 , 就是等她到達 。
that was the first attempt , but it didn't seem substantial enough to convey whatever it was i wanted to convey about rome .	那是第一次嘗試 , 但似乎不夠實質 , 不足以傳達出我想要傳達羅馬的任何東西 。
so i thought , well , i'll just do piazzas , and i'll get inside and underneath and i'll show these things growing and show why they're shaped the way they are and so on .	所以我想 , 好吧 , 我就去做比薩吧 , 我會進到裡面和下面 , 展示這些東西成長的原因 , 顯示它們是如何塑造它們的樣子 , 以此類推 。
and then i thought , that's too complicated . no , i'll just take my favorite bits and pieces and i'll put them inside the pantheon but keep the scale , so you can see the top of sant'ivo and the pyramid of cestius and the tempietto of bramante all side by side in this amazing space .	接著我想 , 這太複雜了 。 不 , 我只會拿我最喜歡的零件和碎片 , 把它們放在萬神廟內 , 保持尺度 , 所以你可以看到 , 聖誕節的頂端 , 以及克西西斯提烏斯的金字塔 , 和巴拉曼特的泰蒂絲 , 全部在這個驚奇的空間中 。
now that's one drawing , so i thought maybe it's time for piranesi to meet escher .	這是一張繪圖 , 所以我想也許是時候讓皮拉內西見面escher 。
you see that i'm beginning to really lose control here and also hope .	你看我開始在這裡失去控制權 , 也開始失去希望 。
there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	這裡有一條很薄的藍色線條 , 貫穿了這個東西 , 有點像是把所有東西連在一起的路線 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	接著我想: 「 等等 , 我在做什麼 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	一本書不僅是蒐集和儲存資訊的好方法 , 而是一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把一層拆開 , 我們把它們看成是頁面 , 用某種方式做 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但 , 把它們想像成層層 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是一個層層向、層向、垂直的層次 , 和我想 , 只要把頁面剝下來 , 就可以讓我思考一下 , 如果我有辦法正確的思考 , 我可以給你們看一些層次的深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬大部分建築物的牆面覆蓋著疤痕 , 數世紀以來 , 改變的疤痕一直在適應 , 而不是被撕毀 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做一個摺疊頁 , 讓你直接放開它 , 你可以看到它背後的意思是 , 疤痕組織 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到 , 在1635年 , 要做出較小的窗戶是很重要的 , 因為壞蛋要來了 , 等等 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	適應一切都被埋在石頭底下 。
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以把這palazzo的一頁剝出來 , 讓你們看看它的內部狀況 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但更重要的是 , 我還可以給你們看那些壯麗的建築物的角落有著巨大的石塊 , 或用磚頭和stuco做的假石塊 , 比較常是這樣 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它會變得稍微立體 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以帶你走下一條狹窄的小街道 , 進入其中一個令人驚訝的廣場 , 使用雙層摺疊頁--如果你像我一樣 , 讀一本彈出式的書 , 你會希望把你的頭塞進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把頭的頁面都包起來 , 就在那短暫的一段時間內 。
and i've really not done anything much more complicated than make foldout pages .	我真的沒有做過比做摺疊頁更複雜的事 。
but then i thought , maybe i could be simpler here .	但後來我想 , 也許我可以簡單一點 。
let's look at the pantheon and the piazza della rotonda in front of it .	咱們來看看萬神殿和皮亞薩•德拉•羅頓達在它前面 。
here's a book completely wide open .	這裡有一本完全開放的書 。
ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好 , 如果我不把這本書全部打開 , 如果我打開它90度 , 我們就從萬神殿的正面往下看 , 看上方 , 或多或少在正方形上方 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我把這本書翻過來 , 我們就在萬神殿的正面看著正方形 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺疊 , 沒有任何戲法只是一本沒有完全開放的書 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這看起來很有前景 。 我想 , 也許我會在裡面做 , 甚至可以把摺紙作品和唯一一部分開放的書結合起來 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	所以 , 我們進入萬神廟 , 它會成長等等 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我想 , 也許我是站在正確的軌道上 , 但它有點失去了它的人類品質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以 , 我回到故事的概念 , 如果你試圖讓人們注意一本書 , 一路上撿起資訊 , 總是件好事 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進步 」 把我當作捕捉標題 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	假如牠是隻賀鴿 , 牠會被稱為 「 荷馬的奧德修女 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是那趟旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果有標題可用 , 用它 。 但這會是一趟穿越羅馬的旅程 , 展示所有我喜歡羅馬的東西 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	是坐在教堂的上方的鴿子 。
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天放棄 , 做成鴿子的東西 。 回來 , 整個地方被支架和綠色網路包覆著 , 這樣鴿子就可以回家了 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以現在是無家可歸的鴿子 , 還得找另一個地方居住 , 這讓我得以通過我最愛的目錄 , 我們從高處開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許牠得要回去和家人同住 ; 那不一定是好事 , 但牠會再次把鴿子聚在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我想 , 這挺有意思的 , 但也許有個人應該用某種方式來參與 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老人 , 他一輩子都在照顧生病的鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會到任何地方 , 去讓他們處於危險之地 , 而他們會和這個傢伙交朋友 , 學會為他做技倆 , 在午餐時間娛樂他之類的地方 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	在這個老人和這些鴿子之間發展出真實的鍵結 。
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他生病了 。 他在故事結束時真的生病了 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他教導他們拼他的名字 , 也就是aldo 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	他們在三、四天不見到他之後 , 出現了一天 , 他住在這個小小的車庫裡 , 他們拼出他的名字 , 飛來飛去 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於有足夠的力量一起爬上梯子爬到屋頂上 , 所有的鴿子 , la紅氣球 , 都在等著他 , 他們把他帶到城牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到這一點:每當他失去一隻鴿子時 , 他就會把那隻鴿子帶出城牆外 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在古羅馬習俗中 , 死者從未被埋在牆內 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這真是個愉快的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這真的會走得很遠 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	總之 , 我經歷了......再說一次 , 如果包裝沒用了 , 如果故事沒到哪裡去 , 我只會想出標題 , 希望書名能把我推向正確的方向 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時它會把我集中得夠多 , 我甚至會做一個標題頁 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	所以 , 這些都是頭銜的頁面 , 最終引領我解決方案 , 這是一位年輕女子的故事 , 她把信息傳到羅馬城外的鴿子 , 送到城市裡的某個人 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	而鴿子正從這裡飛過 , 飛過appian上空 。
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看到墓碑和松果等等的出現 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看到紅線 , 你會看到鴿子的蹤跡 ; 如果你看不到紅線 , 你就是那隻鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	此時 , 若要傳達飛越整個城市的感覺 , 會是什麼樣的感覺 , 完全不動 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	穿過西斯提烏斯金字塔──這些對你來說似乎很熟悉 , 即使你最近沒去過羅馬 , 遠遠超越大門 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這是有點不尋常的事 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一件事情 , 大部份蜂巢的鴿子不會做的事:它採用了隱形的路線 , 這個裝置是我覺得必要的 , 把這本書延伸到大約四頁左右 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們繞過羅馬競技場 , 穿過聖母堂的教堂 , 穿越哥馬利亞 , 以及海克力士的神殿 , 朝著河流前進 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們與米開朗基羅設計的帕拉佐法蘭基羅公司差不多碰撞 , 石頭是從羅馬競技場面逃出來的 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們俯瞰整個柬埔寨的營地 。
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我向我的學生展示的一件事 , 因為它是完全的基礎化 , 否認任何觀點的規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為觀點的唯一規則是 , 如果它看起來是可信的 , 你就成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著找出消失的點在哪裡 ; 一對夫妻在火星上 , 和其他幾位在克雷蒙納州 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但在位於聖塔馬利亞德拉宮殿前的皮亞莎 , 在那裡 , 一定有一場足球比賽正在進行 , 我們被足球擊中 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	現在這是一個被足球擊中很糟糕的畫面 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的碎片:有聖母瑪麗亞•德拉•步調 , 有足球 , 有一點鳥翅目什麼都沒發生 , 所以我得要重新思考它 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你想要看到聖母瑪利亞•德拉•步調 , 這些書很有彈性 , 很有互動性 , 只要轉過身來 , 用另一種方式來看它 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	透過巷子 , 我們可以看到它在紅線上被捕捉到的影響 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	接著 , 鳥兒想辦法把自己拉過去這個中世紀的塔樓 , 只有少數中世紀的塔樓之一 , 朝聖的中世紀塔樓邁進教堂 , 繞著圓頂往下看 , 望向了亞扎那沃納沃納維納納納納納維納 , 我們已經提過、看到、流過了四條河流的伯尼斯塔雕像 , 接著超越了邊境的borromini大樓 , 停在萬神廟的26英尺長 , 讓萬神廟停下來 , 以捕捉我們的氣流 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	接著 , 我們就可以在內部盤旋 , 因為我們在飛行 , 我們不需要擔心重力 , 在這個特定的時刻 , 所以這幅畫可以用頁面上的任何方式來定位 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們通過gesu時 , 我們會覺得很自在 ; 用這種方式來模仿建築 , 並不讓人意外 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	經過美妙的牆壁 , 充滿了我所說的 「 交叉分類 」 ; 漂亮的列車會在 「 新月 」 的標誌上方 , 以此類推 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最後 , 我們抵達了潘拉索的庭院 , 那是我們的目的地 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入閣樓的小窗口 , 在那裡 , 有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他把訊息從小鳥的腿部移開 ; 這是牠說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看著畫板 , 我們看到他正在努力的 , 事實上 , 是這隻鴿子剛剛拍下的旅程地圖 , 紅線延伸到所有的視野中 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這些資訊 , 這樣我們就完成了這個循環的了解 , 你只需要讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	非常感謝大家 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的研究員天空中的兔子是自行組合的 , 不是建造東西 , 而是創造出一些建構自己的東西 , 很像是dna片段本身 。 這是初期階段的一個大概念 。 兔子向我們展示了三個隱藏自我組合的項目 , 在一個自我組合的未來可能會變成什麼樣子 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	天空的tibbits:我們能做出造就自己的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想向各位展示我們製造東西的方式的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 很快我們的建築物和機器就會自我組合、複製、修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以我要向你們展示我相信的 , 是目前的製造狀態 , 接著 , 和一些自然系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	所以 , 在目前的製造業狀態下 , 我們有摩天大樓 , 兩年半的時間 , 五十萬到一百萬個零件 , 相當複雜、嶄新、令人興奮的技術 , 鋼鐵、混凝土、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人振奮的機器 , 可以帶我們進入太空五年--[組裝時間] , 250萬個零件 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但在另一邊 , 如果你看一下自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 可以在一萬奈秒折疊 , 或dna有三十億個鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一個小時內複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 在我們的自然系統中 , 所有這些複雜性 , 但它們極為有效率 , 遠比我們所能建造的任何東西都更有效率 , 遠比我們所能建造的任何東西都還要複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	它們在能源方面的效率遠遠高於
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎不會犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	而且他們可以長壽修復自己 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 關於自然系統 , 有一種超級有趣的東西 ,
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們能將它轉化為我們所處的環境 , 那就有一些令人振奮的潛力 , 可以讓我們建造東西 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵在於自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想要在我們的物理環境中利用自組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	第一 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的東西的複雜性 , 以便我們的建築和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要將之解碼成簡單的序列基本上就是我們的建築物運作的dna
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編寫的部分 , 可以把序列拿出來 , 用它來折疊 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能讓它活化的能量 , 讓我們的部件能夠從程式中折疊起來 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的錯誤矯正缺陷 , 來保證我們已經成功地建立了我們想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以我要給你們看一些我同事和我在麻省理工學院的計畫 , 正在努力實現這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前兩個是macrobot和decibot 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些項目是大規模可重組的機器人--8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	嵌入機械電器、感應器、
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	把你想要折疊的部分解碼成一連串的角度--那麼負120 , 負120 , 0 , 0 , 0 , 120 , 負120--類似的東西 ; 所以一連串的角度 , 或輪流 , 再把那序列通過了弦 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都取出它的負面訊息-120會轉到那邊 , 檢查它是否到達那裡 , 然後傳遞給鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些是傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師 , 在這個項目上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為這真的能帶來光明:這真的是可擴展的嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 幾千美金 , 許多人的時間都可以製造出這個八英尺高的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的能把這個規模擴大嗎 ? 我們真的能把機器人嵌入每個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題是 , 並且著眼於被動性自然 , 或被動地嘗試重新配置程式設計 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它更進一步 , 試圖進行實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上將電腦運算最基本的積木 , 也就是數位邏輯閘 , 直接嵌入到你的零件中 。
so this is a nand gate .	所以這是nand閘門 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一個四面體 , 就是大門要做你的運算 , 你有兩個輸入的四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中之一是使用者的輸入 , 如同你在建構你的磚塊一樣 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另一種是從以前被放置的磚頭中
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它會給你3d空間中的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	所以這意味著使用者可以開始在他們想要的磚塊中加入 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它會計算它之前的功能 , 以及你說你想要它做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 往上或往下 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以 , 在左手邊 , [1、1]輸入等於0輸出值 , 下降了 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0 , 0]輸入是一個輸出值 , 上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	那真正的意思是 , 我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的東西的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有了所有嵌入其中的信息 , 說明了什麼是建構出來的 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	所以這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個例子中 , 我稱之為自給自足的複製 , 因為你的結構包含了精確的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有誤差 , 可以取代一部分 ,
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有的本地資訊都嵌入其中來告訴你如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以有東西爬上去 , 讀它 , 可以在一對一輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有外界指示 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	所以 , 我將要展示的最後一個專案叫做偏差鏈 , 它可能是目前我們所擁有的最令人興奮的例子 , 被動式自組裝系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以 , 它需要重新配置和可編程 , 讓它成為一個完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	所以基本上你有一連串的元素
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每一個元素都完全相同 , 並且有偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以 , 每一個鏈條 , 或每一個元素 , 都想要左轉或左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈時 , 你基本上就是在編寫它 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你在告訴每個單位是否應該向右轉或向左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖晃鍊子 , 它就會折疊成任何你編程的配置--在這個例子中 , 一個螺旋 , 或者說 , 在這個例子中 , 兩個立方體相鄰 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	基本上你可以編程任何立體的形狀或一維的、二維的 , 完全被動地進入這個連鎖鏈 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們未來什麼 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為 , 它告訴我們 , 自我組裝、複製、修復我們身體結構、建築物、機器的新可能性 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	在這些部分有新的可編程性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	由此可知電腦運算的新可能性
we'll have spatial computing .	我們將有空間計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 我們所有的磚塊都能實際地運算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	那是驚人的平行和分散式運算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以這很讓人興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為我在這裡展示的這些項目只是朝向這個未來邁進的一小步 , 如果我們實行這些新科技 , 為一個新的自組裝世界 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 繪製了大陸的地圖 , 甚至去過海底最深的地方兩次 。 下一代要探究的是什麼 ? 生物學家和探險家nathanwolfe提出了這個答案:幾乎所有東西 。 然後我們就可以開始 , 他說 , 隨著未知世界的小小而開始 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	內森•沃夫:探險還剩下什麼 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我造訪了威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特 ,
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡向一位偉大的20世紀探險家 , roychapmanandrews致敬 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他在美國自然歷史博物館的期間 , 安德魯斯帶領了一系列探險隊去未知的區域 , 就像在戈壁沙漠這裡 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	他後來 , 據說 , 印第安納瓊斯角色的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市時 , 我給一群中學學生做公開演說 。
