you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以是當代主義者 , 也就是你專注於人生的喜悅 , 或是當代主義者──這無所謂 , 你的人生被控制了 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是未來的 , 設定的目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是超然的未來:命名為:生命從死後開始 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展出精神靈活性來轉移時間觀點 , 流暢度取決於情況的需求 , 那是你得學會做的事 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 最佳的時間側寫為何 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度積極 。 高度的未來 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	和現代主義的調和 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低於負面和現狀 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的顳葉混合物是從過去得到的 , 會帶給你的根源 。 你連結你的家人、身分 , 和你的自我 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來得到的 , 是翅膀 , 來翱翔到新的目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在的享樂主義得到的就是能量 , 探索你自己的地方、人、感性 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何時候 , 過多的觀點都比正面來得負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來為了成功犧牲了什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間 。 他們犧牲了朋友時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲樂趣的時光 , 犧牲個人的不屈不撓
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲嗜好 。 然後犧牲睡眠 。 所以這會影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	並且為工作、成就和控制
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我相信 , 和一些ted成員有共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這對我產生了共鳴 。 我是貧窮的孩子 , 在南布朗克斯貧民窟長大 , 西西里亞家庭──所有人都住在過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我是以未來的身份來到頂端的人 , 他們做了所有這些犧牲 , 因為老師介入 , 讓我成為未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你等著你會得到其中兩個 , 直到我學會平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上了現代主義 , 加上了過往的焦點 , 所以 , 在76歲時 , 我比以往更有活力、更有生產力 , 我比以往更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們把這個應用在許多世界的問題上:改變學校兒童的輟學率、結合成癮、增強青少年健康 , 用時間隱喻來治癒受創兒童的創傷後壓力症候群 , 讓奇蹟能促進永續性及保育 , 減少身體康復 , 讓50%的學校恢復率下降 , 改變對自殺式恐怖份子的訴求 , 將家庭衝突視為是 「 時區 」 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我想說的是:許多生命的謎題可以透過了解你的時間和其他人的觀點來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法是如此的簡單 , 如此顯而易見 , 但我認為後果真的很深刻 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	現今有多少人的頭條在一百年內會很重要 ? 1000年後 ? 克雷克克克克•克特倫的 「 長遠新聞 」 計畫收集了不只重要的故事 , 還會在數個世紀後 , 引起共鳴 。 在ted2010年 , 他發表了最近的頭條新聞 , 內容是關於形塑我們的未來的潛力 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學、
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:而現在 , 真正的消息是
we are drowning in news .	我們淹沒在新聞裡 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是路透社每年就有350萬則新聞報導 。
that's just one source .	那只是一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:這些故事長期來看 , 有多少真的會很重要 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這就是長期新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這是一個由現在已久的基金會成立的專案 , 由tedsters所創立的 , 包括凱文凱利和史都華特布蘭德 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們要找的就是新聞的故事可能在50、100或10 , 000年後才會出現 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	透過過濾器看新聞時 , 大量的下跌 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	去年 , 要從a.p.中挑選出最頂尖的故事 , 這在十年內會不會重要 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年內會不會重要 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 那有點酷 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但過去一年 , 最頂尖的故事是經濟 , 我只是在賭 , 遲早或之後 , 這個特別的衰退將會是老消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	那麼 , 什麼樣的故事可能會為未來帶來改變呢 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 我們以科學為例 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會經過我們的血液流動來修復東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	若你是老鼠 , 某天已經來到這裡了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	最近的一些故事:奈米bees用真正的蜜蜂毒液來拉動腫瘤 ; 它們將基因傳送到大腦 ; 一個可以爬過人體的機器人 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源呢 ? 我們要如何養活九十億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	現今有60億人在餵飽六十億人 , 我們遇到了麻煩 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	如同我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國會因為沒有基因改造作物而餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾蓋茲已經賭上十億的研究 。
what about global politics ?	全球的政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界將會變得非常不一樣 , 如果中國設立了議程 , 可能的話 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們推翻了美國作為世界最大的汽車市場 , 他們推翻了德國成為最大的出口國 , 並且開始在孩子身上做dna測試 , 來選擇他們的職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們正在尋找各種方法 , 來推回我們所知的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	有些近期的發現:阿根廷有一個螞蟻群 , 已經散播到每個大陸但南極洲 ; 有一個自導的機器人科學家 , 很快地 , 科學可能不再需要我們 , 生命也可能不再需要我們 ; 一個微生物在十二萬年後才會醒來 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	看來 , 有沒有我們 , 生命就會繼續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但我在去年的長篇新聞中 , 選了這個主題:月球上的水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓蟻群更容易在上面放置 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不做 , 中國可能會 , 或是這個房間裡的某個人 , 可能會寫很大的支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長遠來看 , 有些新聞比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家卡羅琳.普魯科將影像從卡西尼號航行到土星 , 把焦點放在它最大的衛星上 , 土衛六上 , 在土衛六上 , 似乎會射出冰噴射機 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	美國太空總署、設計、探索、科學、太空、科技、宇宙、視覺化影像等 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	carolynporco飛送我們到土星
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘內 , 我要帶各位踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這趟旅程是你我已經進行了很多年的旅程 , 大約在五十年前 , 人類第一次踏出我們的星球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在這50年裡 , 我們不僅僅是登上月球 , 還把機器人太空船給所有行星 , 我們登陸了小行星 , 和彗星一起聚落 , 此時 , 我們還有一艘太空船 , 前所知的冥王星 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機器人的任務都是人類旅程中更大的一部分:一趟旅程 , 要了解某件事 , 要了解我們的宇宙地點 , 要了解我們的起源 , 以及地球、地球 , 以及我們 , 居住在它上面的我們 , 來到這個地步 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在所有太陽系中 , 我們可能要去到的地方 , 尋找像這樣的問題的答案 , 有土星 。 在1980年代初期 , 我們去過土星 , 但自從卡西尼號太空船 , 我們對土星的調查變得更加深刻 , 在星際空間中旅行七年之久 , 繞著土星軌道轉 , 在2004年的夏天 , 成為人類到目前為止 , 人類所建立的最遙遠的機器人接觸點 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	現在 , 土星系統是豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘、科學的洞見 , 且顯然是超越了對比 , 這個系統的調查有著巨大的宇宙到達 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光是單獨研究光環 , 我們就有很多關於星星和氣體的圓盤 , 我們稱之為螺旋星系 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這裡有一張很漂亮的圖片 , 是andromedanebula , 它是我們最接近、最大的螺旋星系 , 到銀河系去 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	再來 , 這裡有一幅美麗的化合物 , 由哈柏太空望遠鏡所拍攝 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程其實是其中的一部分 , 也是一種比喻 , 比喻為人類更大的旅程 , 來了解我們周遭所有事物的相互關聯性 , 以及人類如何符合那張圖片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我很痛苦 , 我無法告訴各位我們對卡西尼學過的所有知識 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我無法向你們展示我們過去兩年半所拍攝的美麗圖片 , 因為我根本沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以我要集中講述兩個最令人興奮的故事 , 是從這次重大的探索探險旅程中浮現出來的 , 那是我們在土星附近進行的 , 過去兩年半來都是如此 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星與月球的大型多樣化集合在一起 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的範圍從幾公里大小到和美國一樣大 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	我們所拍攝的大部分美麗的圖片都是土星 , 事實上 , 與其它的衛星與土星有著相同的景象 。 這是土星 , 與土星有著dione , 然後 , 這裡是土星 , 呈現出環狀邊緣 , 呈現出它們有多薄 , 和土衛六有多薄 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	現在 , 土星47顆衛星中的兩個是 「 站立 」 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些是土衛六和土衛六 。 土衛六是土星最大的衛星 , 直到卡西尼號到達那裡 , 是太陽系中最大的未被探索的地形 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	長期以來 , 觀測行星的人的身體
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有很大、很厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為更像是地球上所存在的環境 , 或至少在過去 , 比起在太陽系中其他任何一個身體 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣層主要是分子氮 , 就像你在這裡呼吸的 , 只不過它的大氣含有簡單的有機物質 , 如甲烷、丙烷、乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	這些分子會在土衛六的大氣層中被打斷 , 它們的產品會一起結合製造出霧狀粒子 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這個霧狀是無處不在的 。 它完全是全球性的 , 並且包含了土衛六 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這就是為什麼你無法用肉眼看到表面 , 在可見光的區域 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些霧狀粒子 , 在我們和卡西尼號到達那裡之前 , 經過了數十億年 , 溫柔地漂到表面 , 以厚厚厚的有機泥漿覆蓋地表 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	所以 , 就像土衛六一樣 , 土衛六等於焦油 , 或石油 , 或我們不知道的 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們懷疑的 。 而這些分子 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 可以在土衛六表面溫度上是液態的 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是用來泰坦地球上的水是什麼 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣層中是可以凝結的 , 所以 , 意識到這種情況 , 導致了整個奇異的可能性 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 沒錯 , 在那些雲層上方 , 你有數百公里長的霧狀物 , 阻止任何陽光照射到表面 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度是華氏零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但儘管如此寒冷 , 你還是可以讓雨落在土衛六表面 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六上 , 雨在地球上所做的事:它會雕刻出瓜地 ; 它會形成河流和白內障 ; 它能造出峽谷 ; 它能在大型盆地和隕石坑中池子 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把污水從高山和山丘上沖下 , 下到低地 。 所以停下來想想 , 想一想 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六的表面會是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它是黑暗的 。 土衛六上的高中午是地球上那麼深的地球暮光 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	它很冷 , 很糟糕 , 可能會下雨 , 你可能會站在密西根湖的岸邊 , 用油漆來刺青 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是土衛六的景象 , 在我們到達卡西尼號之前的景象 , 我可以告訴你們 , 我們在土衛六上所發現的 , 雖然它的細節不盡相同 , 但它和那個故事一樣引人入勝 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像卡西尼族一樣 , 過去就像是賈爾•凡爾納的冒險成真 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說 , 它有著濃厚的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這是一張土衛六的照片 , 背光是太陽 , 光環是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	另外一個月球我甚至不知道它是哪一個 。 它是一個非常廣大的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼號上有儀器 , 可以透過這個大氣層看到到表面 , 我的攝影機系統是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	而你看到的是明亮且黑暗的區域 , 這大約是它給我們帶來的 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	實在是太神秘了:我們不能在土衛六上看到的東西 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你靠近一點看這個區域 , 你會開始看到一些東西 , 像是無數的通道--我們不知道 。 你看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	這 , 我們後來發現 , 事實上是個隕石坑 , 但土衛六表面上只有極少的隕石坑 , 意味著它是個很年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	還有一些特徵看起來像板塊一樣 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來已經被拆開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你在一個星球上看到任何線性的東西 , 它就意味著有斷裂 , 像是斷層 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它已經在地質上改變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道的六個月後 , 發生了一場事件 , 許多人認為卡西尼號探測土衛六的高峰期 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	那是惠更斯號探測器的部署 , 歐洲核子探測器 , 當時卡西尼號已經載滿了整個太陽系七年 。 我們將它部署到土衛六的大氣層 , 花了兩個半小時到下降 , 降落在地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只想強調這事件有多重大 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它在外太陽系中首次登陸人類的歷史 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	這件事很顯著 , 在我看來 , 這個事件應該是被讚頌的 , 在美國和歐洲各個城市都應該舉行的膠帶遊行 , 令人難過的是 , 並非如此 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這是另一個原因 。 這是個國際使命 , 這個事件在歐洲、德國都被慶祝了 , 而這個慶祝的簡報在英語口音、美國口音、德語、法語、義大利語、和荷蘭口音都被賦予了 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	它是一場動人的展示 , 展示了 「 聯合國 」 這個詞應該是指:一個真正的聯合國加入 , 為好的努力而努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 要探索一個星球是一項巨大的考驗 , 要了解一個行星系統 , 在人類歷史上 , 人類已經無法接觸到它了 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我是說 , 我只是在談它 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是個極度情緒化的事件 , 也是我個人永遠不會忘記的事 , 你也不該這樣做 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	但 , 總之 , 探測器在降落的過程中 , 測量了大氣的量 , 也拍了全景圖片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴你 , 看到土衛六表面的第一張圖片是怎樣的 。 這是我們所看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這真是令人震驚 , 因為那是我們想要那些從軌道上拍攝的其他照片 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	那是一種不明確的模式 , 地質的模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	它是一種driritic的排水模式 , 只能由液體的流動形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以追隨這些通道 , 可以看到它們是如何匯合的 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們匯集到這裡的渠道 , 流入這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是一條海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是流體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這有點像海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是以16公里長的速度拍攝的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這是在八公里長的海岸線拍攝的照片 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--這大約是航空公司的高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要搭飛機橫越美國 , 你會在這些高度飛行 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這張照片是你在土衛六航空公司的窗口飛越土衛六表面時拍的 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器來到表面休息 , 我要給你們看 , 女士們先生們 , 第一次從外太陽系的一個月球表面拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這裡是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是水冰卵石 , 對嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很顯然 , 它落在其中一個平坦、黑暗的區域 , 它沒有從視線下沉 。 所以它不是我們降落的液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	探測器的結果 , 基本上是等同於泥巴的土衛六 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是個無解的地面 , 被液態甲烷給混淆了 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	可能是這樣 , 透過我們看到的這些管道 , 將土衛六的高地沖下去 , 數十億年來 , 不斷地流入低窪的盆地 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	那就是惠更斯號探測器著陸的地方 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但 , 仍然沒有我們的影像 , 甚至惠更斯的影像 , 任何大型、開放的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 情況更加令人費解 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們在土衛六赤道地區的電影 , 展示這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘有一百公尺高 , 被幾公里長的距離隔離 , 它們持續了數英里和數英里 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	有數百人 , 高達一千或一千兩百英里的沙丘 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六的撒哈拉沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	這顯然是一個非常乾燥的地方 , 或者你不會得到沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 又一次 , 它令人疑惑的是 , 沒有液體的存在 , 直到最後 , 我們看到極地區域的湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	土衛六南極有個湖泊場景 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	大約是安大略湖的大小 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	然後 , 僅僅一個星期半前 , 我們飛過土衛六北極 , 發現 , 同樣地 , 我們找到了一個特徵 , 就是卡斯皮亞海的大小 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 看來 , 液體 , 由於某些我們不了解的原因 , 或者至少在這個季節 , 很明顯是在土衛六的極地 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你會同意我們發現土衛六是一個很了不起、很神奇的地方 , 它是外星人 , 但卻像地球一樣奇怪 , 像地球一樣有著像地球般的地質構造 , 一個很棒的地理多樣性 , 一個令人著迷的世界 , 它只能在太陽系中對抗複雜性和豐富性 , 就是地球本身 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們來到土衛二 。 土衛二是個小衛星 , 它大約是土衛六的十分之一大 。 你可以看到它旁邊的英格蘭 , 只是給你看大小 。 這不是威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	而土衛二非常白 , 它的表面很明亮 , 它的表面很明顯是用骨折來破解的 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是一個地質活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在土衛二上的發現之母在南極被發現 , 我們現在看到的是南極點 , 在那裡 , 我們發現了這個斷裂的系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	而它們是不同的顏色 , 因為它們是不同的組成 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們被塗滿了 。 這些裂痕被塗滿了有機物質 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 這整個 , 整個區域 , 南極區域 , 溫度也升高了 。 這是地球上最熱的地方 , 在身體上 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這很奇怪 , 發現地球上的南極比熱帶還要熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	然後 , 當我們拍下額外的照片時 , 我們發現從這些裂紋上噴射出精細的冰粒 , 延伸到數百英哩外的太空 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們把圖像編碼出來 , 把微弱的光線帶出來 , 我們會看到 , 這些噴射流會傳播到土衛二上方幾千英里的太空中 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊已經檢視過像這樣的畫面 , 像這張 , 思考過卡西尼號的其他成果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得出的結論是 , 這些噴射流在土衛二表面下可能從液態水中噴發出來 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以 , 我們可能有液態水、有機物質 , 以及過熱 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們有可能偶然發現了現代行星探索的聖杯 , 或者說 , 一個可能適合生物居住的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我想我不需要告訴各位 , 在太陽系其他地方的生命的發現 , 不論是在土衛二或其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學意涵 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證實在宇宙中曾經發生過的不只一次 , 而是在我們的太陽系中獨立兩次 , 那就表示 , 根據推斷 , 它在宇宙中出現了驚人的次數 , 以及它137億年的歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球是唯一一顆存在著生命的星球 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 它是獨一無二的 , 它仍然是 , 到目前為止 , 我們唯一知道的家園 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果在座有人在1960年代被警示和連貫的話 , 我們會原諒你 , 如果你不是 , 好吧 , 你們會記得1968年由阿波羅八號太空人所拍攝的這張著名照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次 , 地球從太空來的影像 , 它對我們在宇宙中地方的感知產生了巨大的影響 , 以及我們對地球保護的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	嗯 , 我們在卡西尼號拍過一幅從來沒有人看過的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是太陽的全日全食 , 從土星的另一端看到 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這個不可能美麗的畫面中 , 你看到的是太陽的主光環 , 你看到太陽的折射影像 , 你看到這個光環的形成 , 事實上 , 由土衛二的呼吸所產生 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但 , 就好像那還不夠聰明 , 我們可以看見 , 在這個美麗的影像中 , 看見我們自己的星球 , 擠在土星光環的手臂上 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 看到我們自己遠離婚姻 , 並且捕捉到我們在其他世界中的小型藍杉星球的視野 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	而那 , 以及我們從中得到的看法 , 可能是 , 最後 , 我們從這趟半個世紀開始的發現中得到最好的獎賞 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	到2005年 , 世界僅有15%被繪製出來 。 這在災難發生後 , 減緩了援助的速度 , 隱藏了未知的土地和未知的道路的經濟潛力 。 在這短短的演講中 , 谷歌已故的katragada繪圖師繪製出了全球各地的一群人繪製工具 , 用來繪製他們的世界地圖 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技、科技、
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	已故katragada:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , cyclonenargis破壞了緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人處於急需協助的情況 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要趕人和供應到該地區 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖、沒有道路的地圖、沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 無法協助到達cyclone受害者的地圖 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看到洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信到2005年 , 世界上只有15%的地圖是地理可編碼的細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國執行了 「 聯合國 」 這個問題 , 主要的問題是世界上絕大多數人的臉孔:沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但 , 協助來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google , 40個志願者用一個新的軟體來繪製120 , 000公里的道路 , 3000間醫院 , 物流和救災點 。
and it took them four days .	而且花了他們四天的時間
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們用的新軟體 ? googlemapmaker
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	googlemapmaker是一項科技 , 賦予我們每個人在當地所知的地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這套軟體繪製了一切 , 從道路到河流 , 從學校到當地企業 , 以及視訊商店到角落商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎得主hernandodesoo索托承認 , 為大多數發展中國家經濟升遷的關鍵在於採用大量無人駕馭的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 光在印度 , 就有一兆美元的房地產仍然是不可避免的 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光在去年 , 170個國家就有數以千計的使用者繪製了數以百萬計的資訊 , 創造出了一幅從未想過的細節地圖 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這種做法是來自各地充滿熱情的使用者的力量 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	現在我們來看看一些使用者創造的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 就在我們說話的同時 , 在這170個國家中 , 人們正在繪製這個世界 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的橋樑 , 剛剛在塞內加爾標註了一條道路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	而且 , 離家更近 , chalua是班加羅爾的n.g.道路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何學、手勢辨識、以及機器學習的結果 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以千計的使用者的勝利 , 在數百個城市中 , 一個使用者 , 一次一個編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是一個邀請 , 給我們未被開發的星球70%的人 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 巴勒斯坦的村莊布德鲁斯村在一個十個月長的非暴力抗爭中建立了一場圍繞著他們的橄欖爐子 。 你聽到了嗎 ? 不這麼認為 。 巴西的電影家朱莉亞.巴察問為什麼我們只關注在以色列人的暴力衝突中 , 卻沒有帶給非暴力領袖的注意力 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	朱莉亞•巴哈:注意非暴力事件 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列人和巴勒斯坦人試圖用和平手段來終結這場衝突的努力 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國一起旅行時 , 有一個問題總是出現:巴勒斯坦甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我面臨的挑戰是 , 通常我剛從中東回來 , 在那裡我花時間拍攝了數十位巴勒斯坦人使用非暴力手段來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 來自以色列士兵和居民 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人試圖鑄造一個大規模的非暴力運動 , 來終結該地區的佔領 , 並在該地區建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	但 , 大部分的人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這種在地面上發生的事情和國外的感知之間的分裂 , 也是為什麼我們還沒有巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動的關鍵原因之一 , 已經成功了 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以 , 我今天來這裡是要談談注意力的力量 , 你的注意力的力量 , 以及非暴力運動的出現和發展 , 在西岸、加薩和其他地方但今天 , 我的案例研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 大多缺少的非暴力行為 , 並不是為了巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力手段 , 而是為了我們要開始注意那些已經是的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我用布德鲁斯村來說明這一點 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣布它會建立一個分離的障礙 , 而部分的障礙會在村落的上面建造 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地 , 並且被包圍 , 所以他們會失去使用西岸其他地方的自由 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過激勵當地領導力 , 他們發起了一場和平抗爭活動 , 來阻止這種事發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 所以你們可以從地面上看到實際的樣子 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女子:我們被告知牆會將巴勒斯坦和以色列分開 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德鲁斯村這裡 , 我們發現這面牆會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列人:事實上 , 圍籬已經創造出了恐怖的解決方案 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男:今天你被邀請去參加一個和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你是數十位以色列兄弟姐妹加入的 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列積極分子:軍隊除了非暴力的對抗外 , 沒有什麼比非暴力的對抗更嚇人 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女子:我們看到男人試圖推動士兵 , 但沒有一個人能做到 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩們可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫派對成員:我們必須擺脫傳統思維的思想 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯派對成員:我們處在完全和諧的狀態中 , 我們想要把它散播到所有巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	控告:一個聯合國
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔赫、哈馬斯 , 和受歡迎的前線 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	新聞主播:圍籬的搖擺持續著 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊境警察被派來散佈群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。

it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	像是wallujah , 到處開槍
