but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我身邊有一些人 , 甚至不曾共事過 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗議不會阻止[不清楚]
protester: this is a peaceful march .	抗議者:這是和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	陳述:我們辦得到 ! 我們辦得到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱莉亞•巴哈:當我第一次聽到布德鲁斯村的故事時 , 我很驚訝 , 國際媒體並沒有報導這一連串非凡的事件 , 那是發生在七年前 , 2003年的事 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德鲁斯村成功的事實
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民們 , 在十個月的和平抗爭後 , 說服以色列政府 , 將障礙的路線從他們的土地和綠線上移開 , 也就是國際認可以色列與巴勒斯坦領土之間的界線 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德鲁斯村的抗爭從此蔓延到西岸的村落 , 到耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦社區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	然而媒體仍然沉默在這些故事中 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默帶著深刻的後果 , 讓非暴力能夠增長 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦生存 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭有著一個很重要的共通點 ; 它們都是戲院形式在尋求觀眾的理想 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力演員是唯一不斷得到頭版封面的人 , 吸引巴勒斯坦議題的國際關注 , 對於非暴力領導人來說 , 要對他們的社區做出實例 , 認為公民不服從是可行的選項 , 來解決他們的困境 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量 , 可能對房間裡的父母來說 , 一點都不意外 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	讓你的孩子用越來越大的聲音投擲tantrums最好的方法就是讓他第一次拋出適合的聲音 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	tantrum將成為兒童心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 因為孩子已經知道 , 他可以從中得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母能透過給予孩童的注意力 , 或給予孩童注意力 , 來鼓勵或給予獎勵 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成年人來說也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為可以受到影響 , 取決於國際團體選擇把注意力集中在哪裡 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 在結束中東地區的衝突的核心 , 並為我們帶來和平 , 讓我們能把非暴力行為轉變為一種功能性行為 , 做法是讓現今在地面上更加關注非暴力的領導人 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在拍攝我的影片的過程中 , 在西岸的村落 , 在加薩和東耶路撒冷 , 我看過即使是一部紀錄片也能影響到轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫做瓦拉喬的村莊裡 , 位在離耶路撒冷很近的地方 , 社區正面臨著和布德鲁斯村非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被包圍 , 失去很多土地 , 沒有取得自由 , 不論是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們已經使用非暴力行為大約兩年了 , 但自從沒有人注意過之後 , 卻漸漸不知所措 。
so we organized a screening .	於是我們組織了一個篩選程式 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一個禮拜後 , 他們舉辦了最有利且紀律的示範 , 到約會 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	創辦人說 , 村民看到布德鲁斯村的故事在電影中記錄 , 覺得確實有人在追隨他們所做的事 , 人們在乎 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續往前走 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列這邊 , 有一種新的和平運動 , 叫做索里達里特 , 意思是希伯來語中的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領導者一直在使用布德鲁斯村作為他們主要的招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報導 , 以色列人以前從來沒有活動過 , 看到電影 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉杰和索里德拉特運動的例子顯示 , 即使是小型預算的獨立電影也能扮演一個角色 , 將非暴力轉變成一種功能性行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	現在 , 想像一下 , 大型媒體播放者能夠擁有的力量 , 如果他們開始報導每週在村莊裡發生的非暴力示威 , 像是比利、尼德林、華拉 , 在耶路撒冷的鄰里 , 如希克•賈拉 , 和西爾旺 , 非暴力的領導人 , 在他們的工作中會變得更明顯、更有價值、更有效 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信 , 最重要的是要了解 , 如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們是看不見的 , 彷彿它們從未發生過 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但是我先看過如果我們這麼做 , 它們會乘上來 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們相乘 , 他們的影響力會在以色列巴勒斯坦的衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	而他們的影響力終於可以解開局面 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人已經證明了 , 非暴力在布德鲁斯村這種地方行得通 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們給予他們注意 , 讓他們能證明到處都可行 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙.塞克有一個簡單但強而有力的模式 , 可以為激勵人心的領導力 , 一切都從一個黃金圓圈開始 , 以及 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果 , 馬丁.路德.金 , 以及萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseye , 企業家 , 企業家 , 領導力 , 銷售 , 成功的銷售 ,
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙.史蒂克:偉大領導人如何激發行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要如何解釋當事情不如我們假設時 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或更好的是 , 你要如何解釋當其他人能夠實現似乎違反所有假設的事情時 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果電腦如此創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 他們比所有的競爭對手都更有創意 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們和其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的才能、相同的機構、相同的顧問、相同的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	那為什麼他們似乎有所不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁•路德•金主導民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受苦的男人 , 他肯定不是當時唯一偉大的演說家 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能夠想出控制權、有權力的人飛行時 , 肯定有其他隊伍更有資格、更有資金......
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有達成飛機飛行的權力 , 萊特兄弟打敗了他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他東西在玩 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我做了一個發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我對於我認為世界如何運作的看法 , 甚至深深地改變了我在其中運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一種模式 ,
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 世界上所有偉大且有啟發性的領導者和組織 , 不論是蘋果、馬丁•路德•金恩或萊特兄弟 , 他們都認為 , 採取行動 , 並用相同的方式溝通 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	而且完全與其他人相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的只是抄寫它 , 大概是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱之為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 怎麼做 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小小的點子解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導人能夠激勵其他人不在的地方 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義一下這個詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	地球上每一個人 , 每一個組織都知道他們做了什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們是如何做到的 , 不論你稱之為你不同的價值觀 , 或你的專屬過程或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但 , 非常少數的人或組織知道他們為什麼要做他們的工作 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	藉由 「 為什麼 」 我不是 「 賺取利潤 」 的意思 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	那是結果 。 結果總是 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	到 「 為什麼 」 , 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的原因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織會存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	你為什麼早上下床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	還有為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	嗯 , 結果是 , 我們的思考方式、行動方式、溝通的方式 , 都來自外在 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	這是顯而易見的 。 我們從最清楚的事物到最模糊的事物 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但受啟發的領導者和受啟發的組織 , 不論他們的大小 , 不論他們的產業都認為 , 行動和從內而外的溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果電腦是因為它們很容易理解 , 大家都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果電腦和其他人一樣 , 來自它們的行銷訊息可能聽起來會是這樣的: 「 我們製造出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	他們設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 可以使用和使用者友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一台嗎 ? 「 梅 」 。
and that's how most of us communicate .	而這也是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	大部份的行銷就是這樣做 , 大部份的銷售都是這樣做 , 大部份的人都這樣互相溝通 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們做了什麼 , 我們說我們如何不同 , 或我們如何更好 , 期待某種行為、購買、投票等等 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們和最大的客戶有最好的律師 , 我們總是為我們的客戶做生意 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很棒的氣體哩程序 , 它有皮革座椅 , 購買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	蘋果電腦實際上是這樣溝通的 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信用不同的方式思考 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式 , 就是讓我們的產品優美地設計 , 簡單地使用和使用者友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們只是恰巧做出了很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不一樣吧 ? 你已經準備好向我買台電腦了 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的就是把資訊的順序倒過來 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明的是 , 人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們買你的為什麼 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼這個房間裡的每一個人都很自在地從蘋果電腦買一台電腦
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也很舒服的買了蘋果電腦的mp3播放器 , 或是蘋果電腦的手機 , 或是來自蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 如我之前所說 , 蘋果電腦只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有什麼能將他們與任何競爭者區別開來 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭對手都同樣有資格做出所有這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , gateway出了一台平面螢幕電視機
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很明顯有資格製作平面螢幕電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們多年來一直在做平面螢幕監視器 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	迪爾帶著mp3播放器和pda一起出櫃 , 他們製造出很棒的品質產品 , 他們可以製造出完美的設計產品 , 卻沒有人買一個 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像從dell買一台mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會向電腦公司買mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都在做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是和所有需要你擁有的人一起做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要和相信你所相信的人做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最棒的部分是:我告訴你們的都不是我的看法 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	都在生物學的主題中著手 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 生物學
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看一個人腦的橫切面 , 從上往下看 , 你看到的是人腦 , 實際上是分成三個主要元素 , 和黃金圈完美地相關 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的智人大腦 , 我們的新皮質 , 與 「 等級 」 相對應 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	大腦新皮層負責我們所有的理性和分析思考和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個部分組成了我們的邊緣大腦 , 我們的邊緣大腦負責我們所有的感受 , 像是信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人類的行為 , 所有的決策 , 而且它沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外而外的溝通 , 是的 , 人們可以理解大量複雜的資訊 , 像是特徵、好處、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它只是沒有驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內而外的溝通 , 我們就直接與控制行為的大腦部位對話 , 然後我們讓人們將它合理化 , 用我們所說、所做的有形事物 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這是腸道決策的來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候你可以給一個人所有的事實和數字 , 他們會說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節怎麼說 , 但那只是感覺不對勁 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們要用那個動詞 , 它沒有 「 感覺 」 對嗎 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的腦部不控制語言
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	我們能做的最好的就是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者 , 有時你說你帶著心 , 或帶領你的靈魂 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我很討厭把它分解給你 , 那些不是其他身體部位在控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你的邊緣大腦中控制決策而非語言的部分 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼要做你所做的事 , 大家會回應為什麼要做你所做的事 , 那你要如何讓人們為你投票 , 或向你購買一些東西 , 或 , 更重要的是 , 要忠誠 , 想要成為你所做的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是賣給需要你擁有的人 ; 目標是賣給那些相信你所相信的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是僱用需要工作的人 , 而是僱用那些相信你所相信的事的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 你知道 , 如果你雇用人 , 只因為他們能做一份工作 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你雇用那些相信你所相信的人們 , 他們會為你工作 , 帶著血汗和眼淚 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	除了萊特兄弟之外 , 沒有其他地方比這個更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分的人都不知道samuelpierpontlangley
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到二十世紀初期 , 追求權力的人飛行就像是當天的點點陣圖 。
everybody was trying it .	大家都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	而samuelpierpontlangley有我們假設的成功秘訣 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使是現在 , 你問人們: 「 為什麼你的產品 , 或為什麼你的公司會失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給予你相同的三件事:被忽略、不對的人、不好的市場狀況 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	總是一樣的三件事 , 所以 , 咱們來探索一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley得到了五萬美元的戰爭部門來找出這台飛行機器 。
money was no problem .	錢沒有問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛任職 , 在史密森尼工作 , 當時他非常了解當時的所有大頭腦 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用了最好的心靈金錢 , 市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他到處走動 , 每個人都為langley而紮根 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那為什麼我們從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	距離俄亥俄州 , 俄亥俄州 , 奧維爾和威爾伯萊特幾百英里外 , 他們都沒有我們所認為的成功秘訣 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 他們用腳踏車商店的成績來支付他們的夢想 ; 萊特兄弟團隊沒有一個人擁有大學教育 , 甚至不是奧維爾或威爾本 ; 紐約時報跟著他們到處走 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	不同之處在於 , 奧維爾和威爾本 , 由一個目的、一個信念所驅使 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信 , 如果他們能弄清楚這台飛行機器 , 它就會改變世界的軌道 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley是不同的 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要變得富有 , 他想要成名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富人 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	你看 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	那些相信萊特兄弟的夢想的人 , 用血汗和淚水和他們一起工作的人 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人只為了支付而努力 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們會說故事 , 每次萊特兄弟出去時 , 他們就得拿五組零件 , 因為那是他們在購物前撞上多少次 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 在1903年12月17日萊特兄弟起飛 , 甚至沒有人在那裡體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	我們發現在幾天後
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	進一步證明langley是錯誤的動機:萊特兄弟起飛的那天 , 他放棄了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 這真是太棒了 , 各位 , 我將改善你們的科技 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一個 , 他沒有變有錢 , 他沒有變有名 , 所以他退出 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你相信的事物 , 你會吸引那些相信你所相信的事物的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼要吸引那些相信你所相信的人呢 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	某種東西叫做 「 創新的散播法則 」 , 如果你不知道這個法則 , 你絕對知道這個術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	前2.5%的人口是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%的人口是我們早期的採用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你早期的大多數 , 晚期的大多數和產卵 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人買觸控式語音電話的唯一理由 , 是因為你不能再買rotary手機了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在各個地方 , 在這個規模上的不同時間 , 但創新的擴散法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場的成功 , 或是大眾市場接受一個想法 , 你不能擁有它 , 直到你達到了這個臨界點 , 在15%到18%的市場滲透率之間 , 然後系統就會倒退 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我很喜歡問企業: 「 你對新企業的轉換是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	而且他們很喜歡告訴你: 「 喔 , 大概是10%吧 。 」 很驕傲地說: 「 喔 , 大約是10% 。 」
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以讓超過10%的顧客
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有約10%的 「 得到 」 的人 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們如何描述它們 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那就像是那種直覺的感覺 , 「 喔 , 他們就是懂的 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你要怎麼找到在你和他們做生意之前 , 而不是那些不懂的人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	這裡是這個 , 這個小小的差距 , 你必須關閉 , 就像傑佛瑞•摩爾稱之為 「 跨越隔閡 」 , 因為 , 你看 , 早期大多數的人都不會嘗試 , 直到有人先試過它 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	而這些人 , 創新者和早期的採用者 , 他們很自在地做那些腸道決定 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更加自在地做出那些由他們所相信的世界所驅動的直覺決策 , 而不只是產品能取得的產品 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人排隊 , 排隊等了六個小時 , 第一次出櫃時 , 可以買到iphone , 下週你才可以走進商店 , 買下一個貨架 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人在第一次出櫃時花了四萬美金在平面螢幕電視上 , 即便是這項技術也沒什麼用 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順帶一提 , 他們沒有這麼做 , 因為這項技術太棒了 , 他們自己也這麼做了 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	是因為他們想要成為第一 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 , 而你所做的只是證明你所相信的 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會去做那些證明他們所相信的事情 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	買iphone的人之所以在最初的六個小時裡 , 排隊排隊排了六個小時 , 是因為他們對這個世界的看法 , 以及他們希望每個人如何看待他們:他們是第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我給你們一個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗以及一個有名的成功 , 關於創新的散播法則 。
first , the famous failure .	第一 , 著名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	正如我們之前所說 , 一秒鐘前 , 成功的秘訣是金錢 , 適合的人和適當的市場狀況 , 對嗎 ? 你當時應該有成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	提沃大約在八、九年前 , 到目前為止 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手下 , 沒有糾紛 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們非常有資金 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們用tivo作為動詞
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我時時刻刻提到我在垃圾時間華納dvr上的物品 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是商業失敗的
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺過錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們去ipo時 , 他們的股票大約是30到40美金 , 然後下跌 , 從來沒有在10以上交易 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它在六個以上的交易 , 除了幾個小小的高峰 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品他們告訴我們他們擁有的所有東西
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一個產品 , 可以暫停現場的電視節目 , 跳過廣告 , 重播現場電視 , 記住你的觀看習慣 , 不用你問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	而憤世嫉俗的大多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 , 我們不喜歡它
you're scaring us . "	你嚇到我們了 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種喜歡完全控制你人生的每一方面的人 , 男孩 , 我們是否有產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停現場電視節目 , 跳過廣告 , 記住你的觀看習慣 , 等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 , 而你所做的就是證明你所相信的事 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我給你一個成功的例子 , 說明創新的散播法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	在1963年夏天 , 有25萬人出現在華盛頓的商場上 , 去聽金恩博士演講 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們寄出沒有邀請函 , 也沒有網站來查看日期 。
how do you do that ?	要怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士並不是美國唯一一個偉大的演說家 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是在美國唯一一個受過過過過事前權益的男人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法是不好的 。
but he had a gift .	但他有個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們在美國需要什麼改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他四處走動告訴人們他所相信的
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	" 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , " 他告訴人們 ,
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	而相信他所相信的人們 , 拿他的理由 , 讓他們自己做 , 告訴別人 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中的一些人創造出了結構 , 讓更多人知道這個詞 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	你看 , 25萬人在對的時間出現在對的日子裡 , 聽到他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為他顯現 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為自己顯現 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	這是他們對美國的信念 , 讓他們在公車上旅行八小時 , 站在華盛頓的中央 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 這不是關於黑人與白人:有25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信在這個世界上有兩種法律:那些由較高權威人士所制定的法律 , 以及由男人所制定的法律 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	除非所有由人類所制定的法律都和那些由較高權威制定的法律一致 , 否則我們生活在一個公平世界 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	公民權利運動是最好的一件事 , 協助他為生命帶來理想 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們跟進 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順帶一提 , 他給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有計畫 」 的演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	聽聽現在的政治人物 , 用他們全面的十二點計畫 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們不鼓舞任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者 , 也有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者持有權力或權威的立場 , 但那些領導的人激勵我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們都會追隨那些領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們跟隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	也是那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人 , 能夠激發他們周圍的人 , 或找到激勵他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你要怎麼記住你把車子停在哪裡 ? 你怎麼知道你是朝著正確的方向前進 ? 神經學家尼爾•伯吉斯研究繪製我們周圍空間的神經機制 , 以及它們如何連結到記憶和想像 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學、科學、
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	尼爾會燒掉:你的大腦會如何告訴你你的位置 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們停在大型停車場時 , 我們如何記得我們停車的地方 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	荷馬所面臨的問題是
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	而我們會試著去了解他大腦裡發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從海馬體開始 , 以黃色表示 , 這是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你在那兒有損傷 , 比如阿茲海默症 , 你無法記得事情包括你把車子停在哪裡 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它以拉丁文的 「 海馬 」 來命名 , 和它的 「 海馬 」 相似 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	和大腦的其他部份一樣 , 它是由神經元構成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	所以人腦有大約一千億個神經元在其中 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	而神經元會彼此溝通 , 藉由透過互相連結的小脈衝或刺激來傳送電流 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩種細胞所組成的 , 它是非常密集的相互連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家開始了解空間記憶是如何運作的 , 透過記錄老鼠或老鼠的個別神經元 , 在覓食或探索環境中尋找食物 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以 , 我們要想像我們是從這隻老鼠的海馬體內一個神經元錄下來的 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出一個電的尖刺時 , 會有一個紅點和一個點 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以 , 我們看到 , 這個神經元知道 , 每當老鼠進入到環境中的某個特定位置 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	藉由發送訊號到大腦的其他部分 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以 , 我們可以把神經元的發射速率呈現成動物的位置 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元記錄下來 , 我們會發現當動物在環境中不同部位時 , 不同的神經元會發出訊號 , 就像這個正方形的盒子 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 他們組成了大腦的地圖 , 持續告訴大腦 , 「 我現在在我的環境中在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時需要他們腦部監測的電流活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	其中有些病人玩電玩遊戲開車繞著一個小鎮
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	海馬迴上的細胞會被激活、活躍 , 開始發送電脈衝 , 每當它們開車到那個小鎮的特定地點時 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 一個位置細胞如何知道老鼠或老鼠在其環境中的位置 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這裡的兩個細胞告訴我們環境的界限是特別重要的 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	所以 , 上面的那個比較喜歡在老鼠進入的盒子之間的中間地帶 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	而當你把盒子擴大 , 發射地點就會膨脹 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的那一面有一面牆靠近南邊 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一面牆放進盒子裡 , 那麼 , 細胞兩者都會在盒子裡 , 到達南方 , 當動物在盒子裡四處探索 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以這預測了感知你周圍的界限和方向 , 對海馬體來說尤其重要 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在海馬體的輸入值上 , 細胞在海馬體中找到了哪個專案 , 它的確能在特定的距離和邊緣 , 從老鼠或老鼠到處探索時 , 確切地檢測出界線或邊緣 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	所以 , 左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 當動物接近一面牆 , 或向東邊界線時 , 不論是方形的邊緣 , 或方形的牆壁 , 或圓形的牆壁 , 甚至是桌子的邊緣 , 這些動物都在跑來跑去 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞會發出火花 , 當南邊有界線時 , 不論是桌子的邊緣 , 或牆壁 , 甚至是兩張桌子間的鴻溝都會被拉開 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	所以 , 這就是我們認為位置細胞決定動物在探索時的一種方式 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也可以測試我們認為物體在哪裡 , 像是這個目標旗幟 , 在簡單的環境或確實 , 你的車子會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以我們可以讓人們探索一個環境 , 看到他們必須記得的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 一般來說 , 它們很擅長把標記器放在他們認為旗幟或車子的位置 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們用定位細胞做的一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那樣的情況下 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟的位置 , 是改變了你如何改變環境的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 你看到的 , 如果旗幟位在小方形的環境中 , 然後如果你問人們在哪裡 , 但你讓環境變大了 , 他們認為旗幟的位置和位置細胞被激發出來的方式完全相同 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	這就好像你記起旗幟的位置 , 把發射的位置細胞圖案儲存在你所在位置的位置上 , 然後你就可以藉由移動來回到那個位置 , 以符合你目前位置細胞發射的模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那會引導你回到你想要記住的位置 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們透過移動來到哪裡 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以 , 如果我們踏出一條路線 , 或許我們會停下來 , 游走我們會知道 , 因為我們自己的運動 , 可以整合這條路徑 , 大約是前進的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也會得到這種路徑整合 , 由一種叫做網格細胞的細胞所組成 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	現在 , 網格細胞又被發現了 , 在海馬體的輸入上 , 它們有點像位置細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處探索時 , 每個個別的細胞會在一系列不同的位置上發射 , 這些位置會在一個很普通的三角形網格子內 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你用不同的顏色來紀錄這些網格細胞 , 每個細胞都有類似的網格激發模式 , 橫跨整個環境 , 每個細胞的網格激發模式 , 都和其他細胞相對的位置稍微相對 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	紅色的會在這個格子上起火 , 綠色的會在這個格子上 , 藍色的在這個格子上 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 合起來 , 就好像老鼠可以放置一個虛擬的網格 , 在其環境中散發出的位置 , 有點像你在地圖上找到的緯度和長度線條 , 但使用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它四處移動時 , 電流活動可以從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 來持續追蹤它的位置 , 讓它可以用自己的動作 , 知道它在環境中的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	嗯 , 因為所有的網格激發模式都有相同的對稱性 , 相同的格子方向 , 在橘色這裡顯示 , 這意味著 , 網格中所有網格細胞在特定部位的活動應該會根據我們這六個方向運行 , 或在兩者之間的六個方向而有所改變 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以把人放進核磁共振儀 , 讓他們做一個小小的電玩遊戲 , 就像我給你們看的那個 , 找出這個信號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你的確在人類的大腦中也看到了它 , 這跟你在老鼠身上看到網格細胞的部分一樣 。
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得他的車子在哪個位置 , 用他停車的地方的距離和方向來延伸建築和界線 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	那會是由有限偵測細胞的激發而來的 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他也記得他從汽車公園中取出的路徑 , 這條路會以網格細胞的激發方式呈現 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	現在這兩種細胞都可以讓位置細胞發射
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以回到他停車位的位置 , 藉由移動 , 來找出目前他大腦中位置細胞的發射模式 , 與他停車的位置相符 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這引導他回到視覺暗示的位置 , 像是他的車子是否真的存在 。
maybe it's been towed .	或許已經被灌輸了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去找它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找這種網格激發的模式 , 我們在一系列地點中看到它 , 當我們在做各種自傳記憶任務時 , 就像你上次去婚禮時的記憶一樣 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 可能是代表我們周圍空間的神經機制也被用來產生視覺影像 , 這樣我們才能重現空間場景 , 至少 , 在我們想要想像的時候發生在我們身上的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果發生這種事 , 你的記憶可以從密集的互聯網開始 , 然後重新啟動邊界細胞 , 創造出你觀點周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	而網格細胞可以在這個空間中移動這個視野 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種細胞 , 頭部方向細胞 , 是我還沒提到的 , 它們就像指南針一樣 , 根據你所面臨的狀況 , 會像指南針一樣開火 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義出你想要為你的視覺影像產生的看法 , 所以你可以想像當你在婚禮時發生了什麼事 , 比如說 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	所以 , 這只是個新時代的例子 , 在認知神經科學中 , 我們開始了解心理過程 , 比如你如何記得、想像 , 甚至是以數十億個神經元的行為來思考 。
thank you very much .	非常感謝大家 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 由機構、政府、私營部門和大眾共同驅動的全球安全 。 這不僅僅是開放式風扇的遙遠希望 , 是對詹姆斯•斯塔夫里迪斯的遠景 , 北約的最高指揮官 , 他們分享鮮明的時刻 , 來自近期的軍事史 , 來解釋為什麼未來應該要用橋來建造 , 而不是牆壁 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開放資源、和平、政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯.史特拉迪斯:北約的最高指揮官是如何看待全球安全的 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我要談一下開放原始碼的安全性 , 因為我們必須在21世紀的安全性上更好 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我先說 , 讓我們回顧二十世紀 , 來了解安全的風格對我們是如何運作的 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 一個在法國的戰場 , 就在比利時北方的北方 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	在verdun , 1916年 , 在超過300天的時期 , 有70萬人因此喪命 , 所以大約一天有2 , 000人死亡 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你將它推向二十世紀的安全 , 進入第二次世界大戰 , 你看到史達林升級的戰役 , 300天 , 2百萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 繼續嘗試建造牆壁 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰的戰場 , 到第二次世界大戰的馬吉諾防線 , 接著進入冷戰、鐵幕、柏林圍牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天的演講主題是 , 與其建造牆壁來創造安全 , 我們需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲著名的橋樑 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	它是這座流過飲料河的橋樑 , 是伊佛•安德里奇一部小說的主題 , 它談到如何在歐洲和巴爾幹地區非常困擾的部分 , 隨著時間過去 , 已經有了巨大的圍牆 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	更近期 , 在過去十年 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 猶豫著要團結起來 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我會說 , 同樣地 , 開放式安全就是把國際、跨部門、私人網路連結起來 , 然後用策略性溝通 , 大多是在社交網路上 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	所以 , 讓我來談談為什麼我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們的全球公有物以各種方式攻擊 , 沒有一個威脅到全球公有物的來源 , 會透過築牆來解決 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	現在 , 我是個水手 , 很明顯地 ,
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 排隊員 , 翻遍印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	它沿著協奏曲線沿著它的側邊 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	也就是防止海盜攻擊它 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	海盜是現今世界各地都很積極的威脅 。 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	盜版在馬拉卡河峽也很活躍 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	活躍於幾內亞灣
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到的
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	在全球運輸系統中 , 連續花了一百億美元 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 在這個時候 , 有20艘船 , 500個船員舉行了人質 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是對全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要考慮如何處理它 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉移到另一種海、網路海、
here are photographs of two young men .	這裡有兩位年輕男子的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	在當下 , 他們被監禁了 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們做了一個信用卡詐欺 , 淨資超過一百億美元 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 它是全球經濟失能的2兆年 。
two trillion a year .	一年兩兆
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	那只是在英國的國內生產總值之下 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	所以 , 這個我們無止境地知道的網路大海 , 是激進式開放的基本元素 , 同時也受到威脅 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	在全球公有物中 , 我擔心的另一件事是人口販賣所造成的威脅 , 由於麻醉劑、鴉片等運動 , 從阿富汗出來 , 透過歐洲到美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心從andeanridge北部來的可卡因 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心非法武器和人口販賣的運動 。 最重要的 , 也許是 , 我們擔心人口販賣 , 和它的可怕成本 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	人口販賣主要是在海上 , 但在全球公有物的其他地方 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴你們 , 這是美國海軍陸戰隊的高科技片段 , 我們用它來阻止人口販賣 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是毒品販的半潛水服 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	是在南美洲叢林中建造的 。
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們用那個低科技的木筏抓到它 , 它帶著六噸的可卡因 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四個船員 。 精密的交流會席捲 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種販賣方式 , 在毒品、在人類、在武器上 , 上帝禁止 , 在大規模毀滅性武器中 , 是全球公有物威脅的一部分 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	讓我們今天在阿富汗一起拉近 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是阿富汗的一片洋芋片田
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	世界上百分之八十到九十的嬉皮 , 鴉片和海洛因 , 來自阿富汗 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	我們也在那裡看到 , 當然 , 恐怖主義
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這是基地組織的階段 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到有一股強烈的暴動 , 嵌在那邊 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以 , 這種恐怖主義的擔憂 , 也是全球公有物的一部分 , 我們必須要處理的 。
so here we are , 21st century .	所以 , 現在 , 21世紀 ,
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道我們二十世紀的工具是行不通的 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼做 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我認為 , 我們不會把安全單單靠在槍口的桶子上 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不會只靠槍支的桶子來傳送安全感 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要軍事力量的應用 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們在做的時候 , 我們必須要做得很好 , 且有能力 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的論點是 , 開放式安全是關於國際、跨部門、私人的連結 , 透過網路上的策略性溝通 , 拉扯在一起 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子 , 說明這如何以正面的方式運作 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 。 這些是阿富汗士兵 。
they are all holding books .	他們都拿著書 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說: 「 這很奇怪 。 我想我讀到這個人口統計數據 , 二十幾歲和三十多歲的年輕男男女 , 在阿富汗大多是不識字的 。 」
you would be correct .	你是正確的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	85%進入阿富汗的安全部隊是無法解讀的 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼 ? 因為塔利班在這個時期 , 在這些男人和女人都會學會讀書 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	所以問題是 , 那為什麼他們都站在那裡拿著書呢 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們正在教導他們閱讀 , 在北約和私營機構合作 , 和發展機構合作 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們已經教會了超過二十萬名阿富汗安全部隊以基本水平來閱讀和寫作 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你可以讀和寫在阿富汗時 , 你通常會在口袋裡放一支筆 。
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	在典禮上 , 當這些年輕男女畢業後 , 他們帶著一支很棒的驕傲的筆 , 放進口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	這使得國際間有五十個國家參與了這項使命 , 跨部門這些發展機構和私人公共共事業 , 來接納這類的安全 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	當然 , 我們也在教導他們戰鬥技能 , 但我會說 , 開放式安全意味著 , 以創造更長久的安全性效應的方式來連結 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是美國海軍戰艦 。
it's called the comfort .	所謂的舒適感
there's a sister ship called the mercy .	有一艘姊姊的船叫作慈悲
they are hospital ships .	他們是醫院的船隻 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	這一個 , 舒適 , 在加勒比海和南美海岸進行病人治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	一般來說 , 他們會做40萬個病人的治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	它不是嚴格的軍隊 , 而是人道組織的結合: 「 希望 」 、 「 微笑 」 。
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織發送志願者
interagency physicians come out .	跨部門的醫師出來了 。
they're all part of this .	它們都是這其中的一部分 。
to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	給你們一個例子 , 這個小男孩 , 八歲 , 和他的母親走了兩天 , 來到安慰號的眼科診所 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	當他被配合時 , 在他極端的神奇眼睛上 , 他突然抬起頭 , 說: 「 媽媽 , veoelmundo 。 」
" mom , i see the world . "	「 媽 , 我看到世界了 。 」
multiply this by 400 , 000 patient treatments , this privatepublic collaboration with security forces , and you begin to see the power of creating security in a very different way .	把這個乘以400 , 000個病人的治療 , 這個私人的合作與安全部隊合作 , 你開始看到用截然不同的方式來創造安全的力量 。
here you see baseball players .	這裡你看到棒球選手
can you pick out the two us army soldiers in this photograph ?	你能選出這張照片中的兩個美國軍人軍人嗎 ?
they are the two young men on either side of these young boys . this is part of a series of baseball clinics , where we have explored collaboration between major league baseball , the department of state , who sets up the diplomatic piece of this , military baseball players , who are real soldiers with real skills but participate in this mission , and they put on clinics throughout latin america and the caribbean , in honduras , in nicaragua , in all of the central american and caribbean nations where baseball is so popular , and it creates security .	他們是這兩位年輕男孩兩邊的年輕男孩 。 這是一系列棒球診所的一部分 。 在那裡 , 我們探索了大聯盟棒球聯盟 , 國家部門 , 設立了外交部的部門 , 軍事棒球選手 , 他們是真正的士兵 , 擁有真正的技能 , 卻參與了這個使命 , 他們在拉丁美洲和加勒比的診所 , 在宏都拉比 , 在宏都拉斯 , 在美國的中美洲 , 和加勒比的加拿大 , 加勒比人和加勒比人 , 在加拿大的中美洲 , 加拿大都在中美洲 , 加拿大 , 在中美洲的一些地方 , 巴西 , 巴西人和加拿大都在中美洲的中美洲 , 加拿大公民族人和加拿大 。
it shows role models to young men and women about fitness and about life that i would argue help create security for us .	它呈現給年輕男女的榜樣 , 關於健身 , 以及關於人生的榜樣 , 我會爭論協助為我們創造安全 。
another aspect of this partnership is in disaster relief .	這夥伴關係的另一個面向就是災難解放 。
this is a us air force helicopter participating after the tsunami in 2004 which killed 250 , 000 people .	這是美國空軍直升機參與了2004年海嘯在2004年造成25萬人死亡
in each of these major disasters — the tsunami in 2004 , 250 , 000 dead , the kashmiri earthquake in pakistan , 2005 , 85 , 000 dead , the haitian earthquake , about 300 , 000 dead , more recently the awful earthquaketsunami combination which struck japan and its nuclear industry — in all of these instances , we see partnerships between international actors , interagency , privatepublic working with security forces to respond to this kind of natural disaster .	在每一個重大災難中2004年的海嘯 , 25萬人死亡 , 2005年巴基斯坦的卡許米里大地震 , 8萬5千人死亡 , 海地地震 , 300000人死亡 , 近期 , 嚴重的地震融合了日本 , 以及其核工業 , 在所有這些例子中 , 我們看到國際間的合作 , 跨部門 , 私人合作 , 與國際部門合作 , 和安全部隊合作 , 一起合作 , 來回應這種自然災害 。
so these are examples of this idea of opensource security .	這些都是開放式安全的例子 。
we tie it together , increasingly , by doing things like this .	我們將它綁在一起 , 漸漸地 , 透過這樣的方式 。
now , you're looking at this thinking , " ah , admiral , these must be sea lanes of communication , or these might be fiber optic cables . "	現在 , 你看到的這個想法是: 「 啊 , 阿 , 阿米德 , 這些一定是溝通的海道 , 或是這些可能是光纖電纜 。 」
no . this is a graphic of the world according to twitter .	不是的 。 這是根據twitter推測的世界的圖表 。
purple are tweets . green are geolocation .	紫色是推特 , 綠色是地理分配 。
white is the synthesis .	白色是綜合體 。
it's a perfect evocation of that great population survey , the six largest nations in the world in descending order: china , india , facebook , the united states , twitter and indonesia .	這是一場大規模調查的完美演變 , 全球六大國以下指令命令:中國、印度、臉書、美國、推特和印尼 。
why do we want to get in these nets ?	為什麼我們想要在這些蚊帳裡
why do we want to be involved ?	為什麼我們想要參與其中 ?
we talked earlier about the arab spring , and the power of all this .	我們先前談到阿拉伯之春 , 還有這一切的力量 。
i'll give you another example , and it's how you move this message .	我再舉另一個例子 , 就是你如何移動這個訊息 。
i gave a talk like this in london a while back about this point . i said , as i say to all of you , i'm on facebook . friend me .	我在倫敦演講過一陣子 , 講到這個話題 。 我說 , 如同我對你們說的 , 我在臉書上 , 朋友們 。
got a little laugh from the audience .	聽眾笑了一下 。
there was an article which was run by ap , on the wire .	當時有一篇文章是由ap , 在電線上執行 。
got picked up in two places in the world: finland and indonesia .	在世界上兩個地方被發現:芬蘭和印尼 。
the headline was: nato admiral needs friends .	標題是:北約大會需要朋友 。
and the story was a catalyst , and the next morning i had hundreds of facebook friend requests from indonesians and finns , mostly saying , " admiral , we heard you need a friend , and oh , by the way , what is nato ? "	故事的內容是催化劑 , 隔天早上 , 我有數百個臉書朋友請求 , 來自印尼人和芬蘭 , 主要是說: 「 亞當 , 我們聽說你需要一個朋友 , 喔 , 順便說一下 , 北約有什麼 ? 」
yeah , we laugh , but this is how we move the message , and moving that message is how we connect international , interagency , privatepublic , and these social nets to help create security .	沒錯 , 我們會笑 , 但這是我們如何移動訊息 , 移動那個訊息就是我們如何連結國際、間接、私人、私人網路 , 以及這些社交網路 , 來協助創造安全 。
now , let me hit a somber note .	現在 , 讓我來點註解 。
this is a photograph of a brave british soldier .	這是一張勇敢的英國士兵的照片 。
he's in the scots guards .	他在蘇格蘭警衛隊裡
he's standing the watch in helmand , in southern afghanistan .	他站在helmand的手錶 , 在阿富汗南部 。
i put him here to remind us , i would not want anyone to leave the room thinking that we do not need capable , competent militaries who can create real military effect .	我讓他在這裡提醒我們 , 我不希望有人離開房間 , 認為我們不需要有能力、有能力的軍隊來創造真正的軍事效應 。
that is the core of who we are and what we do , and we do it to protect freedom , freedom of speech , all the things we treasure in our societies .	那就是我們是誰、我們所做的事的核心 , 我們做它來保護自由、言論自由 , 所有我們社會珍惜的東西 。
but , you know , life is not an onandoff switch .	但 , 你知道的 , 人生並不是一個隨機開關 。
you don't have to have a military that is either in hard combat or is in the barracks .	你不需要有一支軍隊 , 要不然就是在艱難的戰鬥中 , 要不就是在巴拉克 。
i would argue life is a rheostat .	我會說 , 生命是rheostat 。
you have to dial it in , and as i think about how we create security in this 21st century , there will be times when we will apply hard power in true war and crisis , but there will be many instances , as we've talked about today , where our militaries can be part of creating 21stcentury security , international , interagency , privatepublic , connected with competent communication .	你必須把它撥進去 , 正如我所想的 , 我們該如何在21世紀創造安全 , 將會有時候當我們在真正的戰爭和危機中 , 將來會有困難的力量 , 但 , 正如我們今天所說 , 我們的軍隊可以成為創造21世紀安全、國際、國際、跨部門、私人、公開的一份子 , 和有能力的溝通 。
i would close by saying that we heard earlier today about wikipedia . i use wikipedia all the time to look up facts , and as all of you appreciate , wikipedia is not created by 12 brilliant people locked in a room writing articles .	最後我想說我們今天聽過維基百科 。 我常常用維基百科去查事實 , 如同你們所欣賞的 , 維基百科並不是由12位傑出人士在一間房間裡寫文章中創造出來的 。
wikipedia , every day , is tens of thousands of people inputting information , and every day millions of people withdrawing that information .	維基百科 , 每天都有成千上萬的人在輸入資訊 , 每天都有數百萬人在戒斷那些資訊 。
it's a perfect image for the fundamental point that no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	對於最基本的觀點 , 這是個完美的圖像 , 沒有人像我們所有人一樣聰明 , 一起思考 。
no one person , no one alliance , no one nation , no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	沒有一個人 , 沒有一個同盟國 , 沒有一個國家 , 沒有人像我們所有人一樣聰明 。
the vision statement of wikipedia is very simple: a world in which every human being can freely share in the sum of all knowledge .	維基百科的願景聲明很簡單:在這個世界中 , 每個人都可以自由地分享在所有知識的總合中 。
my thesis for you is that by combining international , interagency , privatepublic , strategic communication , together , in this 21st century , we can create the sum of all security .	我的論點是 , 透過結合國際、跨部門、私人公開、策略性溝通 , 一起 , 在這個21世紀 , 我們就能創造出所有安全的總和 。
thank you very much . thank you . thank you .	非常謝謝 。 謝謝 。 謝謝 。
